Qada' in Witr for Omitted Recitation: Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on qada' of Witr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the number of rak'ahs to make up (qada') in Witr when recitation is omitted, and state the relied-upon position (mufta bihi).

Core Idea
The number of rak'ahs to repeat depends on whether the tahrimah is invalidated by omitting recitation.

This passage tackles a practical problem: how many rak'ahs must one make up if recitation is omitted in certain rak'ahs of Witr? The Hanafi imams disagree based on their analysis of the effect on the tahrimah (the initial consecration). Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to trace legal reasoning (ta'lil) and identify the operative ruling (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the three opinions
State the core question: when recitation is omitted in one or both pairs (shaf') of Witr, how many rak'ahs are wajib as qada'? List the three positions: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say four rak'ahs in certain cases, Muhammad says two rak'ahs in all cases.
The Imamayn differ in the number of scenarios, but both require four rak'ahs in at least two cases.
2
Understand the 'illa (cause): effect on tahrimah
Analyze each imam's view on whether omitting recitation invalidates the tahrimah. Abu Hanifa: omission in one rak'ah of the first pair does not break the tahrimah. Abu Yusuf: omission never breaks the tahrimah. Muhammad: any omission in the first pair breaks the tahrimah completely.
The tahrimah is the basis for connecting the two pairs; if it remains, the second pair can be 'built' on the first.
3
Trace the tarjih (preference) and the relied-upon narration
Note that Muhammad's narration from Abu Hanifa states that Abu Hanifa ruled qada' of two rak'ahs, but Abu Yusuf denied this. The later mashayikh (scholars) relied on Muhammad's narration and ignored Abu Yusuf's denial. Thus the mufta bihi is two rak'ahs.
Fakhr al-Islam in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir is cited as the authority for this tarjih.
4
Note the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
The practical consequence: a person omitting recitation in the first shaf' must repeat only the first two rak'ahs according to the mufta bihi, whereas according to the other imams they would also need to repeat the second pair (if affected).
This affects the length of the repeated prayer.

Source Text

وإما أن يكون الترك في ركعة من الشفع الأول مع كل الثاني، أو مع ركعة منه، وهما ما قال في «المتن»: وأربع لو ترك في إحدى كل شفع، أو في الثاني وإحدى الأول، وإنما يقضي الأربع عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف؛ لبقاء التحريمة عندهما. أما عند أبي حنيفة، فلأنه ترك القراءة في ركعة من الشفع الأول، والتحريمة لا تبطل به. وأما عند أبي يوسف، فلأن التحريمة لا تبطل بالترك أصلاً، وقد أفسد الشفعين بترك القراءة فيقضي أربعاً. وعند محمد في جميع الصور ليس إلا قضاء الركعتين. قوله: وإما أن يكون...الخ عطف على قوله: «إما أن يكون الترك... الخ، وبيان لصورتين من صور عدم الاقتصار. قوله: في إحدى كل شفع؛ بأن تركها في الأولى مع الثالثة أو الرابعة، أو في الثانية مع الثالثة أو الرابعة. قوله: عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف؛ كون القضاء أربعاً على أصلهما ظاهر لا سترة فيه، وكذا رواه محمد في «الجامع الصغير» عن أبي يوسف عن أبي حنيفة، لكن أنكر أبو يوسف هذه الرواية عنه فيما إذا ترك القراءة في إحدى الأول وإحدى الثاني، وقال: رويت لك عن أبي حنيفة أنه يلزم قضاء ركعتين، ومحمد لم يرجع عن روايته عنه، واعتمد مشايخنا روايته، ولم يلتفتوا إلى إنكار أبي يوسف. كذا في شرح الجامع الصغير لفخر الإسلام. قوله: في جميع الصور؛ المراد به جميع صور المسألة، أو جميع صور قضاء الأربع. فظهر ما قال في «المختصر»: فيقضي أربعاً عند أبي حنيفة فيما ترك في إحدى الأول مع الثاني، أو بعضه: أي ركعة من الشفع الأول مع كل الشفع الثاني، أو في ركعة منه وعند أبي يوسف في أربع مسائل. قوله: إلا قضاء الركعتين؛ لأن ترك القراءة في الشفع الأول مطلقاً ولو في ركعة منه يبطل التحريمة عنده، فلا يصح بناء الشفع الثاني، فلا يجب قضاؤه. قوله: فظهر؛ أي بما فصلت ظهر معنى ما قلت في «مختصر الوقاية»، وعبارته بتمامه هكذا: «وترك القراءة في الشفع الأول يبطل التحريمة عند أبي حنيفة، وعند محمد في ركعة، وعند أبي يوسف لا بل يفسد الأداء فيقضي أربعاً...الخ؛ أي فيقضي أربعا عند أبي حنيفة في مسألتين: إحداهما: أن يتركهما في ركعة واحدة من الشفع الأول وفي ركعتي الثاني. وآخرهما: أن يترك في ركعة واحدة من الشفع الأول، وفي ركعة واحدة من الثاني. وعند أبي يوسف يقضي أربعاً في أربع مسائل: التي يوجد الترك فيها في الشفعين، فاثنان منها هما المذكوران في مذهب أبي حنيفة...
And sometimes the omission is in one rak'ah of the first pair along with all of the second, or with one rak'ah of it, and these are what the text said: 'And four if he omitted in one of each pair, or in the second and one of the first, and he only makes up four according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf because the tahrimah remains with them.' As for according to Abu Hanifa, because he omitted recitation in one rak'ah of the first pair, and the tahrimah is not invalidated by it. And as for according to Abu Yusuf, because the tahrimah is not invalidated by omission at all, and he has corrupted the two pairs by omitting recitation, so he makes up four. And according to Muhammad in all cases, there is only the making up of two rak'ahs. His statement: 'And sometimes it is...etc.' is conjuncted to his statement: 'sometimes the omission...etc.', and it is an explanation of two cases where it is not limited. His statement: 'in one of each pair'; that is, he omitted it in the first with the third or fourth, or in the second with the third or fourth. His statement: 'according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf'; that the four-rak'ah qada' is apparent according to their principles, and likewise Muhammad narrated from Abu Yusuf from Abu Hanifa in al-Jami' al-Saghir, but Abu Yusuf denied this narration from him in the case where he omitted recitation in one of the first and one of the second, and said: I narrated to you from Abu Hanifa that making up two rak'ahs is binding. And Muhammad did not retract from his narration, and our scholars relied on his narration and paid no attention to Abu Yusuf's denial. So in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir of Fakhr al-Islam. His statement: 'in all cases'; means all cases of the issue, or all cases of qada' of four. So what he said in al-Mukhtasar became clear: 'He makes up four according to Abu Hanifa in what he omitted in one of the first with the second, or part of it: i.e. one rak'ah from the first pair with all of the second pair, or in one rak'ah of it. And according to Abu Yusuf in four cases.' His statement: 'except making up two rak'ahs'; because omission of recitation in the first pair absolutely, even in one rak'ah of it, invalidates the tahrimah according to him, so the building of the second pair is not valid, so its qada' is not obligatory. His statement: 'so it became clear'; i.e., with what I detailed, the meaning of what I said in Mukhtasar al-Wiqayah became clear, and its full expression is: 'And omitting recitation in the first pair invalidates the tahrimah according to Abu Hanifa, and according to Muhammad in one rak'ah, and according to Abu Yusuf it does not but rather corrupts the performance so he makes up four...etc.', i.e., he makes up four according to Abu Hanifa in two cases: one: that he omits it in one rak'ah of the first pair and in both rak'ahs of the second; and the other: that he omits in one rak'ah of the first pair and in one rak'ah of the second. And according to Abu Yusuf, he makes up four in four cases: those in which omission occurs in the two pairs, two of which are those mentioned in the madhhab of Abu Hanifa...

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the number of rak'ahs to be performed as qada' (make-up) in Witr prayer when the worshipper omits the qira'ah (recitation) in certain rak'ahs. The Witr prayer consists of a shaf' (two rak'ahs) followed by a single witr rak'ah, but here the discussion involves two shaf' (four rak'ahs) and the witr single? The text is from a commentary on al-Wiqayah and deals with the ruling when omission occurs across the first and second shaf' pairs. The difference stems from the effect of omitting recitation on the validity of the tahrimah (the initial consecration). Abu Hanifa holds that omitting recitation in one rak'ah of the first shaf' does not invalidate the tahrimah, so the second shaf' remains valid and must also be made up, totaling four rak'ahs. Abu Yusuf goes further: the tahrimah is never invalidated by omission at all, but the prayer is corrupted; he also requires four rak'ahs. Muhammad al-Shaybani, however, holds that omitting recitation in any rak'ah of the first shaf' invalidates the tahrimah, so only the two rak'ahs of the first shaf' need to be made up. The author clarifies that the four-rak'ah qada' applies in specific cases, and that although Abu Yusuf denied the narration attributing to Abu Hanifa the two-rak'ah ruling, the relied-upon position (mu'tamad) is the narration from Muhammad, which is followed by the later scholars. The dispute is practical: a person who omits recitation must know how many rak'ahs to repeat. The table (not fully reproduced) illustrates the permutations of omission. This passage demonstrates the Hanafi method of identifying the 'illa (cause) and applying it across cases.

Key Terms
التحريمة (al-tahrimah): The initial takbir (Allahu Akbar) that consecrates the prayer, also used metonymically for the validity of the prayer state.
الشفع (al-shaf'): A pair of rak'ahs, especially the first two rak'ahs of Witr (also used for any pair in nafl).
قضاء (qada'): The act of performing a prayer or its part after its time due to a deficiency or invalidity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school, how many rak'ahs must be made up if one omits recitation in one rak'ah of the first shaf' of Witr?
A) Four rak'ahs
B) Two rak'ahs
C) Three rak'ahs
D) One rak'ah

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school for qada' in Witr when recitation is omitted in the first shaf' is to repeat only the two rak'ahs of that shaf'.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Qada of Witr When Recitation is Omitted
Explaining the dispute on qada for omitting recitation in witr's first shaf'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on the number of rak'ahs to make up when recitation is omitted in the first shaf' of witr, and identify the scenarios that trigger each position.

Core Idea
Omitting recitation in the first shaf' of witr invalidates the tahrimah—but how many rak'ahs to make up is disputed among the three imams.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya explores an intra-Hanafi dispute on the qada of witr when recitation is omitted in the first shaf'. The three main Hanafi authorities—Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Imam Muhammad—disagree on which scenarios require making up two or four rak'ahs. The disagreement hinges on whether the omission invalidates the entire tahrimah or only part of it, affecting the validity of the subsequent rak'ahs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the omission
The act is witr prayer; the omission is recitation in the first shaf'. Determine the effect: does it invalidate the entire prayer (tahrimah) or just that rak'ah?
The first shaf' is the first pair of rak'ahs in witr.
2
State Abu Hanifa's view
Abu Hanifa holds that omission in any rak'ah of the first shaf' invalidates the entire tahrimah, so the whole prayer is invalid. He specifies two scenarios where four rak'ahs are due: (1) omission in one rak'ah of the first shaf' and both of the second, (2) omission in one rak'ah of each shaf'.
His view is the mufta bihi according to the Hidayah.
3
State Abu Yusuf's view
Abu Yusuf extends the invalidation to four scenarios where omission occurs in both shaf's: the two from Abu Hanifa plus omitting in all four rak'ahs and omitting in both of the first and one of the second.
He also requires four rak'ahs in these cases.
4
State Muhammad's view
Imam Muhammad takes a narrower approach: omission only in a single rak'ah does not invalidate the whole prayer; only that rak'ah is corrupt. Therefore, in all cases, only two rak'ahs (the first shaf') need to be made up.
His view is recorded in al-Mukhtasar.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence is the number of rak'ahs for qada: 4 rak'ahs according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (with different scenario counts), vs 2 rak'ahs according to Muhammad.
The tarjih goes to Abu Hanifa's position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فظهر ما قال في «المختصر» : فيقضي أربعاً عند أبي حنيفة فيما ترك في إحدى الأوَّل مع الثَّاني، أو بعضه : أي ركعة من الشفع الأَوَّل مع كل الشفع الثاني، أو في ركعة منه وعند أبي يوسف في أربع مسائل. [١] قوله : إلا قضاء الركعتين؛ لأنَّ ترك القراءة في الشفع الأوّل مطلقاً ولو في ركعة منه يبطل التحريمة عنده، فلا يصح بناء الشفع الثاني، فلا يجب قضاؤه. [٢] قوله : فظهر؛ أي بما فصلت ظهر معنى ما قلت في «مختصر الوقاية»، وعبارته بتمامه هكذا: «وترك القراءة في الشفع الأوّل يبطل التحريمة عند أبي حنيفة، وعند محمد في ركعة، وعند أبي يوسف لا بل يفسد الأداء فيقضي أربعاً...الخ»؛ أي فيقضي أربعا عند أبي حنيفة في مسألتين: إحداهما: أن يتركهما في ركعة واحدة من الشفع الأول وفي ركعتي الثاني. وآخرهما: أن يترك في ركعة واحدة من الشفع الأوّل، وفي ركعة واحدة من الثاني. وعند أبي يوسف يقضي أربعاً في أربع مسائل: التي يوجد الترك فيها في الشفعين، فاثنان منها هما المذكوران في مذهب أبي حنيفة. والثالثة: أن يترك قراءة كلّ ركعات الشفعين. والرابعة أن يترك في ركعتي الشفع الأوّل، وفي ركعة واحدة من الثاني. [١]قوله : وفي الباقي ركعتين، هذا متعلق بقول الشيخين؛ أي في الباقي من المسائل الثمانية يقضي عندهما ركعتين، وهو ست مسائل عند أبي حنيفة، وأربع مسائل على رأي أبي يوسف. [٢] قوله : وهو ست... الخ؛ من هاهنا إلى قوله: وأربع عند أبي يوسف تفسير من الشارح، وخارج عن «المختصر». [٣]قوله : وعند محمد، هذا في «المختصر» متصل بقوله: وفي الباقي ركعتين.
Then what he said in al-Mukhtasar became evident: He makes up four rak'ahs according to Abu Hanifa if he omitted in one of the first with the second, or part thereof: meaning one rak'ah of the first shaf' with the entire second shaf', or in one rak'ah of it. And according to Abu Yusuf, in four cases. [1] His saying: Only the qada of the two rak'ahs; because omitting recitation in the first shaf' absolutely, even in one rak'ah of it, invalidates the tahrimah according to him, so the building of the second shaf' is not valid, so its qada is not obligatory. [2] His saying: Then it became evident; i.e., by the details I gave, the meaning of what I said in Mukhtasar al-Wiqayah became evident, and his exact wording is: 'And omitting recitation in the first shaf' invalidates the tahrimah according to Abu Hanifa, and according to Muhammad in one rak'ah, and according to Abu Yusuf no, rather it corrupts the performance, so he makes up four rak'ahs...etc.'; i.e., he makes up four rak'ahs according to Abu Hanifa in two cases: one: that he omits in one rak'ah of the first shaf' and in both rak'ahs of the second. And the other: that he omits in one rak'ah of the first shaf' and in one rak'ah of the second. And according to Abu Yusuf, he makes up four rak'ahs in four cases: those where omission occurs in both shaf's, two of which are those mentioned in Abu Hanifa's view. The third: that he omits recitation in all rak'ahs of both shaf's. The fourth: that he omits in both rak'ahs of the first shaf' and in one rak'ah of the second. [1] His saying: And in the rest, two rak'ahs, this relates to the statement of the two shaykhs; i.e., in the remaining of the eight cases, according to them he makes up two rak'ahs, which is six cases according to Abu Hanifa, and four cases according to Abu Yusuf's view. [2] His saying: And it is six...etc.; from here to his saying: And four according to Abu Yusuf is an explanation from the commentator, and is outside the Mukhtasar. [3] His saying: And according to Muhammad, this in the Mukhtasar is connected to his saying: And in the rest, two rak'ahs.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the qada (make-up) of witr prayer when recitation (qira'ah) is omitted in the first shaf' (pair of rak'ahs). The commentary explains that according to Abu Hanifa, omitting recitation in the first shaf' completely invalidates the tahrimah (the opening of the prayer), so the second shaf' is not validly built upon it, and thus only the first two rak'ahs need to be made up. However, the matn from al-Mukhtasar states that according to Abu Hanifa, one must make up four rak'ahs in two scenarios: either omitting recitation in one rak'ah of the first shaf' and both rak'ahs of the second, or omitting in one rak'ah of each shaf'. Abu Yusuf extends this to four scenarios where the omission occurs in both shaf's. Muhammad holds that only two rak'ahs need to be made up in all cases. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is typically the view of Abu Hanifa as stated in the Hidayah, but the text here shows the differences.

Key Terms
الشفع (al-shaf'): A pair of rak'ahs; in witr, the first two rak'ahs are the first shaf', the next two (or one) are the second shaf'.
التحريمة (al-tahrimah): The opening takbir or the state of being in prayer; here it refers to the validity of the first shaf' as a prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, in how many scenarios does one make up four rak'ahs when omitting recitation in witr?
A) 1 scenario
B) 2 scenarios
C) 3 scenarios
D) 4 scenarios

Key Takeaway
The intra-Hanafi dispute on qada of witr shows that the same principle (invalidation due to omitted recitation) yields different numbers of make-up rak'ahs depending on whether the invalidation is considered total or partial.

No Qada for Nullifying Nafl After Tashahhud or Mistakenly Starting Nafl
Ruling that no qada is required for two cases involving nafl prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi rulings where nullifying a nafl prayer does not require qada and explain the legal reasoning based on intention and commencement.

Core Idea
No qada for nafl if the second shaf' is not commenced or if the intention was for fard, not voluntary worship.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah explains two important exceptions to the general rule that a nafl prayer once commenced must be completed or made up. The first exception concerns nullifying a four-rak'ah nafl after sitting for tashahhud after two rak'ahs — the second shaf' was never started. The second exception applies to someone who begins a prayer thinking it is obligatory (fard) but then realizes it is not — the prayer turns into nafl without an original intention to undertake a voluntary act. Mastering these exceptions clarifies the subtle relationship between intention and obligation in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
Read the passage to isolate the two scenarios: (1) nullifying a four-rak'ah nafl after performing tashahhud after the first two rak'ahs, and (2) starting a prayer assuming it is fard (e.g., Zuhr) but then remembering it was already performed, causing the prayer to become nafl.
Both cases share the outcome: no qada is required.
2
Understand the rationale for Case 1
In Case 1, the person intended four rak'ahs of nafl. The first two rak'ahs constitute the first shaf' (pair). Sitting for tashahhud after them completes that shaf'. Nullifying after tashahhud means the second shaf' was never entered, so no qada is due for it. The first shaf' was completed and valid; if it was nullified after tashahhud, it was already a complete nafl of two rak'ahs, so no make-up is needed.
Compare with nullifying before tashahhud – then qada is required for the first two rak'ahs because the first shaf' was not completed.
3
Understand the rationale for Case 2
In Case 2, the person began a prayer with the intention of fard (obligatory). When they recall that they already prayed, the obligation is lifted, and the prayer becomes nafl. Since they never intended to perform a nafl voluntarily, they did not undertake a voluntary act. Therefore, nullifying it does not require qada.
Key point: The original intention was to discharge an obligation, not to add a voluntary prayer. The involuntary nafl does not bind the person to completion or qada.
4
Apply the general principle and note exceptions
The general Hanafi principle is that 'it is necessary to complete a nafl that one intentionally started.' These two cases are exceptions: in Case 1, the second shaf' was not intentionally started; in Case 2, the nafl was never intentionally started. Recognising these boundary rules sharpens your understanding of intention and obligation in nafl prayers.
The passage also notes that a follower in the mistaken prayer is similarly exempt from qada.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(ولا قضاء لو تشهد أولاً ثم نقض): أي إن نوى أربع ركعات من النفل، وقعد على الركعتين بقدر التشهد، ثم نقض لا قضاء عليه؛ لأنه لم يشرع في الشفع الثاني، فلم يجب عليه. (أو شرع ظاناً أنه عليه)، هذه المسألة وإن فهمت مما سبق، وهو قوله: ولزم إتمام نفل شرع فيه قصداً. [٤] قوله : ولا قضاء؛ أي لا يجب قضاء شيء لو تشهد بعد الركعتين وقرأ أيضاً فيهما، ثم أفسد بعدما كان نوى أربعاً؛ لأنَّ الشفع الأول قد تم، والثاني لم يشرع فيه، فلم يجب عليه، وإن نقض قبل التشهد يجب عليه قضاء الأوليين، وإن نقض بعد الشروع في الثاني يجب عليه قضاء الأخريين كما مر. [0]قوله : أو شرع؛ أي لا يجب القضاء فيما إذا شرع في صلاة على ظن أنها عليه كصلاة الظهر، ثمَّ تبيَّن أنه كان قد أدّاها، فانقلب هذا نفلاً، فإن أفسده لا يجب قضاؤه؛ لأنه كان شرع فيه لإسقاط ما في ذمته لا لإلزام نفسه بصلاة أُخرى، فإذا انقلبت صلاته نفلاً بتذكر الأداء كانت صلاة لم يلتزمها، فلا يلزمه أداؤها ولا قضاؤها لو أفسد، وكذا لا يجب القضاء على من اقتدى به في هذه الصلاة المظنونة تطوّعاً، ذكره في «التاتارخانية»، وتفصيل هذا المقام في «حواشي الدر المختار».
(And no qada if he performs tashahhud first then nullifies): i.e., if one intends four rak'ahs of nafl, sits after the first two rak'ahs for the extent of tashahhud, then nullifies, there is no qada upon him because he did not commence the second shaf', so it is not obligatory upon him. (Or if he commences thinking it is obligatory upon him), this issue, though understood from what preceded, which is his saying: 'And it is necessary to complete a nafl that one intentionally started.' [4] His saying: And no qada; i.e., no qada is required for anything if he performed tashahhud after two rak'ahs and also recited in them, then nullified after having intended four, because the first shaf' is complete and he did not commence the second, so it is not obligatory upon him. And if he nullified before tashahhud, qada of the first two is obligatory. And if he nullified after commencing the second, qada of the last two is obligatory as previously mentioned. [0] His saying: Or commences; i.e., no qada is required if he commences a prayer thinking it is obligatory upon him, such as Zuhr prayer, then it becomes clear that he had already performed it, so it turns into a nafl. If he then nullifies it, no qada is required because he started it to discharge what was in his liability, not to obligate himself with another prayer. So when it turns into nafl by remembering the performance, it is a prayer he did not undertake, so it is not necessary for him to perform it or make it up if he nullifies it. Similarly, no qada is required for the one who follows him in this assumed prayer as a voluntary act. This is mentioned in al-Tatarkhaniyyah, and the detail of this topic is in the Hashiyah of al-Durr al-Mukhtar.
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage deals with two situations where no qada (make-up) is required after nullifying a nafl prayer. First, if one intends four rak'ahs of nafl, sits after two rak'ahs for tashahhud, and then nullifies the prayer, no qada is required because the first two rak'ahs are considered a complete nafl (the first shaf') and the second shaf' was not yet commenced. However, if nullification occurs before tashahhud or after commencing the second shaf', qada becomes obligatory. Second, if one starts a prayer thinking it is fard (obligatory) but then recalls that they already performed it, the prayer becomes nafl. If they nullify it, no qada is required because they never intended to undertake a voluntary prayer. This is based on the principle that one must complete a nafl that one intentionally started, but in this case, the intention was for fard, not nafl.

Key Terms
التشهد (al-tashahhud): The testimony of faith recited while sitting in the second rak'ah of prayer.
النقض (al-naqd): Nullification of the prayer by committing an act that invalidates it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case where one starts a prayer thinking it is Zuhr (fard) but then remembers he already prayed Zuhr, what is the ruling if he nullifies the prayer?
A) He must make up the prayer
B) No qada is required
C) He must make up two rak'ahs
D) He must perform sujud al-sahw

Key Takeaway
No qada is required for nullifying a nafl when the second shaf' has not been commenced or when the nafl was never intentionally undertaken.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Omitting the Middle Tashahhud in Four-Rak'ah Nafl
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the status of the middle tashahhud in nafl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the qiyas-based ruling of Muhammad and Zufar and the istihsan-based ruling of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf regarding the validity of a four-rak'ah nafl prayer when the middle tashahhud is omitted.

Core Idea
In four-rak'ah nafl, omitting the middle sitting is valid by istihsan, but invalid by qiyas.

This lesson examines a fascinating dispute within the Hanafi school itself. When a person prays four rak'ahs of nafl and forgets or intentionally omits the sitting (tashahhud) after the first two rak'ahs, what is the ruling? Two prominent students of Abu Hanifa, Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani and Zufar ibn al-Hudhayl, argued that the first two rak'ahs become invalid based on qiyas. However, the founding imam, Abu Hanifa, along with Abu Yusuf, ruled that the prayer remains valid, using the principle of istihsan. Understanding this dispute illuminates the school's methodological hierarchy and the practical consequences for worshippers.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: the prayer is valid and no repetition is required.
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Muhammad and Zufar hold that the first pair becomes invalid and must be repeated.
They rely on qiyas.
3
Analyse the opponent's proof
Their qiyas: each pair of nafl is an independent prayer, so the sitting after two rak'ahs is fard (like the final sitting). Omitting it invalidates that unit.
The 'illa is that the sitting is the final sitting of an independent unit.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf use istihsan: the middle sitting in nafl is not prescribed for its own sake, but as an exit point. Since the worshipper continues, the sitting was never required.
They analogize to obligatory prayer where the first sitting is sunnah, not fard.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if the middle tashahhud is omitted, according to Muhammad/Zufar the first two rak'ahs must be repeated; according to Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf the prayer is valid as is.
The mufta bihi is the ruling of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو لم يقعد في وسطه

قوله: فهاهنا صرح بها؛ لكون التصريح أبلغ في البيان، فاندفع ما أورد من أنّ في المتن تكراراً لا فائدة فيه.

قوله: كان ينبغي ... الخ؛ يعني أن مقتضى القياس أن يفسد الشفع الأول ويجب قضاءه؛ لأنَّ كلّ شفع من التطوع صلاة مستقلة، فالقعدة على رأس الركعتين تكون فرضاً لما تقرر أن القعدة الأخيرة فرض، وبترك الفرض تبطل الصلاة عمداً كان أو سهواً، وهذا هو قول محمد وزفر. وعند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف لا يفسد استحساناً؛ لأنَّ القعود على رأس الركعتين من النفل لم تفرض بعينها، بل لغيرها، وهو الخروج على تقدير القطع على رأسهما، فلما لم يقطع وصلاه أربعاً لم تفرض القعدة قياساً على الفرض كذا في «المنية» وشروحها.
Or he did not sit in its middle. [Commentary: His saying: 'here it is expressly stated' because the explicit statement is more eloquent in explanation, so the objection that there is useless repetition in the text is refuted. His saying: 'it would be proper...' means that the requirement of analogy (qiyas) is that the first pair becomes invalid and its qada is obligatory, because each pair of the supererogatory is an independent prayer. Thus the sitting at the end of two rak'ahs is obligatory (fard) since it is established that the final sitting is fard, and by leaving a fard the prayer becomes invalid whether intentionally or forgetfully. This is the view of Muhammad and Zufar. According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, it does not become invalid due to istihsan, because the sitting at the end of two rak'ahs in nafl is not prescribed for its own sake, but for something else, which is exiting, on the condition of cutting off. So when he did not cut off and prayed four rak'ahs, the sitting was not prescribed, by analogy with the obligatory prayer. Thus in al-Munyah and its commentaries.]
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This section presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of a four-rak'ah nafl prayer when the worshipper does not sit for tashahhud after the first two rak'ahs (i.e., he stands directly for the third). Imam Muhammad and Imam Zufar argue by qiyas that each two rak'ahs are an independent unit, and the sitting at the end of the first two is the final sitting of that unit, which is fard. Omitting it, whether intentionally or forgetfully, invalidates that unit and requires qada. Thus the first two rak'ahs are invalid and must be repeated. Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf, however, rule by istihsan that the prayer remains valid. Their reasoning: the sitting after two rak'ahs in nafl is not intrinsically obligatory; it is only prescribed as an exit point if one wishes to stop. Since the worshipper does not stop but continues, the sitting was never required. This is analogous to the obligatory prayer: in a four-rak'ah fard, the first sitting is not fard but sunnah. Therefore, omitting it does not invalidate. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, as it is based on istihsan and is the majority view.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): A legal method that prefers a ruling different from qiyas due to a stronger evidence or need for ease.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning; extending a ruling from an original case to a new case based on a common effective cause ('illa).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the dispute presented, which imams hold that a four-rak'ah nafl prayer becomes invalid if one does not sit for tashahhud after the first two rak'ahs?
A) Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf
B) Muhammad and Zufar
C) All Hanafi imams
D) Only Abu Hanifa

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the mufta bihi position on omitting the middle tashahhud in four-rak'ah nafl is that the prayer remains valid, by istihsan.

Permissibility of Praying Nafl While Sitting
Ruling on performing supererogatory prayer while sitting even if able to stand

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on performing nafl prayer while sitting without excuse and explain the hadith evidence for reduced reward.

Core Idea
Nafl while sitting without excuse is permissible but reward is halved.

This lesson addresses a common question: can one pray extra (nafl) prayers while sitting even if able to stand? The ruling distinguishes between obligatory (fard) and voluntary prayers. Here we explore the permissibility, the evidence, and the consequences for reward based on a famous hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is performing nafl (supererogatory) prayer while sitting, even when capable of standing. The ruling is that it is permissible (ja'iz), not sinful.
Contrast with fard prayer, where standing is a fard condition.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith: 'صلاة القاعد على النصف من صلاة القائم' (The prayer of one sitting is half the prayer of one standing). This is reported by al-Bukhari and others.
The hadith is ahad, giving zanni thubut and dalalah.
3
Analyse the dalil's implication
The hadith compares reward, not validity. It implies that while the act is valid (same obligation of intention and rukn), the reward is reduced to half. This confirms permission without full reward.
Thus, no sin, only diminished merit.
4
Note the preferred sitting posture
The preferred posture is that of tashahhud (mujtami'an), but there is a choice if no excuse.
This is from al-Hidayah.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that sitting is permissible even without excuse, but reward is reduced. This is the established view in Zahir al-Riwayah.
No intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويتنفّل قاعداً مع قدرة قيامه ابتداء

قوله: يتنقل؛ أي يجوز أداء النفل قاعداً مع القدرة على القيام بخلاف الفرض، فإنّ القيام فيه فرض لا يجوز تركه إلا بعذر، نعم إن صلى قاعداً نفلاً من غير عذر نقص ثوابه؛ لحديث: «صلاة القاعد على النصف من صلاة القائم»، أخرجه البخاري وأصحاب السنن، ويُخيّرُ في كيفية القعود، والمختار على ما في «الهداية» وغيره أن يقعد على هيئة التشهد إلا من عذر.
And he performs nafl sitting while being able to stand initially. [Commentary: His saying: 'he performs nafl' means it is permissible to perform nafl while sitting even if one can stand, unlike the obligatory prayer, for standing in it is fard and cannot be left without an excuse. Indeed, if one prays nafl sitting without an excuse, his reward is reduced due to the hadith: 'The prayer of one sitting is half the prayer of one standing,' reported by al-Bukhari and the authors of the Sunan. He is given a choice in the manner of sitting, and the preferred position according to al-Hidayah and others is to sit in the posture of tashahhud unless there is an excuse.]
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This ruling states that it is permissible to perform voluntary (nafl) prayers while sitting even if one is capable of standing. This is unlike the obligatory prayers, where standing is a fard condition that cannot be omitted without a valid excuse. If one prays nafl while sitting without any excuse, his reward is diminished to half that of the standing prayer, as established by the authentic hadith reported by al-Bukhari and others. The preferred manner of sitting is the same as the sitting for tashahhud, i.e., sitting on the left foot with the right foot upright, unless one has a genuine excuse to sit differently.

Key Terms
نفل (nafl): Supererogatory or voluntary prayer beyond the obligatory acts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) No reward
C) Half the reward
D) Double the reward

Key Takeaway
Performing nafl prayer while sitting without excuse is valid but yields half the reward of standing.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Missing the Middle Sitting in Nafl Prayer
Intra-Hanafi dispute on omitting middle sitting in nafl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on omitting the middle sitting in nafl prayer and explain the basis of istihsan over qiyas.

Core Idea
In nafl, the middle sitting is not fard; omitting it does not invalidate by istihsan.

The Hanafi school internally differs on whether omitting the sitting after two rak'ahs in a four-rak'ah nafl prayer invalidates the first unit. This lesson examines the dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (valid) and Imam Muhammad and Zufar (invalid), focusing on the interplay between qiyas and istihsan. You will learn the relied-upon position and the reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the issue
The act is a four-rak'ah nafl prayer where the worshipper omits the sitting (tashahhud) after the first two rak'ahs. The issue is whether this omission invalidates the first pair (shaf') or not.
The issue arises because each shaf' in nafl is considered an independent prayer by some.
2
State the two opposing views
State the view of Muhammad and Zufar: the first shaf' is invalid and must be repeated. Then state the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: the prayer is valid and no repetition is needed.
These are both Hanafi views; the dispute is within the madhhab.
3
Analyze the qiyas of the opposing view
The opposing view uses qiyas: each two rak'ahs in nafl is like a separate prayer, so the sitting after two is the final sitting (fard), and omitting it invalidates that unit.
Understand the analogy: asl is a 2-rak'ah independent prayer; far is the first shaf' of nafl.
4
Understand the istihsan of the majority
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf use istihsan: the sitting in the middle of nafl is not prescribed as fard in itself but only as a preparation for possible termination. Since the worshipper continued, it does not become fard. This overrides the qiyas of the opposing view.
Istihsan is a source of law that allows departing from qiyas for a more equitable result.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and its implication
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: the prayer is valid. The practical consequence is that no repetition is required.
This is the position followed in fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو لم يقعد في وسطه) : أي إذا صلى أربع ركعات من النفل، ولم يقعد في وسطه ، وكان ينبغي أن يفسد الشفعُ الأول ، ويجب قضاؤه ؛ لأن كل شفع من النفل صلاةٌ على حدة، ومع ذلك لا يفسدُ الشَّفَعُ الأول قياساً على الفرض. (٢) قوله : كان ينبغي ... الخ ؛ يعني أن مقتضى القياس أن يفسد الشفع الأول ويجب قضاءه ؛ لأنَّ كلّ شفع من التطوع صلاة مستقلة، فالقعدة على رأس الركعتين تكون فرضاً لما تقرر أن القعدة الأخيرة فرض، وبترك الفرض تبطل الصلاة عمداً كان أو سهواً، وهذا هو قول محمد وزفر . وعند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف لا يفسد استحساناً ؛ لأنَّ القعود على رأس الركعتين من النفل لم تفرض بعينها، بل لغيرها، وهو الخروج على تقدير القطع على رأسهما، فلما لم يقطع وصلاه أربعاً لم تفرض القعدة قياساً على الفرض كذا في «المنية» وشروحها.
He said: 'Or he did not sit in its middle' meaning: if he prayed four rak'ahs of nafl and did not sit in its middle, it would be necessary that the first pair becomes invalid and must be made up, because every pair of nafl is a separate prayer; yet the first pair is not invalidated by analogy with the obligatory prayer. He said: 'It would be necessary... etc.' meaning that the requirement of analogy is that the first pair becomes invalid and must be made up because every pair of supererogatory prayer is an independent prayer, so the sitting at the end of two rak'ahs becomes obligatory (fard) since it is established that the last sitting is fard, and by omitting a fard the prayer is invalidated whether done intentionally or forgetfully. This is the view of Muhammad and Zufar. According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, it is not invalidated by istihsan because the sitting at the end of two rak'ahs in nafl is not prescribed as fard in itself, but for something else, which is exiting (the prayer) on the assumption of cutting off according to their view; since he did not cut off but prayed four, the sitting did not become fard, by analogy with the obligatory prayer. This is as stated in Al-Munyah and its commentaries.
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the ruling on performing four rak'ahs of nafl prayer without sitting for tashahhud after the first two rak'ahs. The text first explains the apparent meaning of the matn: if one prays four rak'ahs of nafl and omits the middle sitting, the first pair (shaf') would be invalid according to qiyas (analogy) because each pair of two rak'ahs in nafl is an independent unit of prayer. The sitting at the end of two rak'ahs would be considered the final sitting (fard) for that unit, and omitting it invalidates that unit. This is the position of Imam Muhammad and Imam Zufar. However, the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, who rule by istihsan (juristic preference) that the first pair is not invalidated. Their reasoning is that the sitting in the middle of a four-rak'ah nafl prayer is not prescribed as fard in itself; rather, it is intended as a preparation for the possibility of ending the prayer at that point. Since the worshipper continues to four rak'ahs, the sitting does not become obligatory. This is analogous to the obligatory prayer where missing the first sitting does not invalidate the prayer. The text cites Al-Munyah and its commentaries as sources for this ruling. The mufta bihi (operative position for fatwa) is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and the prayer remains valid without requiring repetition.

Key Terms
شَفْع (shaf'): A pair of rak'ahs; in nafl each two rak'ahs is considered a separate unit of prayer.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; a method of reasoning that overrides qiyas in favor of a more equitable ruling.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning used to derive a ruling for a new case based on a similar established case.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The first two rak'ahs are invalid and must be repeated.
B) The prayer is valid and no repetition is needed.
C) The entire prayer is invalid.
D) Only the first two rak'ahs are valid.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, omitting the middle sitting in nafl prayer does not invalidate the prayer, due to istihsan overriding qiyas.

Ruling on Sitting in Nafl Prayer: Permissibility and Degrees of Dislike
Rulings on starting nafl sitting and switching from standing to sitting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on starting nafl prayer sitting, explain the hadith proof, and distinguish between Abu Hanifa's and Imam Muhammad's views on sitting after starting standing.

Core Idea
Starting nafl sitting is permissible; sitting after starting standing is mildly disliked; the soundest view is no dislike.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah clarifies the rulings on sitting during nafl prayer. It addresses whether one may start a nafl prayer sitting if able to stand, and whether switching from standing to sitting is allowed. The text presents the proof from hadith, an intra-Hanafi disagreement, and the preferred view of later authorities.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish fard from nafl
Identify that standing in fard is a rukn, but in nafl it is not. Hence, sitting in nafl is permissible but reduces reward.
This is the foundational distinction.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith 'صلاة القاعد على النصف من صلاة القائم' (prayer of the sitter is half of the stander) indicates permissibility with lesser reward.
This hadith is reported by Bukhari and others.
3
Examine the starting case vs. the switching case
Starting nafl sitting is allowed without excuse. But if one starts standing, then sits, it is deemed makruh tanzihi (or not) according to different views.
The text uses 'kareha' (disliked) for switching.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Muhammad holds that switching is not permissible, analogizing the start to a vow. Abu Hanifa holds it is permissible but disliked.
The majority respond that starting does not obligate all parts.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
Later authorities (Al-Bahr, Al-Ghunya) state that there is no dislike at all; this is the most correct view.
This is the operative position for fatwa today.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يتنفل قاعداً مع قدرة قيامه ابتداء 11 ] قوله : فهاهنا صرح بها ؛ لكون التصريح أبلغ في البيان، فاندفع ما أورد من أنّ في المتن تكراراً لا فائدة فيه. (٣) قوله : يتنقل ؛ أي يجوز أداء النفل قاعداً مع القدرة على القيام بخلاف الفرض ، فإنّ القيام فيه فرض لا يجوز تركه إلا بعذر ، نعم إن صلى قاعداً نفلاً من غير عذر نقص ثوابه ؛ لحديث: «صلاة القاعد على النصف من صلاة القائم» ، أخرجه البخاري وأصحاب السنن، ويُخيّرُ في كيفية القعود، والمختار على ما في «الهداية»(۲) وغيره أن يقعد على هيئة التشهد إلا من عذر. وكره بقاء إلا بعذر وراكباً مومئاً خارج المصر وكره بقاء إلا بعذر ) : أي إن قَدِرَ على القيام يجوز أن يشرع في النفل قاعداً، وإن شَرَعَ في النَّفْلِ قائماً كُرة أن يقعد فيه مع القدرة على القيام إلا بعذر، فأراد بحال الابتداء حالَ الشَّروع، وبحال البقاء حالَ وجودِهِ الذي بعد الشروع. [٢]قوله : قاعداً...الخ ؛ ويجوز أيضاً أن يتمه قائماً ويقوم قبل الركوع، حين يبقى قدر من القرآن فيركع ويسجد قائماً ، ثبت ذلك من الفعل النبوي صلى الله عليه وسلم في «صحيح مسلم، وغيره. [٣]قوله : كره ؛ الظاهر أنّ الكراهة تنزيهيّة، وهذا على ما اختاره بعض المشايخ ، والأصح أنه لا كراهة، صرح به في «البحر» و«الغُنية» وغيرهما.
He performs nafl sitting while able to stand initially. He said: here he explicitly stated it because explicitness is more effective in explanation, thus refuting the objection that there is repetition in the matn without benefit. (3) His statement: 'he performs nafl' means it is permissible to perform nafl sitting while able to stand, unlike obligatory prayer, where standing is fard and may not be left except for an excuse. However, if one prays nafl sitting without an excuse, his reward is diminished due to the hadith: 'The prayer of one sitting is half the prayer of one standing' – reported by Bukhari and the authors of Sunan. He has a choice in how to sit, but the preferred method as in Al-Hidayah and others is to sit in the posture of tashahhud unless there is an excuse. 'And it is disliked to continue sitting except with an excuse, and (praying) while riding and gesturing outside the city.' Meaning: if he is able to stand, it is permissible to start nafl sitting; but if he started nafl standing, it is disliked for him to sit while able to stand except with an excuse. He meant by 'initial state' the state of beginning, and by 'state of remaining' the state after beginning. [1] His statement: 'disliked' means permissible with dislike. According to Imam Muhammad, it is not permissible because the start is considered like a vow in commitment; if he vows to pray standing, he may not sit, so too if he commits by starting. The answer is that he did not undertake to stand for the remaining parts, so the start does not obligate all parts. [2] His statement: 'sitting... etc.' It is also permissible to complete it standing and to stand before ruku', when there remains a quantity of Quran (to recite), then he bows and prostrates standing. This is established from the Prophetic action in Sahih Muslim and others. [3] His statement: 'disliked' – apparently it is a mild dislike (karahah tanzihiyyah). This is as chosen by some scholars, but the most correct is that there is no dislike, as stated in Al-Bahr and Al-Ghunya and others.
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This passage provides the rulings on sitting during nafl prayer. It first establishes that it is permissible to begin nafl prayer while sitting even if one is able to stand, unlike obligatory prayer where standing is mandatory. However, if one chooses to sit without an excuse, the reward is reduced to half, as indicated by the authenticated hadith. The worshipper may choose how to sit, but the preferred method is in the tashahhud posture. Then the discussion addresses the case where one starts the nafl while standing. In this scenario, it is considered disliked (makruh tanzihi) to subsequently sit down if one is still able to stand, unless there is an excuse. Imam Muhammad holds that it is not permissible at all, analogizing the start of prayer to a vow: if one vows to pray standing, he cannot sit. However, the majority respond that starting does not create a commitment for all parts; he only committed to the acts he performed. The text also notes that some later scholars, such as those in Al-Bahr and Al-Ghunya, hold that there is no dislike at all, and this is considered the sounder view. Additionally, it is permissible to begin standing, then sit for part of the recitation, and then stand again for ruku' and sujud, as demonstrated by the practice of the Prophet ﷺ in Sahih Muslim.

Key Terms
نفل (nafl): Supererogatory prayer; voluntary acts of worship beyond the obligatory.
كراهة تنزيهية (karahah tanzihiyyah): Mild dislike; an act that is better to avoid but is not sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the most correct view in the Hanafi school (as per Al-Bahr and Al-Ghunya), what is the ruling on sitting in nafl prayer after having started standing, if one is able to stand?
A) Haram
B) Makruh Tahrimi
C) Makruh Tanzihi
D) No dislike (ja'iz)

Key Takeaway
Starting nafl sitting is permissible with half reward; sitting after starting standing is subject to ikhtilaf, but the soundest view is that it is not disliked.

Defining Gesturing in Prayer and the Travel Zone
Defining legal terms for prayer on a riding animal and the travel zone

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of 'ima'' (gesturing) in prayer and explain the Hanafi definition of 'outside the city' as the place where qasr is permitted, distinguishing it from fixed-distance definitions.

Core Idea
Gesturing replaces bowing and prostration; 'outside the city' is where travel concessions begin, not a fixed mileage.

This lesson examines two critical terms from the matn that define the parameters of prayer for a traveler: the concept of gesturing (ima') and the geographical limit of the city (misr). Understanding these definitions is essential for correctly applying the rulings of prayer during travel. The passage clarifies the linguistic origin of 'momi'an' and establishes the authoritative Hanafi view on 'outside the city' as cited from Al-Bahr.

Guided Path
1
Linguistic parsing of 'مومئاً'
Identify the root and verb form: awma'a with hamza, though some Arabs use a ya. Understand the literal meaning of gesturing.
This establishes the correct pronunciation and derivation.
2
Legal definition of 'مومئاً'
In fiqh, it refers to performing ruku' and sujud through head gestures when unable to physically bow or prostrate, e.g., when praying on a riding animal.
Gesture substitutes for the actual movements.
3
Linguistic and legal definition of 'خارج المصر'
Literally 'outside the city', legally defined as the place where qasr (shortening prayer) is permitted for a traveler.
It is not a fixed distance but the start of travel.
4
Identify the correct Hanafi view
The text states 'this is the correct view' as per Al-Bahr, affirming that 'outside the city' is where qasr is allowed, whether it is outside a city or a village.
This distinguishes it from other opinions that require a specific distance.
5
Distinguish from other opinions
Some schools define 'outside the city' as a fixed distance (e.g., two marhalah). The Hanafi school uses a functional definition based on the commencement of travel.
This leads to practical differences in when qasr becomes permissible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : مومئاً ؛ بالهمز في الآخر ، تقول : أَوْمَأْتُ إليه، لا أَوْمَيْتُ، وقد تقول العرب : أومى بالياء أيضاً. كذا في «المغرب» : أي ساجداً أو راكعاً إيماء. قوله : خارج المصر؛ المراد به محل القصر، الذي يجوز فيه للمسافر قـصـر الصلاة خارج المصر كان أو خارج القرية، هذا هو الصحيح. كذا في «البحر»
His statement: 'gesturing' (momi'an) with a hamza at the end; you say auma'tu ilayhi (I gestured to him), not aumaytu; and some Arabs say auma with a ya as well. As stated in Al-Mughrib: it means prostrating or bowing by gesture. His statement: 'outside the city' means the place where shortening (qasr) is permitted, where it is permissible for the traveler to shorten prayer, whether outside the city or outside the village. This is the correct view, as stated in Al-Bahr.
Source pages p. 230

Commentary
This passage provides definitions of two key terms from the matn related to prayer during travel: 'gesturing' (مومئاً) and 'outside the city' (خارج المصر). Regarding the first term, the text clarifies its linguistic form: the verb is awma'a with a hamza, though some Arabs drop the hamza. In legal context, it refers to performing the actions of bowing (ruku') and prostration (sujud) by means of head gestures (ima'), which is allowed when one is unable to perform the physical movements normally, for example when praying on a riding animal. The second term, 'outside the city', is defined as the area where the traveler may shorten prayers (qasr). This is the generally accepted definition, contrasting with other opinions that specify a particular distance like one mile or two farsakhs. The text cites Al-Bahr as the source for this correct view.

Key Terms
إيماء (ima'): Gesture; in prayer, performing ruku' and sujud by head motions when unable to do physically.
خارج المصر (kharj al-misr): The area outside the city limits where travel rulings apply, specifically where qasr is permitted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One mile beyond the city.
B) The area where the traveler may shorten prayer.
C) The last building of the city.
D) Any place outside the city regardless of distance.

Key Takeaway
Gesturing (ima') substitutes physical movements in prayer when unable; the travel zone (خارج المصر) is defined by the permissibility of qasr, not a fixed distance.

Sitting in Optional Prayer After Starting Standing
Commentary on matn regarding sitting in nafl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sitting in nafl after starting standing and identify the intra-Hanafi disagreement.

Core Idea
Sitting after starting standing in nafl is permissible; the later relied view is no dislike.

This lesson examines the ruling for someone who begins an optional prayer standing but later decides to sit. The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement on permissibility and dislike, with the later mufta bihi being pure permissibility without dislike.

Guided Path
1
State the issue
Identify the act: starting a nafl prayer standing, then sitting while able to stand.
2
Identify the Hanafi positions
State Abu Hanifa's, Abu Yusuf's, and Muhammad's views per the text.
Abu Hanifa permits without karaha; Abu Yusuf permits; Muhammad does not permit except for excuse.
3
Examine the evidence
Read the hadith from 'A'ishah cited in the commentary.
The Prophet (saw) would sit and then stand before ruku.
4
Apply the tarjih
Note that the later relied-upon view is no karaha, per 'al-Bahr' and 'al-Ghunya'.
5
State the mufta bihi
The operative ruling for fatwa is that it is permissible without dislike.

And it is disliked to remain (sitting) except for an excuse, and (praying) as a rider gesturing outside the city. [1] His saying: 'disliked' means it is permissible with dislike, and according to Muhammad (al-Shaybani), may God be pleased with him, it is not permissible because the initiation is considered like a vow in terms of obligation; so if one vows to pray standing, it is not permissible for him to sit, similarly if he obligates it by initiation. The response: he did not actually perform the standing for the remaining part, so initiation does not necessitate all its parts. [2] His saying: 'sitting...' etc.; It is also permissible for him to complete it standing and to stand before bowing, when a portion of the Quran remains, then he bows and prostrates standing. This is established from the prophetic action, peace be upon him, in Sahih Muslim and others. [3] His saying: 'disliked'; apparently the dislike is tanzihi (not severely disliked), and this is according to the choice of some shaykhs, but the most correct is that there is no dislike, as stated in 'al-Bahr' and 'al-Ghunya' and others. [4] His saying: 'gesturing' with a hamza at the end; one says 'awma'tu ilayhi', not 'awmaytu', and sometimes the Arabs say 'awma' with ya' as well. As in 'al-Mughrib': meaning prostrating or bowing with gestures. [0] His saying: 'outside the city'; what is meant is the place where shortening is permissible, where it is permissible for the traveler to shorten prayer, whether outside the city or outside the village. This is the correct view. As in 'al-Bahr'. (1) The author (al-Marghinani) decisively stated the dislike of nafl while sitting if one started it standing while able to stand except for an excuse, and the commentator followed him in his commentary, and in 'al-Niqayah', 'al-Mukhtar', 'al-Multaqa', and 'Durar al-Hukkam'. But it is said in 'al-Durr al-Mukhtar': the most correct is that there is no dislike, following 'al-Bahr', and this is the choice of the author of 'Bidayat al-Mubtadi', 'al-Kanz', and 'al-Munya'. This is according to Imam Abu Hanifa. As for the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is not permissible except for an excuse. See 'Mukhtasar al-Quduri'. (2) From 'A'ishah, may God be pleased with her: 'The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, used to pray sitting and recite while sitting, and when there remained from his recitation about thirty or forty verses, he would stand and recite while standing, then bow, then prostrate, then do the same in the second rak'ah.' In Sahih Muslim, etc. (3) 'al-Mughrib' (p.496): 'And sometimes the Arabs say awma bira'sihi meaning he indicated no.' (4) It is said: if he goes a mile; it is said: two or three farsakhs. See: 'Radd al-Muhtar'. (5) 'al-Bahr al-Raiq' (2:69). To other than the qibla, he only said 'outside the city' due to the saying of Ibn 'Umar: 'I saw the Messenger of God praying on a donkey while heading to Khaybar, gesturing with gestures.' And since this action was contrary to analogy, it was confined to its specific case. According to him (Abu Hanifa), and according to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is permissible in the city as well, but with dislike according to Muhammad, may God be pleased with him. As in 'Hilbat al-Mujalli'. [1] His saying: 'to other than the qibla'; meaning whichever direction the animal faces, and it is not a condition to face the qibla at the start of the prayer; indeed it is recommended when there is no difficulty. And if he prays to other than the direction the animal faces and to other than the qibla, it is not permissible. As in 'al-Bahr' and 'al-Hilbah'. [2] His saying: 'due to the saying of Ibn 'Umar'; i.e., 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar ibn al-Khattab: 'I saw the Messenger of God...' the hadith, narrated by Muslim, Abu Dawud, and al-Nasa'i, but in it there is no 'gesturing with gestures', and that has been established from the narration of Jabir, may God be pleased with him, in Ibn Hibban's Sahih, and Anas in al-Daraqutni's book 'Ghara'ib Malik'. [3] His saying: 'And since...' etc.; its summary: Since performing nafl to other than the qibla was established from the Lawgiver, and it is contrary to the principles because it contradicts texts that make facing the qibla obligatory, this ruling was confined to the specific case where it was narrated, which is performing nafl outside the city, and it does not extend to performing nafl within the city, nor to obligatory prayers.
Source pages p. 230

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on a matn that states two rulings regarding optional (nafl) prayers: first, it is disliked to remain sitting in nafl after starting it standing unless there is an excuse; second, a rider may perform nafl with gestures (ima') outside the city, even if not facing the qibla. The commentary clarifies each part. For the first ruling, the commentator explains that 'disliked' here means permissible with dislike (karaha tanzihiyya). Imam Muhammad holds it is absolutely impermissible, likening the initiation of prayer to a vow. The response is that the standing performed at the start does not necessitate standing for the remaining parts. The commentator notes that some later scholars (e.g., from 'al-Bahr' and 'al-Ghunya') consider there is no dislike at all—this is the relied-upon view (mufta bihi). For the second ruling, the commentary defines 'gesturing' (ima') linguistically and explains that 'outside the city' refers to the place where shortening (qasr) is permitted. The hadith of Ibn 'Umar (saw) is cited as the proof: the Prophet (saw) prayed on a donkey heading to Khaybar with gestures. Since this action contradicts the general obligation to face the qibla, the concession is limited to the specific case: optional prayers outside the city. Abu Hanifa confines it to outside the city, while the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) permit it within the city, though Muhammad regards it as disliked. The commentary then discusses facing the qibla: the rider may pray in whatever direction the animal faces, without the initial condition of facing the qibla. However, it is recommended to face the qibla when possible. If one prays in a direction other than both the animal's direction and the qibla, it is invalid. Finally, the reasoning behind limiting the concession is explained: since the ruling is contrary to general principles (usul), it cannot be extended analogically. Thus, it applies only to nafl outside the city, not to obligatory prayers or nafl within the city.

Key Terms
كراهة تنزيهية (karāha tanzīhiyya): A level of dislike that does not necessitate sin; the act is permissible but avoiding it is better.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the most correct view (al-ashahh) in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on sitting in a nafl prayer after starting it standing?
A) It is impermissible and invalidates the prayer.
B) It is permissible with dislike (makruh tanzihi).
C) It is permissible without dislike.
D) It is obligatory to remain standing.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is that sitting in nafl after starting standing is permissible without dislike, based on prophetic practice.

Performing Optional Prayer While Riding Outside the City
Commentary on matn regarding rider's prayer outside city

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing voluntary prayers on a mount with gestures outside the city and identify the scope of the concession.

Core Idea
Nafl prayer on a moving mount with gestures is a specific concession limited to outside the city.

This lesson covers the unique dispensation for optional prayers while traveling on an animal without facing the qibla. The Hanafi school confines this concession to outside the city limits, based on the hadith of Ibn 'Umar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
The act is performing a voluntary (nafl) prayer while riding on an animal, using gestures (ima') for bowing and prostration, and not facing the qibla.
2
State the Hanafi position on location
Abu Hanifa restricts the concession to outside the city (kharij al-misr). Abu Yusuf and Muhammad permit it inside the city, but Muhammad considers it disliked.
Note the disagreement on location.
3
Examine the evidence
The hadith of Ibn 'Umar: the Prophet (saw) prayed on a donkey heading to Khaybar with gestures.
This is the direct proof.
4
Understand the legal reasoning
Since this ruling contradicts the general principle of facing qibla, it is confined to the specific case mentioned (outside the city) and not extended by qiyas.
The commentary says 'li-annahu khilaf al-usul fa-uqtusira 'ala mawridihi'.
5
State the mufta bihi
The relied-upon view is that of Imam Abu Hanifa: the concession is limited to outside the city.
From 'al-Bahr' and 'Hilbat al-Mujalli'.

And it is disliked to remain (sitting) except for an excuse, and (praying) as a rider gesturing outside the city. [1] His saying: 'disliked' means it is permissible with dislike, and according to Muhammad (al-Shaybani), may God be pleased with him, it is not permissible because the initiation is considered like a vow in terms of obligation; so if one vows to pray standing, it is not permissible for him to sit, similarly if he obligates it by initiation. The response: he did not actually perform the standing for the remaining part, so initiation does not necessitate all its parts. [2] His saying: 'sitting...' etc.; It is also permissible for him to complete it standing and to stand before bowing, when a portion of the Quran remains, then he bows and prostrates standing. This is established from the prophetic action, peace be upon him, in Sahih Muslim and others. [3] His saying: 'disliked'; apparently the dislike is tanzihi (not severely disliked), and this is according to the choice of some shaykhs, but the most correct is that there is no dislike, as stated in 'al-Bahr' and 'al-Ghunya' and others. As in 'al-Mughrib': meaning prostrating or bowing with gestures. (1) The author (al-Marghinani) decisively stated the dislike of nafl while sitting if one started it standing while able to stand except for an excuse, and the commentator followed him in his commentary, and in 'al-Niqayah', 'al-Mukhtar', 'al-Multaqa', and 'Durar al-Hukkam'. But it is said in 'al-Durr al-Mukhtar': the most correct is that there is no dislike, following 'al-Bahr', and this is the choice of the author of 'Bidayat al-Mubtadi', 'al-Kanz', and 'al-Munya'. This is according to Imam Abu Hanifa. As for the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is not permissible except for an excuse. See 'Mukhtasar al-Quduri'. (2) From 'A'ishah, may God be pleased with her: 'The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, used to pray sitting and recite while sitting, and when there remained from his recitation about thirty or forty verses, he would stand and recite while standing, then bow, then prostrate, then do the same in the second rak'ah.' See: 'Radd al-Muhtar'. (5) 'al-Bahr al-Raiq' (2:69). To other than the qibla, he only said 'outside the city' due to the saying of Ibn 'Umar: 'I saw the Messenger of God praying on a donkey while heading to Khaybar, gesturing with gestures.' And since this action was contrary to analogy, it was confined to its specific case. According to him (Abu Hanifa), and according to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is permissible in the city as well, but with dislike according to Muhammad, may God be pleased with him. As in 'Hilbat al-Mujalli'. [1] His saying: 'to other than the qibla'; meaning whichever direction the animal faces, and it is not a condition to face the qibla at the start of the prayer; indeed it is recommended when there is no difficulty. And if he prays to other than the direction the animal faces and to other than the qibla, it is not permissible. As in 'al-Bahr' and 'al-Hilbah'. [2] His saying: 'due to the saying of Ibn 'Umar'; i.e., 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar ibn al-Khattab: 'I saw the Messenger of God...' the hadith, narrated by Muslim, Abu Dawud, and al-Nasa'i, but in it there is no 'gesturing with gestures', and that has been established from the narration of Jabir, may God be pleased with him, in Ibn Hibban's Sahih, and Anas in al-Daraqutni's book 'Ghara'ib Malik'. [3] His saying: 'And since...' etc.; its summary: Since performing nafl to other than the qibla was established from the Lawgiver, and it is contrary to the principles because it contradicts texts that make facing the qibla obligatory, this ruling was confined to the specific case where it was narrated, which is performing nafl outside the city, and it does not extend to performing nafl within the city, nor to obligatory prayers.
Source pages p. 230

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on a matn that states two rulings regarding optional (nafl) prayers: first, it is disliked to remain sitting in nafl after starting it standing unless there is an excuse; second, a rider may perform nafl with gestures (ima') outside the city, even if not facing the qibla. The commentary clarifies each part. For the first ruling, the commentator explains that 'disliked' here means permissible with dislike (karaha tanzihiyya). Imam Muhammad holds it is absolutely impermissible, likening the initiation of prayer to a vow. The response is that the standing performed at the start does not necessitate standing for the remaining parts. The commentator notes that some later scholars (e.g., from 'al-Bahr' and 'al-Ghunya') consider there is no dislike at all—this is the relied-upon view (mufta bihi). For the second ruling, the commentary defines 'gesturing' (ima') linguistically and explains that 'outside the city' refers to the place where shortening (qasr) is permitted. The hadith of Ibn 'Umar (saw) is cited as the proof: the Prophet (saw) prayed on a donkey heading to Khaybar with gestures. Since this action contradicts the general obligation to face the qibla, the concession is limited to the specific case: optional prayers outside the city. Abu Hanifa confines it to outside the city, while the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) permit it within the city, though Muhammad regards it as disliked. The commentary then discusses facing the qibla: the rider may pray in whatever direction the animal faces, without the initial condition of facing the qibla. However, it is recommended to face the qibla when possible. If one prays in a direction other than both the animal's direction and the qibla, it is invalid. Finally, the reasoning behind limiting the concession is explained: since the ruling is contrary to general principles (usul), it cannot be extended analogically. Thus, it applies only to nafl outside the city, not to obligatory prayers or nafl within the city.

Key Terms
مومئاً (mūmi'an): Performing gestures (īmā') instead of normal bowing and prostration, typically when riding or unable to fully bend.
خارج المصر (khārij al-miṣr): Outside the city or town, specifically the area where it is legally permissible to shorten prayers (qasr).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi, where is the concession for performing nafl prayer with gestures on a mount applicable?
A) Inside the city only.
B) Outside the city only.
C) Both inside and outside the city.
D) Only in the mosque.

Key Takeaway
The rider's gesture prayer for nafl is a specific concession limited to outside the city; inside the city, normal qibla conditions apply.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Praying Nawafil on a Riding Animal: Ruling and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on nawafil on a ride without qibla

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying nawafil on a riding animal without facing the qibla, distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and apply the condition that starting the prayer on the ground then mounting invalidates it.

Core Idea
Nawafil on a ride without qibla is restricted to outside the city according to Abu Hanifa; the Sahibayn permit it inside.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah explains when it is permissible to perform voluntary prayers (nawafil) on a riding animal without facing the qibla, a practice established by the Prophet (saw) outside Medina. The author presents an intra-Hanafi disagreement: Imam Abu Hanifa limits this exception to outside the city, while his two companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, extend it to inside the city, with Muhammad considering it disliked. The commentary also clarifies a secondary issue: what happens if the rider dismounts or mounts during the prayer. Understanding this dispute helps you navigate ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school and apply the correct ruling in different circumstances.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the core dispute
The act is performing voluntary (nafl) prayers on a riding animal when the animal faces a direction other than qibla. The core dispute is whether this is restricted to outside the city (misr) or also permitted inside the city. Note that this ruling applies only to nawafil, not to obligatory prayers.
The matn states: 'إلى غير القبلة' – the essential direction is the animal's heading; facing qibla at the start is recommended, not obligatory.
2
Analyze the proof and the principle of limiting exceptions
The proof is the hadith of Ibn Umar: the Prophet prayed on a donkey heading to Khaybar (outside Medina) making gestures (ima'). Because this action contradicts the general rule that qibla is required (based on Quranic texts), Abu Hanifa limits the exception to the specific context of the hadith – outside the city. This follows the legal principle that exceptions to qiyas are not extended beyond their occasion.
The hadith is reported by Muslim, Abu Dawud, and al-Nasa'i; the gesture (ima') is confirmed in other narrations.
3
Compare the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn
Abu Hanifa: Not allowed inside the city. Abu Yusuf: Allowed inside, no dislike. Muhammad: Allowed inside but disliked (makruh tanzih). Their basis: the hadith does not explicitly restrict to outside, so general permissibility applies; but Muhammad adds karahah due to potential carelessness inside the city.
The 'Sahibayn' refer to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the two main students of Abu Hanifa.
4
Understand the ruling when the rider dismounts or mounts mid-prayer
If one starts the prayer as a rider (using gestures), then dismounts and performs full ruku' and sujud, the prayer is valid because he performs it more completely. If one starts on the ground (obligated to full movements), then mounts, the prayer becomes invalid because the opening takbir obligated bowing and prostration, which cannot be performed by gestures while riding.
The commentary refutes an analogy with a sick person: the rider's gestures are not a substitute due to inability but a permitted reduction; thus dismounting improves the prayer.
5
Apply the mufta bihi position and note the thamarah al-khilaf
The relied-upon position for fatwa is that of the Sahibayn: it is permissible inside the city, with karahah according to Muhammad (or without according to Abu Yusuf). The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf): A Hanafi following Abu Hanifa would not pray nafl on a ride inside the city; following the Sahibayn, he may, but with dislike if opting for Muhammad's view.
Later Hanafi works like 'Halbat al-Mujalli' often adopt the Sahibayn's view.

Source Text
