إلى غير القبلة
إلى غير القبلة)، إنما قال : خارج المصر بقول ابن عمر: «رأيت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يصلي على حمار، وهو متوجه إلى خيبر يومى إيماء»، ولَمَّا كان هذا الفعل مخالفا للقياس اقتصر على مورده.
وعندهما : يجوز ذلك في المصر أيضاً، لكن بكراهة عند محمد الله. كذا في «حلبة المجلي».
[١] قوله : إلى غير القبلة ؛ أي جهة توجهت الدابة، ولا يشترط استقبال القبلة في ابتداء الصلاة، نعم يستحب ذلك عند عدم الحرج، ولو صَلَّى إلى غير ما تَوَجَّهت إليه دابة وإلى غير القبلة لم يجز. كذا في «البحر»، و«الحلبة».
[٢] قوله : لقول ابن عمر ؛ أي عبد الله بن عمر بن الخطاب : رأيت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ...» الحديث، أخرجه مسلم وأبو داود والنسائي، لكن ليس فيه يومئ إيماء، وقد ثبت ذلك من رواية جابر الله عند ابن حبان في صحيحه»، وأنس له عند الدار قطني في كتاب «غرائب مالك».
[٣] قوله : ولما كان ... الخ ؛ حاصله : أنه لَمَّا ثبت أداء النفل إلى غير القبلة من الشارع وهو خلاف الأصول ؛ لكونه مخالفاً لنصوص افتراض استقبال القبلة، اقتصر ذلك على موضع ورد فيه، وهو أداء النفل خارج المصر، ولم يتعدّ هذا الحكم إلى أداء النفل في المصر، وكذا إلى الفرائض.
فلو افتتحه راكباً، ثُمَّ نَزَلَ بنى، وبعكسِهِ فَسَد ؛ لأن في الأول" ما يؤديه أكمل " مما وجب عليه ، وفي الثَّاني انعقدت التحريمةُ موجبة للركوع والسجود، ولا يجوز أداؤه بالإيماء.
[١١] قوله : لأن في الأوّل ؛ أي فيما إذا شرع راكباً ثم نزل.
[١٢] قوله : ما يؤديه أكمل ؛ لأن الواجب عليه عند الشروع هو الإيماء بإحرامه راكباً، فإذا نزل وركع وسجد أداه أكمل فلا بأس به. فإن قلت : يلزم بناء القوي على الضعيف، فلا يجوز كالمريض يصلي بالإيماء ثم يقدر على الركوع والسجود. قلت : الإيماء من المريض بدل من الأركان لا من الراكب ؛ لأنَّ البدل يصار إليه عند العجز والراكب قادر على الأركان بأن يقوم في الركابين، ويركع ويسجد، فمع ذلك لما جوز له الجلوس والإيماء صار ذلك قوياً في نفسه. كذا في «البناية».
Book of Prayer: Prayer of Witr and Nawafil. 'Facing other than the qibla.' (He said:) He only said: outside the city, based on the statement of Ibn Umar: 'I saw the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) praying on a donkey, heading towards Khaybar, making gestures.' And since this act was contrary to analogy, it was limited to its context. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): It is permissible also inside the city, but with dislike according to Muhammad. Likewise in 'Halbat al-Mujalli'. [1] His statement: 'facing other than the qibla' means any direction the animal faces, and it is not a condition to face the qibla at the beginning of the prayer; rather, it is recommended when there is no difficulty. If he prays facing other than the direction the animal faces and other than the qibla, it is not permissible. Likewise in 'al-Bahr' and 'al-Halba'. [2] His statement: 'based on the statement of Ibn Umar' meaning Abdullah ibn Umar ibn al-Khattab: 'I saw the Messenger of Allah ...' the hadith reported by Muslim, Abu Dawud, and al-Nasa'i, but it does not contain 'making gestures'; that is confirmed from the narration of Jabir (may Allah be pleased with him) in Sahih Ibn Hibban, and from Anas (may Allah be pleased with him) in al-Daraqutni's 'Gharai'b Malik'. [3] His statement: 'And since this was contrary to analogy...' The summary: Since the performance of nawafil facing other than the qibla is established from the Lawgiver and is contrary to the principles (because it contradicts texts stipulating facing the qibla), it is limited to the context in which it occurred, i.e., performing nawafil outside the city, and this ruling does not extend to performing nawafil inside the city, nor to obligatory prayers. 'If he begins (prayer) as a rider, then dismounts, he builds upon it; and the reverse invalidates it.' Because in the first case, he performs it in a more complete manner than what was required of him, while in the second case, the opening takbir was concluded obligating bowing and prostration, and it is not permissible to perform it with gestures. [11] His statement: 'because in the first' means when he started as a rider and then dismounted. [12] His statement: 'he performs it in a more complete manner' because what was obligatory upon him at the start was gestures due to his beginning as a rider; so when he dismounts and bows and prostrates, he performs it more completely, so there is no harm. If it is objected: This would mean building the strong upon the weak, which is not allowed, like a sick person who prays with gestures and then is able to bow and prostrate. I say: The gestures of the sick person are a substitute for the pillars, not for the rider; because substitution is resorted to due to inability, whereas the rider is capable of the pillars by standing in the stirrups, bowing, and prostrating. Nevertheless, since sitting and gesturing were permitted for him, that (gesturing) became strong in itself. Likewise in 'al-Binayah'.
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the ruling of performing voluntary (nafl) prayers on a riding animal while facing other than the qibla. The matn states the ruling as restricted to outside the city (misr), which is the view of Imam Abu Hanifa. The proof is the hadith of Ibn Umar where the Prophet (saw) prayed on a donkey facing Khaybar, making gestures (ima'). Since this action contradicts the general obligation of facing the qibla, Abu Hanifa limits it to the specific context of traveling outside the city. His two companions, Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad, however, permit it inside the city as well, though Muhammad considers it disliked (makruh). The commentary further explains that the essential direction is that of the animal's heading; it is recommended but not obligatory to face the qibla at the start. If one prays facing a direction other than the animal's heading and other than the qibla, it is invalid. The passage then addresses a related secondary ruling: if one begins the prayer as a rider, then dismounts, the prayer remains valid (he builds upon the earlier part). Conversely, if one begins on the ground and then mounts, the prayer is invalid because the opening takbir (tahrimah) obligated bowing and prostration, which cannot be fulfilled by gestures while riding. The commentary refutes an objection comparing this to a sick person who substitutes gestures and later recovers, explaining that the rider's gesture is not a substitute but a reduced form that is considered strong in itself due to the permissibility granted.

Key Terms
الإيماء (al-ima'): Gesturing with the head or body for bowing and prostration instead of full movements, permitted for the rider or the sick.
التحريمة (al-tahrimah): The opening takbir (saying Allahu Akbar) that begins the prayer and makes it binding.
الكراهة (al-karahah): Dislike; in Hanafi fiqh, karahah tanzihiyyah means it is better to avoid, but the act is valid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) Outside the city only
D) Not permissible in any location

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of praying nawafil on a ride without qibla is agreed upon outside the city, but there is a valid intra-Hanafi difference regarding inside the city.

Tarawih Prayer: Twenty Rak'ahs, Sunnah Mu'akkadah
Ruling with evidence on Tarawih's number and status

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Tarawih (number and legal status) and explain the evidence from the hadith of the Prophet's fear of obligation.

Core Idea
Tarawih is twenty rak'ahs of confirmed sunnah, not mere recommendation, based on the Prophet's practice.

Tarawih prayer during Ramadan is a distinctive act of worship. The Hanafi school affirms that it is a sunnah mu'akkadah (confirmed sunnah) consisting of twenty rak'ahs. This lesson clarifies the ruling, addresses an internal Hanafi difference, and presents the primary evidence from the Prophet's ﷺ actions and words.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its categories
Read the matn: 'Tarawih is twenty rak'ahs sunnah.' The commentary clarifies that it is sunnah mu'akkadah, not mustahabb. Note the two categories and their implications for reward and blame.
Sunnah mu'akkadah is a higher level than mustahabb.
2
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The text mentions two narrations from Abu Hanifa: one says mustahabb, the other says sunnah. His companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) adopted the sunnah view, and this is the relied-upon position.
The weaker narration is not given weight.
3
Cite the dalil (proof)
The commentary cites the hadith: 'Nothing prevented me from coming out... except that I feared it would be prescribed upon you.' This shows the Prophet led Tarawih on three nights and then stopped.
The hadith is narrated by multiple sources.
4
Explain the wajh al-dalalah (how it proves the ruling)
The Prophet's action of leading and then stopping only out of fear of obligation indicates that the act is highly recommended (sunnah mu'akkadah) but not obligatory. If it were merely mustahabb, he would not have feared obligation.
The fear of fard shows the strong emphasis.
5
State the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
The relied-upon Hanafi position: Tarawih is twenty rak'ahs, sunnah mu'akkadah, performed in congregation. Omission without excuse is makruh tanzih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سن التراويح عشرون ركعة
[٣] قوله : سنّ التراويح ... الخ ؛ اعلم أنه اختلف في أنّ التراويح سنة مؤكدة أو مستحب، فروي عن أبي حنيفة الاستحباب ، وروى عنه الاستنان، وهو الصحيح المختار عند أصحابه، ولا عبرة بمخالفته، وكذا أداؤه بالجماعة سنة مؤكدة، وكذا عدده ؛ أي عشرون ركعة. أما استنان الأوليين فقد ثبت من المواظبة النبوية الحكمية ؛ لما ثبت أنه قام بهم في ثلاث ليال من رمضان في الليلة الثالثة والعشرين، ثم في الخامسة والعشرين، ثمّ في السابعة والعشرين، وترك بعد ذلك، وقال: «لم يمنعني من الخروج إليكم إلا أني خشيت أن تفرض عليكم ) ، أخرجه أبو داود ومسلم والنسائي والترمذي وغيرهم، فدل ذلك على أنه لولا خوف الافتراض لدام بهم على ذلك.
Tarawih is twenty rak'ahs. [3] His statement: 'Tarawih is sunnah...' etc.; know that there is difference of opinion whether Tarawih is sunnah mu'akkadah or mustahabb. It is narrated from Abu Hanifa that it is mustahabb, and it is narrated from him that it is sunnah, and that is the correct and chosen view of his companions, and no attention is paid to his opposition. Likewise, performing it in congregation is sunnah mu'akkadah, and likewise its number, i.e., twenty rak'ahs. As for the first two (rak'ahs) being sunnah, it is established by the Prophetic continuous practice in principle; because it is established that he performed it with them on three nights of Ramadan: the twenty-third night, then the twenty-fifth, then the twenty-seventh, and then he stopped and said: 'Nothing prevented me from coming out to you except that I feared it would be prescribed upon you.' This was reported by Abu Dawud, Muslim, al-Nasa'i, al-Tirmidhi, and others. So this indicates that were it not for the fear of obligation, he would have continued with them.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage establishes the ruling of Tarawih prayer during Ramadan. The matn declares that Tarawih is twenty rak'ahs and sunnah. The commentary clarifies that there is an internal Hanafi difference: some narrations from Abu Hanifa consider it mustahabb, while the stronger and chosen view (as per his companions) is that it is sunnah mu'akkadah (a confirmed sunnah). This is the adopted position. The congregation for Tarawih is also sunnah mu'akkadah, and the number is firmly twenty rak'ahs. The proof is the Prophet's (saw) action: he led the companions in Tarawih on three nights (the 23rd, 25th, and 27th of Ramadan) but then stopped because he feared it might become obligatory upon them. This demonstrates that it is a highly recommended sunnah, not obligatory. The hadith is cited from multiple sources.

Key Terms
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah mu'akkadah): A confirmed sunnah; an act the Prophet consistently performed and encouraged, but not obligatory. Omission is disliked.
مستحب (mustahabb): Recommended but not emphasized; performing it is rewarded but omitting it is not disliked.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

intermediate

Starting Prayer as a Rider: Dismounting During Prayer
Ruling and rationale for validity of dismounting after starting prayer as a rider

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on dismounting after starting prayer as a rider, distinguish it from the reverse case, and explain the rationale using the distinction between a substitute (badal) and original performance.

Core Idea
Starting prayer as a rider and dismounting is valid because you improve, not weaken, your performance.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in prayer: a person begins an obligatory prayer while riding, due to necessity, and then dismounts during the prayer. The Hanafi school rules that this is valid, while the opposite case (starting on ground and mounting) is invalid. The reasoning involves a comparison with a sick person who recovers during prayer. Understanding this ruling clarifies the importance of performing acts of worship in the most complete manner possible and the nature of concessions (rukhas) in prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios and their rulings
Read the passage and extract the two opposite cases: (1) starting as a rider then dismounting – valid; (2) starting on ground then mounting – invalid. Note the key terms 'yabni' (builds) and 'fasid' (invalid).
The ruling is clear: the first is permissible, the second is not.
2
Understand the rationale (ta'lil) for the first case
The passage explains: because the rider performed what is more complete (akmal) than what was obligatory. Upon starting, the rider was permitted to use gesture (ima). Dismounting and performing actual ruku and sujud is an enhancement, not a violation.
The obligation at the start was gesture; actual pillars are superior.
3
Analyze the objection and response
The commentator raises an objection via qiyas: if a sick person starts with gesture then recovers, continuing with actual pillars is invalid (building strong on weak). Why isn't the rider case similar? The response distinguishes: the sick person's gesture is a substitute (badal) for the actual pillars, so his foundation is weak. The rider's gesture is not a substitute; he is capable of actual pillars but permitted to sit and gesture, so his foundation is strong.
Key distinction: substitute vs. original permission.
4
Derive the underlying principle
The underlying principle is that an act performed by concession (rukhsa) can later be upgraded to a more complete act without invalidating the prayer, because the foundation is not defective. However, one cannot downgrade from a complete act to a concession.
This principle applies in other areas of fiqh as well.
5
Apply the ruling to practical scenarios
Consider variations: if a rider starts prayer by gesture due to travel, then returns home and dismounts, the prayer is valid. If a person on the ground mounts a moving animal, the prayer is invalid because the opening takbir obligated actual pillars.
Always check the starting state and the direction of change.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلو افتتحه راكباً، ثُمَّ نَزَلَ بنى، ويعكسه فَسَد (فلو افتتحه راكباً، ثُمَّ نَزَلَ ،بنى، وبعكسِهِ فَسَد ؛ لأن في الأول " ما يؤديه أكمل " مما وجب عليه ، وفي الثَّاني انعقدت التحريمةُ موجبة للركوع والسجود، ولا يجوز أداؤه بالإيماء. قوله : لأن في الأوّل؛ أي فيما إذا شرع راكباً ثم نزل. (۲) قوله : ما يؤديه أكمل؛ لأن الواجب عليه عند الشروع هو الإيماء بإحرامه راكباً، فإذا نزل وركع وسجد أداه أكمل فلا بأس به. فإن قلت : يلزم بناء القوي على الضعيف، فلا يجوز كالمريض يصلي بالإيماء ثم يقدر على الركوع والسجود. قلت : الإيماء من المريض بدل من الأركان لا من الراكب؛ لأنَّ البدل يصار إليه عند العجز والراكب قادر على الأركان بأن يقوم في الركابين، ويركع ويسجد، فمع ذلك لما جوز له الجلوس والإيماء صار ذلك قوياً في نفسه. كذا في «البناية».
If he begins it [prayer] while riding, then he dismounts, he builds [upon what he has performed], and the opposite of it is invalid; because in the first case, he performs what is more complete than what was obligatory upon him, and in the second case, the tahrimah [opening takbir] was concluded obligating ruku and sujud, and it is not permissible to perform it by gesture. He said: 'because in the first' i.e., in the case when he started as a rider then dismounted. (2) He said: 'what he performs is more complete' because the obligation upon him at the start was gesture by his ihram as a rider, so when he dismounts and performs ruku and sujud, he performs it more completely, so there is no harm. If you say: this leads to building the strong on the weak, so it is not permissible, like a sick person who prays by gesture then becomes able to perform ruku and sujud. I say: The gesture of the sick person is a substitute for the pillars, not of the rider; because the substitute is resorted to in inability, and the rider is capable of the pillars by standing in the stirrups and performing ruku and sujud; nevertheless, when sitting and gesture were permitted for him, that became strong in itself. Thus in al-Binaya.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling and its justification from the commentary of al-Wiqayah. The ruling states that if a person begins an obligatory prayer while riding (a permissible situation due to necessity), and then dismounts during the prayer, the prayer is valid and he may continue building upon what he has already performed. Conversely, if he begins the prayer on the ground and then mounts an animal, the prayer becomes invalid. The reason: in the first case, the person's initial actions by gesture were acceptable given his state, and by dismounting he is able to perform the actual pillars (ruku and sujud) more completely, which is an improvement, not a defect. In the second case, the opening takbir (tahrimah) was contracted in a state that obligated him to perform actual ruku and sujud (since he was on the ground), so performing the rest by gesture is not permissible, as the prayer would be incomplete. The commentator addresses an objection via qiyas: It might be argued that this ruling resembles a sick person who starts praying by gesture and then recovers during prayer; in that case, the prayer is invalid because one would be building a strong subsequent part on a weak foundation. The answer distinguishes the two: the sick person's gesture is a substitute (badal) for the actual pillars, so when he can perform the actual pillars, his foundation was weak. However, the rider's gesture is not a substitute; he is actually capable of performing the pillars (by standing in the stirrups, etc.) but is permitted to use gesture due to his situation. Thus his initial performance is not weak, and dismounting to perform the actual pillars is valid.

Key Terms
التحريمة (al-tahrimah): The opening takbir that makes prayer begin and prohibits worldly actions
الإيماء (al-ima): Gestures of head or body for ruku and sujud when unable to perform actual bowing and prostration
بدل (badal): Substitute; in this context, the gesture of a sick person is a substitute for the actual pillars, whereas the rider's gesture is not a substitute but a permitted alternative.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a person starts his obligatory prayer as a rider and then dismounts during the prayer?
A) The prayer is invalid because he built strong on weak.
B) The prayer is valid because he performs the obligatory acts more completely.
C) It depends on whether he intended to dismount at the start.
D) The prayer becomes nafl.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, upgrading from a permissible concession to a more complete performance during prayer is valid, provided the initial foundation was strong (i.e., not a substitute for inability).

The Sunnah of Taraweeh Being Twenty Rak'ahs
Establishing taraweeh as sunnah mu'akkadah of twenty rak'ahs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on taraweeh (twenty rak'ahs, sunnah mu'akkadah) and explain the evidence from the Prophet's practice and the Caliphs' consensus.

Core Idea
Taraweeh is twenty rak'ahs sunnah mu'akkadah, established by the Caliphs' practice and the Prophet's precedent.

The Hanafi school holds that taraweeh prayer in Ramadan is an emphasized sunnah of twenty rak'ahs. This lesson explores the textual evidence from the Prophet's own practice and the consensus of the Rightly Guided Caliphs, and clarifies an intra-madhhab difference regarding its status.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling and its level
Identify the act (taraweeh) and its ruling level (sunnah mu'akkadah). Note that the matn explicitly states 'the sunnah of taraweeh is twenty rak'ahs.'
2
Examine the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Understand that within the school there are two narrations from Abu Hanifa: istihbab and istinan. The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is istinan (sunnah mu'akkadah).
3
Trace the dalil for the sunnah nature
The Prophet prayed with companions on three nights and then stopped out of fear of obligation. This indicates the act is desirable but not obligatory – hence sunnah.
4
Trace the dalil for the number
The Caliphs Umar, Uthman, and Ali consistently prayed twenty rak'ahs. The hadith 'Adhere to my sunnah and the sunnah of the Rightly Guided Caliphs' makes their practice a source of sunnah.
5
Apply the ruling practically
The mufta bihi ruling: taraweeh is twenty rak'ahs, performed in congregation, and its omission is disliked but not sinful.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(1) فعن عائشة : إن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم صلى في المسجد ذات ليلة فصلى بصلاته ناس، ثم صلى من القابلة فكثر الناس، ثم اجتمعوا من الليلة الثالثة، أو الرابعة فلم يخرج إليهم رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم، فلما أصبح قال : قد رأيت الذي صنعتُم فلم يمنعني من الخروج إليكم إلا أني خشيت أن تفرض عليكم»، في صحيح البخاري (1) : (313) , و(صحیح مسلم» (1 : 524)، وغيرهما. وأما العدد فروى ابن حبّان وغيره أنه صلى بهم في تلك الليالي ثمان ركعات ، وثلاث ركعات وتراً)، نعم ثبت اهتمام الصحابة على عشرين في عهد عمر وعثمان وعلي (3) فمن بعدهم ) ، أخرجه مالك وابن سعد والبيهقي وغيرهم، وما واظبت عليه الخلفاء فعلاً أو تشريعاً أيضاً سنة (0) ; لحديث: «عليكم بسنتي وسنة الخلفاء الراشدين، أخرجه أبو داود وغيره. (2) فعن جابر بن عبد الله الله قال : صلى بنا رسول الله الله في شهر رمضان ثمان ركعات وأوتر فلما كانت الليلة القابلة اجتمعنا في المسجد ورجونا أن يخرج فيصلي بنا فأقمنا فيه حتى أصبحنا فقلنا : يا رسول الله رجونا أن تخرج فتصلي بنا قال : إني كرهت - أو خشيت - أن يكتب عليكم الوتر» في (صحيح ابن حبان (6) : (173) , وضعفه شيخنا الأرنؤوط. (3) فعن يحيى بن سعيد الله : أن عمر بن الخطاب له أمر رجلا يصلي بهم عشرين ركعة في مصنف ابن أبي شيبة (2) : (136) , ورجاله ثقات إلا أن يحيى لم يدرك عمر . ينظر : «إعلاء السنن: 75)، وغيرها. The sunnah of taraweeh is twenty rak'ahs. (3) His statement: 'the sunnah of taraweeh ... etc.' Know that there is a difference of opinion whether taraweeh is a strongly recommended sunnah or a mustahabb. It is narrated from Abu Hanifa that it is mustahabb, and it is narrated from him that it is sunnah, and this is the correct and chosen view of his companions, and no attention is paid to opposition. Likewise, its performance in congregation is a strongly recommended sunnah, and likewise its number, i.e., twenty rak'ahs. As for the sunnah of the first two [rak'ahs], it is established by the prophetic continuous practice in meaning; because it is established that he [the Prophet] prayed with them on three nights of Ramadan – on the twenty-third night, then on the twenty-fifth, then on the twenty-seventh – and he left it after that, and said: 'Nothing prevented me from coming out to you except that I feared it would be made obligatory upon you.' This was narrated by Abu Dawud, Muslim, al-Nasa'i, al-Tirmidhi, and others, indicating that if not for the fear of obligation, he would have continued with them. (1) From Aisha: ... And as for the number, Ibn Hibban and others narrated that he prayed with them on those nights eight rak'ahs and three rak'ahs of witr... Indeed, the concern of the Companions for twenty [rak'ahs] is established during the time of Umar, Uthman, and Ali, and those after them, narrated by Malik, Ibn Sa'd, al-Bayhaqi, and others. And what the caliphs persisted in, whether by action or as legislation, is also sunnah, due to the hadith: 'Adhere to my sunnah and the sunnah of the Rightly Guided Caliphs,' narrated by Abu Dawud and others. (2) From Jabir... (3) From Yahya ibn Sa'id... (4) From Ibn Abi al-Hasna'... (5) From Ibn Umar... (6) This issue is neglected by many, despite the agreement of Hanafi usul scholars upon it... (7) In Sahih Ibn Hibban... (8) Tuhfat al-Akhyar...
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on al-Wiqayah establishes the Hanafi ruling on taraweeh prayer. It begins by stating the matn: 'The sunnah of taraweeh is twenty rak'ahs.' The sharh then clarifies that within the Hanafi school there is a difference of opinion regarding the level of recommendation: some narrations from Abu Hanifa consider taraweeh mustahabb (recommended), but the relied-upon position of his disciples (and the mufta bihi) is that it is a sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah). Moreover, performing it in congregation is also a sunnah mu'akkadah. The proof for its legitimacy is drawn from the Prophet's own practice: he prayed taraweeh with the Companions on three nights in Ramadan but stopped out of fear that it would become obligatory. This shows that the action itself was desirable and that if not for that fear, it would have continued. As for the specific number of twenty rak'ahs, the evidence comes from the consistent practice of the Rightly Guided Caliphs – Umar, Uthman, Ali, and those after them – who instituted twenty rak'ahs. The passage argues that such practice is considered sunnah because of the hadith 'Adhere to my sunnah and the sunnah of the Rightly Guided Caliphs.' Juristic principle: The practice of the caliphs, especially when they acted with consensus or as official legislation, is a source of sunnah in the Hanafi school. The passage also includes multiple narrations to support both the Prophet's eight-rak'ah precedent and the Companions' twenty-rak'ah practice, resolving the apparent discrepancy by noting that the Prophet's eight rak'ahs were done in the early stage, while the later consensus of the Companions on twenty rak'ahs became the established norm.

Key Terms
التراويح (al-tarawih): The night prayer performed in Ramadan after the 'isha prayer, consisting of twenty rak'ahs in the Hanafi school
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah mu'akkadah): A recommended act that the Prophet performed consistently and encouraged; omission is disliked but not sinful
الاستنان (al-istinan): The view that taraweeh is sunnah (as opposed to mustahabb), derived from the narrator's preference

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) It is not fixed; it varies by region.

Key Takeaway
Taraweeh is a sunnah mu'akkadah of twenty rak'ahs, established by the Caliphs' consensus with the Prophet's implicit approval.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Tarawih Prayer: Ruling, Time, and Number of Rak'ahs
States the ruling, proof, structure, and time of Tarawih prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of Tarawih prayer in the Hanafi school, identify its time, number of rak'ahs, and explain the proof from the practice of the Companions.

Core Idea
Tarawih is sunnah, not fard, because the Prophet ceased it out of fear of obligation; the Companions continued it.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah clarifies the legal status of Tarawih prayer. It affirms that Tarawih is a sunnah prayer established by the practice of the rightly-guided caliphs. The text also details the number of rak'ahs (20 in 5 tarwihas), the recommended time, and the flexibility in recitation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that Tarawih is sunnah (سنة). Identify what act is being ruled upon: the night prayer in Ramadan performed in congregation after Isha.
The ruling is sunnah muakkadah (confirmed sunnah), not fard or wajib.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is twofold: the continuous practice of the khulafa al-rashidun (rightly-guided caliphs) and the Prophet's explanation for not continuing it himself—fear of it becoming obligatory.
The dalil is the Sunnah (practice of the Companions) and the Prophet's tacit approval.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Companions' adherence shows the act is recommended; the Prophet's excuse (fear of obligation) shows it is not fard. Together they establish sunnah status.
If it were fard, the Prophet would not have left it; his leaving with a valid reason proves it is not obligatory.
4
Note the number and structure
Tarawih consists of five tarwihas (ترويحات), each tarwiha being four rak'ahs, totalling 20 rak'ahs. Each tarwiha ends with two taslims and a sitting of similar duration.
The term 'tarwiha' literally means 'rest' because a break is taken after each set.
5
Analyze the ikhtilaf on time
Three views are mentioned: (1) after Isha before and after witr (preferred by most Hanafi authorities), (2) only between Isha and witr, (3) the entire night. The first is considered the most correct.
The practical implication: if one misses some Tarawih, he can pray after witr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بعد العشاء قبل الوتر وبعده خمس ترويحات، لكل ترويحة تسليمتان وجلسة بعدهما قدر ترويحة، والسنة فيها الختم مرة واحدة، ولا يترك لكسل القوم، ولا يوتر بجماعة خارج رمضان. وإنما كانت التراويح سنة؛ لأنه واظب عليها الخلفاء الراشدون، والنبي بين العذر في ترك المواظبة، وهو مخافة أن تكتب علينا. قوله: وبعده؛ أي الوتر، فلو فاته بعضها وقام الإمام إلى الوتر أوتر معه، ثم صلى ما فاته. قوله: ترويحات؛ الترويحة: اسم لكل أربع ركعات؛ لأنه تحصل الراحة بعدها، وهم مخيرون في الجلسة بعدها بين الذكر والصلاة والسكوت. قوله: قدر ترويحة؛ هذا مستحب إن لم يطول القراءة فيها، ولم يثقل على القوم ذلك. اختلفوا في وقتها: الأول: بعد العشاء قبل الوتر وبعده، وهو اختيار المصنف، وصاحب الكنز، والملتقى، والمراقي، وظاهر اختيار ملا مسكين في شرح الكنز، وصححه صاحب الاختيار، وقال صاحب الدر المختار: هو الأصح. الثاني: ما بين العشاء والوتر، وصححه في الخلاصة، ورجحه في غاية البيان بأنه المأثور المتوارث. الثالث: أن وقتها الليل كله قبل العشاء وبعده، وقبل الوتر وبعده؛ لأنها قيام الليل، قال صاحب البحر: لم أر من صححه. لكن الاختيار الأفضل في زماننا قدر ما لا يثقل على الناس، وقد أفتى أبو الفضل الكرماني والوبري أنه إذا قرأ في التراويح الفاتحة وآية أو آيتين لا يكره، ومن لم يكن عالما بأهل زمانه، فهو جاهل.
After Isha, before Witr and after it, five tarwihas. For each tarwiha, two taslims and a sitting after them the duration of a tarwiha. The sunnah in it is to complete (the Quran) once. It should not be left due to the laziness of the people. And one should not pray witr in congregation outside Ramadan. And indeed tarawih is sunnah because the rightly-guided caliphs adhered to it, and the Prophet explained the excuse for not adhering continuously, which is the fear that it would be prescribed upon us. His statement: 'and after it' means after Witr. So if one misses some of it and the Imam stands for Witr, he should pray Witr with him, then pray what he missed. His statement: 'tarwihas' - tarwiha is a name for every four rak'ahs, because rest is obtained after them. They have a choice in the sitting after it between remembrance, prayer, and silence. His statement: 'the duration of a tarwiha' - this is recommended provided the recitation is not lengthened in it and it is not burdensome for the congregation. They differed concerning its time: The first: after Isha before Witr and after it, and this is the choice of the author, the author of al-Kanz, al-Multaqa, al-Maraqi, the apparent choice of Mulla Miskeen in Sharh al-Kanz, and the author of al-Ikhtiyar authenticated it, and the author of al-Durr al-Mukhtar said: it is the most correct. The second: between Isha and Witr, authenticated in al-Khulasa and preferred in Ghayat al-Bayan because it is the transmitted practice. The third: its time is the entire night before Isha and after it, before Witr and after it, because it is night prayer. The author of al-Bahr said: I have not seen anyone authenticate it. But the best choice in our time is an amount that does not burden the people. Abu al-Fadl al-Kirmani and al-Wabari gave fatwa that if one recites in tarawih al-Fatiha and one or two verses, it is not disliked, and whoever is not knowledgeable of the people of his time is ignorant.
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage begins by stating the ruling on Tarawih prayer. In the Hanafi school, Tarawih is a sunnah prayer performed in Ramadan. Its recommended time is after Isha prayer, and it extends before Witr and even after Witr for those who missed some. The number is five tarwihas, each tarwiha being four rak'ahs, so total twenty rak'ahs. Each tarwiha ends with two taslims, meaning two separate units of two rak'ahs each. After each tarwiha there is a sitting of similar duration. The sunnah is to complete the entire Quran once during the month. It should not be abandoned due to laziness; the imam should not skip it. Witr is not prayed in congregation outside Ramadan, implying that during Ramadan it is sunnah to pray witr in congregation after tarawih. Then the passage gives the reason Tarawih is sunnah: the khulafa al-rashidun continuously observed it, and the Prophet did not continue out of fear that it would become obligatory. The commentator explains key phrases: 'after it' means after witr; if one misses some tarawih, he can catch up after witr. 'Tarwiha' is defined as a set of four rak'ahs because it is followed by a rest. The sitting after it can be spent in dhikr, salah, or silence. The recommended duration of the sitting is the time of a tarwiha itself, but this is conditional on not prolonging recitation unduly. Then a discussion of the time of tarawih: three views are mentioned: (1) after Isha before and after witr (the preferred view of the author and most Hanafi authorities), (2) only between Isha and witr, (3) the whole night. The first is deemed the most correct. Practically, the duration should be adjusted to avoid burdening the congregation. The fatwa of later scholars allows reciting only al-Fatiha and a couple of verses per rak'ah if needed.

Key Terms
ترويحة (tarwiha): A set of four rak'ahs in Tarawih prayer, after which a rest is taken.
الوتر (al-witr): The odd-numbered prayer performed after Isha, which in Ramadan is prayed in congregation after Tarawih.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the hukm (ruling) of Tarawih prayer according to the Hanafi school?
A) Fard
B) Wajib
C) Sunnah
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Tarawih is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah muakkadah) consisting of 20 rak'ahs, its time extends from after Isha to after Witr, and it should not be abandoned.

Salah — Prayer

Salat al-Kusuf: Ruling and Conditions
States ruling of eclipse prayer as sunnah in congregation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of Salat al-Kusuf, identify its conditions, and explain why it is performed without adhan/iqamah.

Core Idea
Eclipse prayer is a sunnah congregation without adhan, led by the Jumu'ah imam, based on the Prophet's practice.

Eclipses are awe-inspiring natural events. The Prophet ﷺ established a special prayer during solar (and lunar) eclipses. This passage from the Hanafi text clarifies its ruling, conditions, and how it is called. Unlike the five daily prayers, the eclipse prayer is sunnah, prayed in congregation, but without the usual adhan and iqamah — instead, a simple call 'as-salatu jamiah' is used.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that at the time of a solar eclipse, the imam of Jumu'ah leads the people in two rak'ahs like nafl. Identify that the act is Salat al-Kusuf and its ruling is sunnah (not wajib).
The ruling is based on the Prophet's practice, not a Quranic command.
2
Note the conditions for validity
List the conditions mentioned: the prayer must be performed in a non-makruh time, led by the imam authorized for Jumu'ah and Eid (to avoid fitna from multiple congregations), and it is prayed in congregation (jama'ah).
The condition of the imam being the Jumu'ah imam is specific to the Hanafi school.
3
Understand the number of rak'ahs
The minimum is two rak'ahs. However, more may be added: either two rak'ahs with a taslim or four rak'ahs with one taslim. The passage clarifies this is the minimum.
Unlike regular nafl, the eclipse prayer is not limited to two rak'ahs.
4
Understand the call to prayer
Adhan and iqamah are not recited. Instead, the caller says 'as-salatu jamiah' (prayer is gathering). This is based on a hadith in Muslim.
This distinguishes the eclipse prayer from the five daily prayers.
5
Identify the proof (dalil)
The hadith reported by Muslim that the Prophet ﷺ prayed the eclipse prayer and called 'as-salatu jamiah' is the proof. This is a sunnah ahad hadith, zanni in transmission but qati' in meaning.
The Hanafi school accepts ahad hadith for establishing sunnah actions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل عند الكسوف يصلي إمام الجمعة بالناس ركعتين كالنفل أي على هيئة النافلة بلا أذان وإقامة. قوله: فصل... الخ؛ لما كانت مسائل صلاة الكسوف والاستسقاء ممتازة عما سبق صدر بيانها بعنوان الفصل. قوله: عند الكسوف؛ يقال: كسفت الشمس والقمر كسفاً، وخسفت الشمس والقمر خسفاً، وهما مصدران متعديان، والكسوف والخسوف لازمان والأفصح تخصيص الكسوف بالشمس والخسوف بالقمر، وهو الجاري على ألسنة الفقهاء. كذا في البناية. قوله: يصلي؛ أي إن كان الوقت غير مكروه؛ لأن صلاة الكسوف نافلة، فلا تؤدى في أوقات الكراهة. كذا في الجوهرة النيرة. قوله: إمام الجمعة؛ أي المأذون له بإقامة الجمعة والعيدين؛ لأن اجتماع الناس ربما أورث فتنة، فلا يصلون في مساجدهم، بل يصلون جماعة واحدة. كذا قال العيني في البناية. قوله: ركعتين؛ هذا بيان للأقل؛ فإن شاءوا صلوا أربعاً، وإن شاءوا أكثر، كل ركعتين بتسليمة، أو كل أربع. قوله: بلا أذان وإقامة؛ ولو نادى بـ: الصلاة جامعة، لاجتماع الناس لا بأس به، ثبت ذلك في العهد النبوي، أخرجه مسلم.
Section: At the time of solar eclipse, the imam of Jumu'ah prays with the people two rak'ahs like nafl, i.e., in the manner of supererogatory prayer, without adhan or iqamah. His statement: 'Section...' - since the issues of eclipse prayer and rain-seeking prayer are distinct from what preceded, their explanation is introduced with a section heading. His statement: 'at the eclipse' - it is said: the sun and moon eclipse (kasafat) with kasf, and the sun and moon eclipse (khasafat) with khasf, both are transitive verbs, but kasuf and khusuf are intransitive, and the most eloquent is to specify kasuf for the sun and khusuf for the moon, and this is what is current among jurists. Thus in al-Binaya. His statement: 'he prays' - i.e., provided the time is not disliked, because eclipse prayer is nafl, so it is not performed during disliked times. Thus in al-Jawhara al-Nayyira. His statement: 'imam of Jumu'ah' - i.e., the one authorized to lead Jumu'ah and the two Eid prayers, because the gathering of people might lead to fitna, so they do not pray in their own mosques, but rather pray as one congregation. Thus al-Ayni said in al-Binaya. His statement: 'two rak'ahs' - this is a statement of the minimum; if they wish, they may pray four, or more, each two rak'ahs with a taslim, or each four. His statement: 'without adhan and iqamah' - even if he calls out 'as-salatu jamiah' to gather the people, there is no harm in it; this is established in the prophetic era, recorded by Muslim.
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This section introduces the rulings on Salat al-Kusuf (solar eclipse prayer). The Hanafi school holds that eclipse prayer is sunnah, not wajib. It is performed in congregation, led by the imam who leads Jumu'ah, to avoid fitna. The prayer consists of two rak'ahs, but can be increased to four or more, each two rak'ahs with a taslim or each four rak'ahs. It is prayed in the manner of nafl, meaning without adhan or iqamah. However, if the caller announces 'as-salatu jamiah' to gather people, it is permissible as established from the time of the Prophet (Muslim). The commentator then explains key terms: 'at the eclipse' - the technical distinction between kasuf (for sun) and khusuf (for moon). The prayer is performed only when the time is not makruh, since it is nafl. The imam prayed in congregation, but only the imam of Jumu'ah leads it, not any imam, to prevent multiple congregations. The minimum rak'ahs is two, but more can be added.

Key Terms
الكسوف (al-kusuf): An eclipse of the sun.
النافلة (al-nafl): Supererogatory prayer, recommended but not obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How is the eclipse prayer called to the congregation?
A) With adhan and iqamah
B) With 'as-salatu jamiah'
C) With a special call like 'Allahu Akbar' repeated
D) With a loud cry without specific words

Key Takeaway
The eclipse prayer is a sunnah congregation without adhan, called by 'as-salatu jamiah', led by the Jumu'ah imam, with a minimum of two rak'ahs, based on the Prophet's practice.

Salah — Prayer

Salat al-Kusuf: Ruling and the Ruku Dispute
States the Hanafi ruling on eclipse prayer and the dispute on the number of rukus per rak'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on salat al-kusuf, identify the point of dispute with the Shafi'i school, and evaluate the Hanafi response to the conflicting hadith reports.

Core Idea
The eclipse prayer is a sunnah two-rak'ah prayer with one ruku per rak'ah; conflicting reports are resolved by interpreting extra rukus as observational confusion.

Salat al-kusuf (eclipse prayer) is a sunnah prayer performed when a solar eclipse occurs. The Hanafi school outlines specific rules: it is led by the Friday Imam, prayed in congregation without adhan, and consists of two rak'ahs like supererogatory prayers. However, a well-known dispute arises between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the number of rukus in each rak'ah. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi position, the opposing view, and the reasoning behind the school's reliance on the one-ruku narration.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the basic ruling of the eclipse prayer: it is a sunnah prayer performed in two rak'ahs, led by the Friday Imam, without adhan or iqamah. The minimum is two rak'ahs, but more may be added. The key detail: each rak'ah contains only one ruku.
The phrase 'كالنفل' (like supererogatory) indicates it is sunnah, not fard.
2
Identify the opposing school and their view
The Shafi'i school holds that each rak'ah of the eclipse prayer contains two rukus. This is based on multiple narrations from companions like Aisha (radiyallahu anha) in Sahih Muslim.
The Shafi'i view is considered stronger in transmission by many muhaddithun.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the Shafi'i evidence: the hadith of Aisha describes the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wasallam) praying four rukus in two rak'ahs (i.e., two rukus per rak'ah). These narrations are found in the major hadith collections.
The number of companions narrating the two-ruku version is larger, giving it apparent strength.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school argues that the two-ruku narrations arose from confusion. The event happened only once in Madinah, and observers at the back (like Aisha and Ibn Abbas) may have mistaken the Prophet raising his head to check the sun for an extra ruku. The one-ruku practice is confirmed by the narration of Ibn Samurah and the practice of Ibn al-Zubayr.
The principle here is that contradictory reports on a single event cannot all be literally true; one must be given priority through interpretation (ta'wil).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis perform one ruku per rak'ah, while Shafi'is perform two rukus per rak'ah. The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is the one-ruku position.
The tarjih within the Hanafi school relies on the correctness of the interpretive argument, not on the number of narrators.

وعن قبيصة الهلالي ، قال : كسفت الشمس على عهد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فخرج فزعاً يجر ثوبه وأنا معه يومئذ بالمدينة، فصلى ركعتين فأطال فيهما القيام، ثم انصرف وانجلت ، فقال : إنما هذه الآيات يخوف الله بها ، فإذا رأيتموها يعني فصلوا كأحدث صلاة صليتموها من المكتوبة» في «المستدرك» (۱) : ٤٨٢)، وصححه، وسنن البيهقي الكبير»(۳: ۳۳۲)، و«سنن أبي داود (۱) (۳۰۸) ، و (سنن النسائي الكبرى (١) : (٥٧٦) ، و(المجتبى»(٣: ١٤١)، و«شرح معاني الآثار (۱) (۳۳۱) ، و(مسند أحمد»(٥ : ٦٠)، وغيرها. (۳) على أصول المذهب ليس أقوى ثبوتاً وإنما الأقوى هو الركوع الواحد لأن ما روي أنه صلى في كل ركعة ركوعين فهو من باب الاشتباه الذي يقع لمن كان في آخر الصفوف فعائشة رضي الله عنها في صف النساء وابن عباس في صف الصبيان، والذي يدلك على صحة هذا التأويل أنه لا لو لم يفعل ذلك بالمدينة إلا مرة فيستحيل أن يكون الكل ثابتاً، فعلم بذلك أن الاختلاف من الرواة للاشتباه عليهم ، وقيل : إنه لو كان يرفع رأسه ليختبر حال الشمس هل انجلت أم لا ؟ فظنه بعضهم ركوعاً فأطلق عليه اسمه فلا يعارض ما سبق مع هذه الاحتمالات
Section: During the eclipse, the Friday Imam prays with the people two rak'ahs like supererogatory prayer. (That is, in the manner of supererogatory prayer without adhan and iqamah.) [Commentary:] ... The Imam of Friday means the one authorized for Friday and Eid prayers, because gathering of people might cause fitna; they should not pray in their mosques but instead pray as one congregation. ... The statement 'two rak'ahs' indicates the minimum; if they wish they may pray four, or more, each two rak'ahs with a taslimah, or every four. ... Without adhan and iqamah; but if he calls out 'al-salatu jamiah' for gathering the people, there is no harm; that is established from the prophetic era, narrated by Muslim. ... According to us, in every rak'ah there is one bowing, but according to al-Shafi'i, two bowings. ... The one bowing is like other two-rak'ah prayers, it is reported from the action of Ibn al-Zubayr, mentioned by al-Bukhari in his Sahih, and it is confirmed from the prophetic action in the narration of Ibn Samurah, reported by Abu Dawood, Ibn Majah, al-Nasai, al-Tirmidhi and others. ... Two bowings is stronger in transmission from the Prophet via narrations from a group of companions, reported by the authors of the Sahihs and others that he lengthened the recitation, then bowed, then stood and recited less than the first recitation, then bowed again, doing so in each rak'ah. ... The research on this topic is lengthy, its place is in the extensive books. ... According to the principles of the madhhab, it is not stronger in transmission; rather the stronger is one bowing, because what is reported that he prayed with two bowings in each rak'ah is based on confusion among those at the back rows; Aisha was in the women's row and Ibn Abbas in the children's row; what proves the correctness of this interpretation is that he did not do this in Madinah except once, so it is impossible for all to be established; thus the difference is from the narrators' confusion. It is also said that if he raised his head to check the condition of the sun whether it had cleared, some thought it was a bowing and called it by that name, so it does not contradict what preceded given these possibilities.
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the number of rukus in the eclipse prayer (salat al-kusuf). The matn states the basic ruling: the Imam (the Friday Imam) leads the people in two rak'ahs like supererogatory prayer, without adhan or iqamah, though calling 'al-salatu jamiah' is permissible. The commentator expands on each part, noting that it is a sunnah prayer (confirmed by a footnote) and that it is not performed during prohibited times. The minimum is two rak'ahs, but more may be added in units of two or four with a single taslimah. The key dispute arises in the later part: the Hanafi school (indicated by 'عندنا') holds that each rak'ah contains only one ruku, like other prayers. In contrast, Imam al-Shafi'i holds that each rak'ah contains two rukus. The commentator provides evidence for the Hanafi position from the practice of Ibn al-Zubayr and the prophetic narration of Ibn Samurah. For the Shafi'i position, narrations from multiple companions support two rukus. The Hanafi response is a tahrif (interpretation) that the narrations of two rukus stem from confusion among observers who mistook the Prophet raising his head to check the sun's status for an extra ruku. The commentator further strengthens the Hanafi position by noting that the event happened only once in Madinah, so multiple contradictory narrations cannot all be correct. Thus, the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is one ruku per rak'ah.

Key Terms
الكسوف (al-kusuf): Solar eclipse: the partial or total covering of the sun by the moon
الخسوف (al-khusuf): Lunar eclipse: the darkening of the moon
صلاة الكسوف (salat al-kusuf): The prayer performed during the occurrence of a solar eclipse
إمام الجمعة (imam al-jumu'ah): The person authorized to lead Friday and Eid prayers; he leads the eclipse prayer to avoid fitna
ركوع (ruku): Bowing in prayer; the act of bending at the waist with hands on knees

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One ruku per rak'ah
B) Two rukus per rak'ah
C) Three rukus per rak'ah
D) Four rukus per rak'ah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules salat al-kusuf as a sunnah two-rak'ah prayer with one ruku per rak'ah, reconciling conflicting hadith through contextual interpretation.

The Ruku Count in Eclipse Prayer
Inter-madhhab dispute on ruku count in eclipse prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the number of rukus in eclipse prayer and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the Hanafi method of reconciling conflicting narrations (ishtibah).

Core Idea
Eclipse prayer has one ruku per rak'ah; conflicting reports arise from observers' confusion.

The eclipse prayer (salat al-kusuf) is a sunnah prayer performed during a solar or lunar eclipse. A key point of difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools is the number of bowings (rukus) in each cycle (rak'ah). This dispute centers on how to interpret the various hadith reports on the Prophet's practice. In this lesson, we will examine the proofs from both sides and the Hanafi method of reconciling apparent contradictions.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that each rak'ah of the eclipse prayer contains one ruku, like other two-rak'ah prayers. Identify this as the mufta bihi position.
This is based on narrations from Ibn al-Zubayr and Ibn Samura.
2
Identify the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that each rak'ah contains two rukus. Recognize this as a legitimate ikhtilaf.
This is supported by numerous hadith from many Companions.
3
Examine the proofs from both sides
Review the Hanafi dalil: hadith of Ibn Samura (Abu Dawud, Ibn Majah, etc.) and the Shafi'i dalil: multiple authentic reports of two rukus. Note that both sides have strong transmission chains.
The Shafi'i reports are actually more numerous.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi scholar argues that the two-ruku reports stem from confusion (ishtibah) among observers at the back rows, who mistook the Prophet's raising his head to check the sun for a second bowing. The Prophet only performed this prayer once in Medina, so multiple conflicting reports cannot all be accurate.
This is a classic Hanafi method of reconciling contradictory hadith.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafi prays 2 rak'ahs with a total of 2 rukus; Shafi'i prays 2 rak'ahs with a total of 4 rukus. Knowing this helps when following or leading mixed-madhhab congregations.
The Hanafi ruling remains one ruku per rak'ah in practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعندنا في كلِّ ركعة ركوع واحد ، وعند الشَّافِعِي ركوعان
[١] قوله : ركوع واحد ؛ أي كسائر الصلوات الثنائيّة، هو المروي من فعل ابن الزبير، ذكره البخاري في صحيحه، وهو الثابت من الفعل النبوي برواية ابن سمرة، أخرجه أبو داود وابن ماجة والنسائي والترمذي وغيرهم.
[٢] قوله : ركوعان ؛ هذا هو الأقوى ثبوتاً عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بروايات جمع من الصحابة، رواه أصحاب الصحاح وغيرهم أنه يركع بعد القراءة طويلاً ثم قام فقرأ أدنى من القراءة الأولى ثمّ ركع طويلاً، هكذا فعله في كل ركعة، والبحث في هذا البحث طويل، مكانه الكتب المبسوطة.
[٣] على أصول المذهب ليس أقوى ثبوتاً وإنما الأقوى هو الركوع الواحد لأن ما روي أنه صلى في كل ركعة ركوعين فهو من باب الاشتباه الذي يقع لمن كان في آخر الصفوف فعائشة رضي الله عنها في صف النساء وابن عباس في صف الصبيان، والذي يدلك على صحة هذا التأويل أنه لم يفعل ذلك بالمدينة إلا مرة فيستحيل أن يكون الكل ثابتاً، فعلم بذلك أن الاختلاف من الرواة للاشتباه عليهم ، وقيل : إنه لو كان يرفع رأسه ليختبر حال الشمس هل انجلت أم لا ؟ فظنه بعضهم ركوعاً فأطلق عليه اسمه فلا يعارض ما سبق مع هذه الاحتمالات
According to us, in each rak'ah there is one bowing, and according to al-Shafi'i, there are two bowings. [1] His statement: one bowing; meaning like other two-rak'ah prayers, it is narrated from the action of Ibn al-Zubayr, mentioned by al-Bukhari in his Sahih, and it is established from the prophetic action by the narration of Ibn Samura, reported by Abu Dawud, Ibn Majah, al-Nasa'i, al-Tirmidhi and others. [2] His statement: two bowings; this is stronger in transmission from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) by narrations of a group of Companions, reported by the authors of the Sahihs and others that he bowed long after recitation, then stood and recited less than the first recitation, then bowed long, thus he did in each rak'ah, and the research on this is lengthy, its place is in the extended books. [3] According to the principles of the school, it is not stronger in transmission; rather the stronger is one bowing, because what is narrated that he prayed two bowings in each rak'ah is from the type of confusion that occurs for those at the back rows—Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) in the women's row and Ibn Abbas in the boys' row. What indicates the correctness of this interpretation is that he did not do this in Medina except once, so it is impossible that all are established. Thus it is known that the difference is from the narrators due to confusion upon them. And it is said: perhaps he raised his head to check the state of the sun whether it had cleared or not, so some thought it was a bowing and called it by that name. So it does not contradict what preceded with these probabilities.
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the number of bowings (rukus) in each rak'ah of the eclipse prayer (salat al-kusuf). The Hanafi position, stated first, is that there is one ruku per rak'ah, as in other prayers. The commentator then explains that this is supported by narrations from Ibn al-Zubayr and Ibn Samura, and the hadith is found in major collections. The Shafi'i position, that there are two rukus per rak'ah, is acknowledged as being reported by many companions and found in the Sahihs. However, the Hanafi scholar then defends the one-ruku position by arguing that the reports of two rukus are not stronger according to Hanafi principles. He explains that the two-ruku reports stem from confusion: those at the back rows, like Aisha and Ibn Abbas, might have misperceived the Prophet's actions. Specifically, the Prophet may have raised his head to check the sun, and those behind thought it was a second bowing. Moreover, the Prophet only performed this prayer once in Medina, so multiple conflicting reports cannot all be correct. Thus, the Hanafi school maintains the one-ruku position as the stronger view.

Key Terms
ركوع (rukuʽ): Bowing in prayer; a pillar (rukn) of salah
اشتباه (ishtibāh): Confusion or ambiguity in perception; used here to explain conflicting hadith

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the evidence for one ruku per rak'ah in eclipse prayer?
A) It is the only narration from the Prophet
B) The two-ruku narrations are due to confusion and the Prophet only performed the prayer once
C) The Shafi'i position is not valid at all
D) Consensus of the Companions on one ruku

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school maintains one ruku per rak'ah in eclipse prayer, resolving conflicting hadith through the principle of ishtibah (confusion).

Quiet Recitation, Elongation, Supplication, and No Sermon in Eclipse Prayer
Hanafi rulings on eclipse prayer performance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four rulings for eclipse prayer according to the Hanafi school and evaluate the evidence for quiet versus loud recitation.

Core Idea
Eclipse prayer is recited quietly, elongated, followed by supplication, and has no sermon.

The eclipse prayer (ṣalāt al-kusūf) is a sunnah muakkadah with specific performance details. This passage from ʿUmdat al-Riʿāyah outlines four key rulings: quiet recitation, elongation of the prayer, supplication afterwards, and the absence of a sermon. It also presents the intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abū Ḥanīfah and the two Ṣāḥibayn on whether recitation should be quiet or loud, and explains how Abū Ḥanīfah reconciles conflicting hadiths.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four rulings
The passage states four rulings: quiet recitation (ikhfā'), elongation (taṭwīl), supplication (duʿā'), and no sermon (khuṭbah). Each has a basis in the Sunnah.
The rulings are presented in order in the matn.
2
Analyze the proof for quiet recitation
Abū Ḥanīfah cites the hadith of Ibn ʿAbbās that he heard no word from the Prophet’s recitation, and the report in Abū Dāwūd that companions did not hear his voice. Determine how these prove quietness.
The hadith of ʿĀʾishah about loud recitation is interpreted as accidental or instructional.
3
Understand the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad hold that recitation should be loud based on ʿĀʾishah’s hadith. Note how the text reconciles this by interpreting the loudness as exceptional.
The muftā bihī is Abū Ḥanīfah’s view.
4
Examine the evidence for elongation and supplication
Elongation is proven by authentic aḥādīth that the Prophet recited as long as Sūrah al-Baqarah. Supplication is supported by the action of the Prophet during the eclipse.
The remembrances in bowing and prostration are also elongated.
5
Understand why there is no sermon
The Prophet’s sermon after the eclipse was a one-time response to a false belief, not a regular practice. Thus, a sermon is not sunnah.
Al-Baḥr and other sources confirm this.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مخفياً مطولاً قراءته فيهما وبعدَهُما يدعو حتى تنجلي الشمس، ولا يخطب
[١] قوله : مخفياً ؛ من الإخفاء ؛ أي يُخفي القراءة، هذا عند أبي حنيفة، لما روى أنه قرأ، قال بعض أصحابه : لا نسمع له صوتاً، أخرجه أبو داود، وقال ابن عباس : «لم أسمع منه حرفاً من القراءة»، أخرجه أحمد وأبو يعلى وأبو نُعيم في «الحلية». وقالا : يجهر بالقراءة لما في الصحيحين عن عائشة رضي الله عنهما : «جهر النبي في صلاة الخسوف بقراءته»، وهو عنده محمول على الجهر الاتفاقي ببعض ما يقرأ، أو الجهر التعليمي.
[٢] قوله : مطولاً ؛ من التطويل، لما ثبت في الصحاح الستة أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم طول القراءة وقرأ نحو سورة البقرة، وكذا ثبت عنه لتطويل أذكار الركوع والسجود والأدعية.
[٣] قوله : يدعو ؛ إن شاء دعا مستقبلاً جالساً أو قائماً، أو يستقبل القوم بوجهه، والناس يؤمنون، قال النعمان بن بشير : كسفت الشمس على عهد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فجعل يصلي ركعتين ويسأل حتى انجلت، أخرجه النسائي وغيره.
[٤] قوله : ولا يخطب ؛ أي الخطبة بعد صلاة الكسوف ليست بمسنونة، وما رُوي عن النبي أنه خطب وقال : «إنّ الشمس والقمر آيتان من آيات الله لا ينكسفان لموتِ أحد ولا لحياته» ، فإنّما كان للردّ على من قال : إنها كسفت لموت إبراهيم ابن النبي، وكان يوم موته يوم كسوفها، لا لأنها مشروعة له، كذا في «البحر»، وغيره.
Quietly, elongating his recitation in both, and after them he supplicates until the sun clears, and he does not deliver a sermon. [1] His statement: 'quietly' - from concealment; meaning he conceals the recitation. This is according to Abu Hanifa, because it is narrated that he recited, and some of his companions said: 'We do not hear his voice,' reported by Abu Dawud, and Ibn Abbas said: 'I did not hear a single letter of recitation from him,' reported by Ahmad, Abu Ya'la, and Abu Nu'aym in al-Hilya. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say: he recites aloud, because in the two Sahihs from Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her): 'The Prophet recited aloud in the lunar eclipse prayer.' And his (Abu Hanifa's) view is that it is interpreted as accidental volume in some parts or for teaching purposes. [2] His statement: 'elongating' - from prolongation, because it is established in the six authentic books that the Prophet (peace be upon him) lengthened the recitation and recited about Surah al-Baqarah, and similarly it is established from him the elongation of the remembrances of bowing, prostration, and supplications. [3] His statement: 'he supplicates' - if he wishes, he supplicates facing the qibla while sitting or standing, or he faces the people with his face, and the people say amen. Al-Nu'man ibn Bashir said: 'The sun eclipsed during the time of the Messenger of Allah, and he began to pray two rak'ahs and ask (supplicate) until it cleared.' Reported by al-Nasa'i and others. [4] His statement: 'and he does not deliver a sermon' - meaning the sermon after the eclipse prayer is not sunnah, and what is narrated from the Prophet that he gave a sermon and said: 'Verily the sun and moon are two signs of Allah, they do not eclipse for the death of anyone nor for his life' - that was only to refute those who said it eclipsed for the death of Ibrahim, the Prophet's son, and it was the day of his death that was the day of eclipse, not because it is prescribed for it. This is as in al-Bahr and others.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage outlines four key rulings for the eclipse prayer (salat al-kusuf) according to the Hanafi school. First, the recitation is performed quietly (ikhfā'), which is the position of Abu Hanifa. He relies on narrations that the Prophet's recitation was inaudible to those nearby, such as in the hadith of Ibn Abbas who did not hear a single letter. However, Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad hold that the recitation should be aloud (jahr), citing a hadith from Aisha that the Prophet recited aloud in the lunar eclipse prayer. Abu Hanifa interprets that loudness as accidental or instructional. The mufta bihi position is quiet recitation, as preferred by the majority of later Hanafi scholars. Second, the recitation and the remembrances in bowing and prostration should be elongated, based on authentic reports that the Prophet recited as long as Surah al-Baqarah. Third, after the prayer, one should supplicate (du'ā') while facing the qibla or the congregation, and the people say amen. This is supported by the action of the Prophet. Fourth, there is no sermon (khuṭbah) after the prayer; any report of the Prophet delivering a sermon was not to establish a sunnah but to correct the mistaken belief that the eclipse was due to the death of his son Ibrahim.

Key Terms
إخفاء (ikhfā'): To conceal the voice; here means quiet recitation in eclipse prayer
جهر (jahr): Loud recitation; the opinion of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad in eclipse prayer

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is wajib to recite aloud
B) It is recommended to recite quietly, and that is the mufta bihi position
C) It is makruh to recite quietly
D) There is no difference between quiet and loud

Key Takeaway
Eclipse prayer is performed with quiet recitation, elongation, supplication, and no sermon; the Hanafi school relies on the hadith of Ibn Abbas for quietness.

Rulings on Eclipse and Rain Prayer with the Recitation Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on recitation volume in solar eclipse prayer, plus rulings on lunar eclipse and rain prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings for solar eclipse, lunar eclipse, and rain prayer, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on recitation in the solar eclipse prayer.

Core Idea
In the Hanafi school, solar eclipse prayer is recited silently, contrary to the loud recitation of the two companions.

This lesson covers the rulings for solar eclipse prayer (salat al-kusuf), lunar eclipse prayer (salat al-khusuf), and the rain prayer (istisqa'). The central legal dispute within the Hanafi school concerns whether the recitation in the solar eclipse prayer should be silent (mukhfiyan) or aloud (jahr). The text also discusses the absence of congregation for lunar eclipse and rain prayer, and the debate over a sermon (khutbah) after these prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three prayers and their legal status
From the passage, list the three prayers: solar eclipse prayer, lunar eclipse prayer, and rain prayer. The solar eclipse prayer is sunnah muakkadah; the lunar eclipse prayer is prayed individually; the rain prayer is du'a without congregational prayer according to Abu Hanifa.
2
Focus on the recitation dispute in solar eclipse prayer
Note that the matn states 'mukhfiyan' (silently). Abu Hanifa holds silent recitation, citing hadiths where the Prophet's voice was not heard. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold aloud, citing the hadith of Aisha that the Prophet recited aloud.
3
Examine the Hanafi response to the opposing evidence
The commentary interprets the hadith of Aisha as referring to occasional loudness or for teaching purposes, not as a regular practice. This defends the silent recitation position.
4
Apply the ruling to lunar eclipse and rain prayer
For lunar eclipse, no congregation; individuals pray silently. For rain prayer, no prescribed congregational prayer; the sunnah is to supplicate and seek forgiveness for three days facing the qibla.
5
Analyze the khutbah dispute for rain prayer
The well-known Hanafi position is no sermon after rain prayer. However, some later fatwas (al-Khulasa, Fatawa Qadi Khan) consider a sermon preponderant based on authentic narrations.

مخفياً مطولاً قراءته فيهما وبعدَهُما يدعو حتّى تنجلي الشمس، ولا يخطب (مخفياً مطولاً) قراءتَهُ فيهما وبعدَهُما يدعو " حتى تنجلي الشمس ، ولا يخطب ) [١] قوله : مخفياً ؛ من الإخفاء ؛ أي يُخفي القراءة، هذا عند أبي حنيفة له، لما روى أنه قرأ، قال بعض أصحابه : لا نسمع له صوتاً)، أخرجه أبو داود، وقال ابن عباس : «لم أسمع منه حرفاً من القراءة ) ، أخرجه أحمد وأبو يعلى وأبو نُعيم في «الحلية». وقالا : يجهر بالقراءة لما في الصحيحين عن عائشة رضي الله عنهما : «جهر النبي في صلاة الخسوف بقراءته» (۳) ، وهو عنده محمول على الجهر الاتفاقي ببعض ما يقرأ، أو الجهر التعليمي. [٣] قوله : يدعو ؛ إن شاء دعا مستقبلاً جالساً أو قائماً، أو يستقبل القوم بوجهه، والناس يؤمنون، قال النعمان بن بشير : كسفت الشمس على عهد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فجعل يصلي ركعتين ويسأل حتى انجلت)، أخرجه النسائي وغيره. [٤]قوله : ولا يخطب ؛ أي الخطبة بعد صلاة الكسوف ليست بمسنونة، وما رُوي عن النبي أنه خطب وقال : «إنّ الشمس والقمر آيتان من آيات الله صلى الله عليه وسلم لا ينكسفان لموتِ أحد ولا لحياته» () ، فإنّما كان للردّ على من قال : إنها كسفت لموت إبراهيم ابن النبي ي له ، وكان يوم موته يوم كسوفها ، لا لأنها مشروعة له ، كذا في «البحر»)، وغيره.

وإن لم يحضر صلوا فرادى كالخسوف ولا جماعة في الاستسقاء، ولا خُطبة، وإن صلوا وحدانا جاز، وهو دعاء واستغفار، ويستقبل بهما القبلة وإن لم يحضر ) : أي إمامُ الجمعة ، (صلّوا فرادى (١) كالخسوف"، ولا جماعة في الاستسقاء، ولا خُطبة، وإن صلوا وحداناً جاز، وهو دعاء واستغفار، ويستقبل بهما القبلة وذكر في «الخلاصة» و«فتاوى قاضي خان»: إنّه يخطب بعد الصلاة، ولعله أرجح، وإن كان خلاف المشهور بين أصحابنا ؛ لثبوت الخطبة عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كهيئة الخطب عند البخاري ومسلم وأحمد والحاكم وابن حبان والنسائي وغيرهم، كما بسطه العيني في «البناية»(۲)، وتأويله بما ذكر بعيد.

(۱) قوله : صلوا... الخ ؛ عللوه بأنّ في الجمع بدون حضور الإمام المأذون له احتمال الفتنة، وذكر في «المحيط»: إنّه إن أذن الإمام الأعظم الذي يصلي الجمعة والعيدين، فحينئذ يؤمهم إمام حيهم في مسجدهم.
[۲] قوله : كالخسوف (۳) ؛ أي خسوف القمر، فإنّه ليست في صلاته جماعة مسنونة، فإنّها لم تنقل وإن نقلت صلاة ركعتين فيه عن النبي عند الدارقطني. [٣] قوله : ولا جماعة ؛ أعلم أنّ الاستسقاء وهو طلب المطر والدعاء بإنزاله عند الاحتياج إليه ليست فيه عند أبي حنيفة جماعة مسنونة، ولو صلّى بالجماعة جاز عنده أيضاً.
ومن قال : إنها مكروهة عنده فقد غلط، ولا تسن الخطبة أيضاً ؛ لأنها تبع لجماعة الصلاة، وإذ ليست فليست والمسنونُ فيه هو الدعاء والاستغفار مستقبل القبلة في الصحراء، ويخرج الإمامُ ومَن معه متواضعين متخاشعين، يفعلون ذلك ثلاثة أيام. وحجته في ذلك ما روي أنه استسقى في خطبة الجمعة)، ولم ترد عنه صلاة خاصة لذلك.

Quietly, lengthening his recitation in them, and after them he supplicates until the sun clears, and he does not deliver a sermon. (Quietly, lengthening) his recitation in them, and after them he supplicates "until the sun clears, and he does not deliver a sermon." [1] His saying: quietly; from concealment; meaning he conceals the recitation. This is according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, because it is narrated that he recited, some of his companions said: We do not hear his voice. Reported by Abu Dawud. And Ibn Abbas said: I did not hear a letter of the recitation from him. Reported by Ahmad, Abu Ya'la, and Abu Nu'aym in al-Hilya. And they (the two companions) said: He recites aloud because of what is in the two Sahihs from Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her: "The Prophet ﷺ recited aloud in the solar eclipse prayer." And according to him (Abu Hanifa), this is interpreted as occasional aloudness in some of what he recited, or teaching aloudness. [2] His saying: lengthening; from prolongation, because it is established in the six authentic collections that the Prophet ﷺ lengthened the recitation and recited about the length of Surah al-Baqarah. Likewise, it is established from him to prolong the remembrances of bowing and prostration and supplications. [3] His saying: he supplicates; if he wishes, he supplicates facing the qibla sitting or standing, or he faces the people with his face, and the people say amen. Al-Nu'man ibn Bashir said: The sun eclipsed during the time of the Messenger of Allah ﷺ, so he began to pray two rak'ahs and ask until it cleared. Reported by al-Nasa'i and others. [4] His saying: and he does not deliver a sermon; meaning the sermon after the solar eclipse prayer is not sunnah. And what is narrated from the Prophet that he delivered a sermon and said: "Indeed, the sun and the moon are two signs from the signs of Allah; they do not eclipse for the death of anyone nor for his life." That was only to refute those who said it eclipsed for the death of Ibrahim, the Prophet's son, and that day was the day of his death, not because it is prescribed for it. Thus in al-Bahr and others.

And if (the imam) is not present, they pray individually like the lunar eclipse. There is no congregation in the rain prayer, and no sermon. And if they pray individually, it is permissible. It is supplication and seeking forgiveness. He faces the qibla with both. And if (the imam of Friday) is not present, they pray individually like the lunar eclipse. There is no congregation in the rain prayer, and no sermon. And if they pray individually, it is permissible. It is supplication and seeking forgiveness. He faces the qibla with both. And it is mentioned in al-Khulasa and Fatawa Qadi Khan: He delivers a sermon after the prayer, and perhaps it is more preponderant, even though it is against the well-known view among our companions, because the sermon is established from the Prophet ﷺ in the manner of sermons according to al-Bukhari, Muslim, Ahmad, al-Hakim, Ibn Hibban, al-Nasa'i, and others, as al-'Ayni elaborated in al-Binaya. And interpreting it as mentioned is far-fetched.

(1) His saying: they pray... etc.; they explained that gathering without the presence of the authorized imam has the potential for discord. And it is mentioned in al-Muhit: If the supreme imam who leads Friday and the two 'Eids permits, then the imam of their district leads them in their mosque.
[2] His saying: like the lunar eclipse; meaning the lunar eclipse prayer: there is no sunnah congregation in it, because it is not transmitted, even though two rak'ah prayer for it is transmitted from the Prophet by al-Daraqutni. [3] His saying: and no congregation; know that the rain prayer (istisqa'), which is seeking rain and supplication for its descent when needed, has no sunnah congregation in it according to Abu Hanifa. And if one prays with congregation, it is also permissible according to him.
And whoever says it is disliked (makruh) according to him has erred. And the sermon is not sunnah either, because it is a consequence of congregational prayer, and since there is no congregation, there is none. The sunnah therein is supplication and seeking forgiveness facing the qibla in an open space. The imam and those with him go out humbly and submissively, doing that for three days. His evidence for that is what is narrated that he sought rain in the Friday sermon, and no specific prayer for it is reported from him.

(3) al-Khusuf: is the veiling of the moon's surface or part of it when the earth is between it and the sun. See al-Sihah (1:345). Commentary
This passage from 'Umda al-Ri'ayah is an expansion on rulings for solar eclipse prayer (salat al-kusuf), lunar eclipse prayer (salat al-khusuf), and the rain prayer (salat al-istisqa'). It begins by establishing that in the solar eclipse prayer, the recitation is to be performed quietly (mukhfiyan) and lengthened (mutawwilan). After the prayer, the imam should supplicate until the sun clears, and no sermon is delivered. The commentary immediately delves into an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa holds that the recitation is silent, citing a hadith where the Prophet's voice was not heard and the hadith of Ibn 'Abbas. However, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the two companions) hold that the recitation should be aloud, based on the hadith in the two Sahihs from 'Aisha that the Prophet recited aloud. The commentator explains that Abu Hanifa interprets that hadith as either occasional loudness or for teaching purposes. The disputed point is the thamarah al-khilaf: in practice, Hanafis following the matn recite silently, but some later fatwas may consider both valid.

The passage then moves to the length: the recitation should be prolonged, as proven by the six authentic hadith collections and the Prophet's lengthy qiyam in such prayers. After the eclipse ends, the imam may supplicate facing the qibla or the congregation, who respond with amin. The absence of a sermon after the eclipse prayer is then justified: the Prophet's reported sermon on the occasion of the solar eclipse was not to establish a sunnah but to refute the claim that the eclipse was due to the death of his son Ibrahim. The well-known Hanafi position is that there is no sermon for the eclipse prayer.

Later, the passage addresses the case when the imam (of Friday) is absent: for lunar eclipse, people pray individually (not in congregation), following the same ruling as solar eclipse. Regarding the rain prayer (istisqa'), there is no sunnah congregation, no sermon, but individuals may pray individually. The sunnah is for the imam and people to go out to an open space for three days, humbly supplicating and seeking forgiveness facing the qibla. The commentator notes a contrary view in al-Khulasa and Fatawa Qadi Khan that a sermon is performed after the rain prayer, deeming it more preponderant, but the common position is against it. This position is based on the established practice from the Prophet, who sought rain during a Friday sermon without a special prayer.

Throughout, the commentator relies on hadith evidence and Hanafi principles, maintaining the school's distinctions between obligatory, sunnah, and permissible acts.

Key Terms
مخفياً (mukhfiyan): Performing recitation in a low voice such that it is not audible to others.
مطولاً (mutawwilan): Lengthening the recitation and other parts of the prayer more than usual.
كسوف (kusuf): Solar eclipse; covering of the sun's light.
خسوف (khusuf): Lunar eclipse; covering of the moon's light.
استسقاء (istisqa'): Prayer for rain; consists of supplication and seeking forgiveness, without prescribed congregational prayer according to Abu Hanifa.
خطبة (khutbah): A sermon delivered after the eclipse prayer or rain prayer; not sunnah in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling regarding recitation in the solar eclipse prayer?
A) It is performed aloud (jahr).
B) It is performed silently (mukhfiyan).
C) It is optional; the imam may choose.
D) It is performed with a slight murmur.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that recitation in the solar eclipse prayer is silent, based on the matn and Abu Hanifa's view, while the congregation and khutbah for lunar and rain prayers are not sunnah.
