Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Salat al-Istisqa': Congregation and Khutbah – The Hanafi Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on ruling of salat al-istisqa'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on congregational prayer and khutbah for istisqa', and evaluate which position is relied upon in later Hanafi fatwa.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa: no sunnah congregation or khutbah; Sahibayn: sunnah to pray two rak'ahs with khutbah.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya presents divergent views within the Hanafi school regarding salat al-istisqa' (prayer for rain). While the well-known (mashhur) position attributed to Abu Hanifa holds that congregational prayer and khutbah are not prescribed, his two students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, consider them sunnah, supported by authentic hadith. The commentator notes that later Hanafi authorities have regarded the khutbah after prayer as more preponderant (arjah), illustrating how rulings can be re-evaluated in light of stronger evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue in dispute
The core disagreement is whether salat al-istisqa' should be performed in congregation with a khutbah, or whether it is simply individual supplication. Note that both sides agree that making dua and istighfar is sunnah.
This is not about permissibility of praying for rain, but about the form.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and its proof
Abu Hanifa holds that there is no sunnah congregation and no khutbah. The sunnah is to go out to the desert, facing qiblah, making dua and istighfar for three days. His proof: the Prophet (PBUH) performed istisqa' only within a Friday khutbah, without a separate prayer.
The commentator clarifies that congregation is permissible (jaza) but not sunnah.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their proof
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that it is sunnah for the imam to lead two rak'ahs audibly (like Eid) and deliver a khutbah after the prayer. Their proof: multiple hadiths in the Sunan and Sahihayn report that the Prophet did exactly that, including turning his cloak.
The commentator suggests these hadiths may not have reached Abu Hanifa.
4
Examine the tarjih (preference) of later scholars
The commentator cites al-Khulasa and Fatawa Qadi Khan, which consider the khutbah after prayer as arjah, despite contradicting the mashhur. This shows that later Hanafi muftis leaned toward the Sahibayn's view due to stronger hadith evidence.
The mashhur remains the majority position, but the mufta bihi may vary.
5
Note additional details: turning cloak and presence of dhimmi
The passage also covers the sunnah of qalb al-rida' (turning the cloak) which is recommended according to Imam Muhammad and the three other schools. It also prohibits the presence of a dhimmi because mercy is sought and curses descend on disbelievers.
These details are not part of the core dispute but enrich the ruling.

And if he (the imam of Friday) is not present, they pray individually like the lunar eclipse, and there is no congregation in istisqa', nor a khutbah. And if they pray individually, it is permissible. It is supplication and seeking forgiveness, and they face the qiblah for both. And it is mentioned in al-Khulasa and Fatawa Qadi Khan that he delivers a khutbah after the prayer, and perhaps it is more preponderant, even though it is contrary to the well-known (mashhur) among our companions; because the khutbah is established from the Prophet (PBUH) in the manner of sermons as found in Bukhari, Muslim, Ahmad, al-Hakim, Ibn Hibban, al-Nasa’i and others, as al-‘Ayni elaborated in al-Binaya, and its interpretation as mentioned is far-fetched. The commentator says: His statement: 'they pray...' etc.; they reasoned that in gathering without the presence of the authorized imam there is a possibility of fitna. And it is mentioned in al-Muhit: if the supreme imam who leads Friday and Eid prayers gives permission, then the imam of their district leads them in their mosque. His statement: 'like the lunar eclipse'; meaning a lunar eclipse, for there is no sunnah congregation in its prayer, as it was not transmitted, although two rak'ahs during it are transmitted from the Prophet by al-Daraqutni. His statement: 'and no congregation'; know that istisqa', which is asking for rain and supplicating for its sending down when in need, according to Abu Hanifa there is no sunnah congregation in it, and if one prays in congregation, it is permissible according to him as well. And whoever says it is makruh according to him has erred. And the khutbah is also not sunnah because it is dependent on the congregation of prayer, and since there is no congregation, there is no khutbah. And the sunnah is supplication and seeking forgiveness facing the qiblah in the desert, and the imam and those with him go out humbly and submissively, doing that for three days. His proof for that is what was narrated that he (PBUH) performed istisqa' in the Friday khutbah, and no specific prayer for it was reported from him. The Book of Prayer: The Prayer of Witr and Supererogatory Prayers. Without turning the cloak and the presence of a dhimmi, without turning the cloak and the presence of a dhimmi. And according to the two (Sahibayn), it is sunnah for the imam to pray two rak'ahs like Eid, reciting audibly, and to deliver a khutbah after them, because the narrators of the four Sunan and the two Sahihs and others reported that he did so. And perhaps these reports did not reach the Imam (Abu Hanifa); otherwise he would not have denied the sunnah of congregation. The commentator says: His statement: 'without turning the cloak'; its manner: he makes its upper part its lower part and its lower part its upper part, crossing its two ends behind, and it is sunnah according to Muhammad and the three imams (i.e., the other three schools) for him, because it is established from him (PBUH) in the istisqa' khutbah according to Abu Dawud and others, and the wisdom in it is optimism. His statement: 'and the presence of a dhimmi'; meaning without the presence of a disbeliever in that gathering, even if he is a dhimmi, because istisqa' is for sending down mercy, and upon the disbelievers descends curse, so their presence detracts from success.

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya is a detailed commentary on the rulings of salat al-istisqa' (prayer for rain) within the Hanafi school. It begins by restating the matn: when the Friday imam is absent, people pray individually for the eclipse, and for istisqa' there is no congregational prayer or khutbah; individual prayer is permissible, and the essence is dua and istighfar facing the qiblah. The commentator then presents a view from al-Khulasa and Fatawa Qadi Khan that a khutbah after the prayer is more preponderant (arjah), despite contradicting the well-known (mashhur) position among early Hanafis. This is based on strong hadith evidence from major compilations. The commentator explains that the reason for not having congregation without the imam is the fear of fitna, but if the supreme imam grants permission, the local imam may lead. He clarifies that Abu Hanifa's position is not that congregational prayer is makruh; it is merely not sunnah, but permissible. The sunnah is to go out for three days making dua and istighfar. Abu Hanifa's proof is that the Prophet (PBUH) performed istisqa' during a Friday khutbah without a special prayer. The passage then moves to the Book of Witr and Optional Prayers, stating that according to the Sahibayn, the imam should pray two rak'ahs audibly like Eid and deliver a khutbah after, citing hadith. The commentator speculates that these reports may not have reached Abu Hanifa. The sunnah of turning the cloak (qalb al-rida') is described: flipping the upper part to the lower and vice versa, crossing ends behind the back, which is a sunnah according to Imam Muhammad and the three other schools. The wisdom is optimism (tafa'ul). Finally, the presence of a dhimmi is prohibited because istisqa' seeks mercy, while disbelievers bring curse, harming the success of the supplication. This passage therefore presents both the mashhur Hanafi view and an alternative, later preference, along with practical details.

Key Terms
استسقاء (istisqa'): The act of asking Allah for rain, particularly when in need, through supplication and prayer.
قلب رداء (qalb al-rida'): Turning the cloak by reversing its upper and lower parts and crossing the ends behind the back, as a sign of humility and optimism.
ذمي (dhimmi): A non-Muslim living under Muslim rule with a pact of protection (dhimma).
خطبة (khutbah): A sermon delivered before or after a congregational prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what is the sunnah in salat al-istisqa'?
A) Praying two rak'ahs in congregation with a khutbah
B) Making supplication (dua) and seeking forgiveness (istighfar) facing the qiblah
C) Offering a sacrifice
D) Reciting specific prayers in the mosque

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has an internal difference on whether istisqa' involves congregational prayer; the mashhur position follows Abu Hanifa against congregation, but later scholars consider the khutbah preferable due to stronger hadith evidence.

Rulings on Turning the Cloak and Prohibition of Dhimmi Presence in Istisqa
Explaining the sunnah of turning the cloak and excluding non-Muslims from istisqa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on turning the cloak during istisqa and explain why the presence of a dhimmi is prohibited.

Core Idea
Turning the cloak in istisqa is sunnah, and dhimmis must not attend because mercy is sought while curses descend on them.

The istisqa prayer has specific sunan and conditions. This passage clarifies the correct ruling on turning the cloak (which the matn appears to deny) and explains the exclusion of non-Muslims. Additionally, we see an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the congregation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
Read the passage and note the two key rulings: turning the cloak and the prohibition of dhimmi presence. Observe that the base text uses 'bila' (without) but the commentary corrects the turning ruling to sunnah.
The base text's 'bila' is not the operative ruling; the commentary provides the correct hadith-based ruling.
2
Analyze the evidence for turning
Find the hadith cited for turning the cloak. Note that it is considered sunnah according to Muhammad and the three Imams, with the wisdom of optimism (tafa'ul).
The turning is a physical act symbolizing reversal of hardship.
3
Examine the exclusion of dhimmis
Understand the reasoning: istisqa seeks mercy, while curses descend on disbelievers. Their presence detracts from the purpose, so they should not attend.
This is a condition for the prayer's efficacy, not its validity.
4
Study the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on congregation
Note that Abu Hanifa did not consider congregation sunnah, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad did. The commentator suggests the hadith did not reach Abu Hanifa.
The mufta bihi is the view of the two, as it is supported by authentic reports.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Conclude that the relied-upon position is to pray in congregation, turn the cloak, and exclude dhimmis. These are all sunnah or recommended acts.
The turning of the cloak is agreed upon; the congregation is preferred.

Chapter of Prayer: Prayer of Witr and Supererogatory Prayers. [Ruling: The imam prays] without turning the cloak and without the presence of a dhimmi. And according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is recommended that the imam pray two rak'ahs like the Eid prayer, reciting aloud, and deliver a sermon after it, because the authors of the four Sunan and the two Sahihs and others narrated that he (the Prophet) did so. [1] His saying: 'without turning the cloak': its manner is that he makes its top its bottom and its bottom its top, crossing its two ends behind him. [2] His saying: 'and without the presence of a dhimmi' i.e. without the presence of a disbeliever in that gathering, even if he is a dhimmi, because istisqa is for sending down mercy, and curses descend upon disbelievers, so their presence detracts from success.

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the rulings of the istisqa prayer. The base text states two conditions: (1) the imam does not turn his cloak, and (2) no dhimmi should be present. The commentator explains that according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, it is recommended for the imam to pray two rak'ahs like the Eid prayer with audible recitation and a sermon, based on hadith reports. They suggest Abu Hanifa may not have known these reports. Then the commentator details the turning of the cloak: the manner is to reverse the cloak, top to bottom and bottom to top, crossing the ends behind. This is sunnah according to Muhammad and the three Imams (Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and the later imams) because it is authentically reported. The wisdom is optimism (tafa'ul). Regarding the presence of a dhimmi, the passage clarifies that even a dhimmi who is a non-Muslim should not attend, because istisqa seeks mercy, and curses descend on disbelievers, thus their presence impedes the prayer's effectiveness.

قلب رداء (qalb al-rida'): To reverse the cloak by turning its top to bottom and crossing the ends behind the back.
ذمي (dhimmi): A non-Muslim living under Muslim protection with a covenant.
استسقاء (istisqa): The prayer performed to seek rain from Allah during drought.

When to Cut Your Individual Prayer to Join the Congregation
Ruling statement with detailed conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on cutting an individual obligatory prayer to join the congregational prayer, distinguishing between fard and nafl cases and identifying the conditions that trigger the obligation to cut.

Core Idea
Cut your fard prayer to join jama'ah only if you haven't prostrated the first rak'ah or if the prayer is not four-rak'ah.

This lesson covers a common scenario: you start praying an obligatory prayer alone in the mosque, and then the iqamah for the same prayer is called. Should you continue alone or join the congregation? The Hanafi school provides a detailed set of conditions that determine whether cutting your current prayer is wajib, permissible, or even discouraged. We will unpack the matn and its commentary to give you a precise toolkit for this situation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Determine whether the prayer you started is fard (obligatory) or nafl (supererogatory). Also note the location of the iqamah relative to where you are praying.
The ruling only applies to fard prayers that are being performed in the same place where iqamah is called.
2
Apply the condition of sajdah
If you have not yet performed the prostration (sajdah) of the first rak'ah, you must cut your prayer and join. If you have prostrated, look at the number of rak'ahs of your prayer.
The first rak'ah's prostration is the tipping point; before it, cutting is straightforward.
3
Determine whether to cut based on prayer type
If the prayer is not a four-rak'ah prayer (i.e., two or three rak'ahs), you must cut even if you have prostrated. If it is a four-rak'ah prayer, you must have added at least one extra rak'ah after the first (i.e., you are in the second or later rak'ah) to be able to cut; otherwise, you do not cut.
The reasoning: continuing would make you miss the congregation due to completing the majority of the prayer.
4
Handle the manner of cutting
You may cut either by saying the taslim (salutation) or by making the takbir with the intention to join the imam, which automatically terminates your current prayer.
Both methods are valid; the second is more efficient as it directly merges you into the congregation.
5
Note the exception for nafl and case of Maghrib
If you are in a supererogatory prayer (including sunnah of Zuhr or Jumu'ah), you do not cut; rather, you complete two rak'ahs and then join. However, if you cut an obligatory prayer after two rak'ahs in Maghrib, those two rak'ahs become nafl, and praying nafl after sunset before Maghrib is disliked if it causes delay.
The relied-upon position is to complete the sunnah as two rak'ahs, as preferred by Ibn al-Humam.

Chapter on Catching the Obligatory Prayer. (Whoever starts an obligatory prayer and the iqamah is established for him: if he has not prostrated for the first rak'ah, or he has prostrated while being in a non-four-rak'ah prayer, or in a four-rak'ah prayer and he adds another to it, he should cut his prayer and follow the imam.) That is, whoever starts an obligatory prayer alone, and the iqamah for this fard is established—the pronoun in 'established for him' refers to the iqamah, as one says 'a beating was beaten'—if he has not prostrated for the first rak'ah, he cuts and follows. And if he has prostrated: if he is in a non-four-rak'ah prayer, he likewise cuts; because if he does not cut and prays another rak'ah, he would complete his prayer in a two-rak'ah prayer and would have performed the majority in a three-rak'ah prayer, and the majority has the ruling of the whole, so he would miss the congregation; or because he would become a voluntary performer: praying two rak'ahs after sunset in Maghrib. [1] His saying: 'in an obligatory prayer' is a restriction excluding supererogatory prayer, for one who starts a supererogatory prayer when the iqamah for the fard is established does not cut absolutely—whether he has performed one prostration or not—rather he completes it as two rak'ahs. Likewise for the sunnah of Zuhr and the sunnah of Jumu'ah if the iqamah is established or the imam delivers the sermon, as preferred by Ibn al-Humam and his student Ibn Amir Hajj, and chosen by many of our companions; some chose that he completes it as four because it is one prayer, and preferred by the author of Tanwir al-Absar. [2] His saying: 'iqamah is established for him' means in that place; if it is established in the mosque while the individual is at home or in another mosque, he does not cut. [3] His saying: 'he cuts' means he cuts that prayer while standing; it is said: with a salutation, and it is said: by saying the takbir while standing intending to start the imam's prayer, so the first ends necessarily. [4] His saying: 'the majority' so it does not invalidate due to the semblance of completion, even if true completion does not occur. [5] His saying: 'he becomes' means if he cuts at the end of two rak'ahs and prays with the imam. [6] His saying: 'voluntary performer...' etc.: for what he cuts becomes supererogatory, and supererogatory prayer after sunset before Maghrib is disliked according to the majority of our scholars; they reasoned that it necessitates delaying the Maghrib prayer which is disliked; there is a lengthy discussion in Fath al-Qadir, and the correct view is that there is no dislike if it does not cause delay.
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This chapter deals with the situation where a person starts an obligatory prayer individually and then the congregational prayer for that same obligatory prayer is established. The matn provides the detailed rulings: if he has not yet performed the prostration of the first rak'ah, he must cut his prayer and join the congregation. If he has prostrated, then in prayers other than the four-rak'ah ones (i.e., two or three rak'ah), he also cuts because continuing would lead to confusion. In four-rak'ah prayers, if he adds another rak'ah after prostrating, he cuts. The commentary clarifies that this applies only to obligatory prayers, not supererogatory ones. In supererogatory prayers, he does not cut; he completes two rak'ahs, even for the sunnah of Zuhr or Jumu'ah, unless the imam has begun the sermon. The commentary also specifies that the iqamah must be in the same place; if it is established elsewhere, he does not cut. The manner of cutting is either by saying the salutation or by intending to join the imam with a takbir. The passage also discusses that if he cuts after two rak'ahs in Maghrib, those two rak'ahs become supererogatory, which is disliked if it delays Maghrib.

Key Terms
إدراك الفريضة (idrak al-faridah): Catching the obligatory congregational prayer by joining the imam before it ends.
قطع (qat'): To terminate the current prayer intentionally to join the congregation.
متنفل (mutanaffil): One who performs a supererogatory (nafl) prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) He completes one rak'ah and then cuts.

Key Takeaway
Cutting an individual fard prayer to join the congregation is wajib under specific conditions regarding prostration and prayer type; supererogatory prayers are not cut but completed as two rak'ahs.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Cutting Individual Fard to Join Congregation
Explains conditions for cutting individual fard to join congregation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for cutting an individual fard prayer to join the congregation and apply the Hanafi ruling when three rak'ahs have been performed.

Core Idea
Cutting individual fard to join congregation is recommended unless three rak'ahs have been prayed — then completion is obligatory.

The Hanafi school values the merit of congregational prayer even at the expense of an individual beginning. However, the decision to cut an individual fard is not arbitrary; it depends on how much of the prayer has been completed. This lesson unpacks the detailed conditions laid out in the matn and explains the underlying logic, including the principle that 'the majority takes the ruling of the whole'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its general ruling
The act is cutting an individual fard prayer to join the congregation. The general ruling is that it is recommended (mustahabb) when specific conditions are met.
This is not a prohibited invalidation; it is a legitimate transfer to nafl.
2
Analyze the first condition: before sujud of the first rak'ah
If the individual has not yet performed the sajdah of the first rak'ah, he cuts immediately and follows the imam.
No nafl issue arises because the first rak'ah is incomplete without sajdah.
3
Analyze the second condition: after sujud in a non-4-rak'ah prayer
If he has performed sajdah but the prayer is not a 4-rak'ah one (e.g., Fajr or Maghrib), he also cuts. This is because by continuing he would complete (in Fajr) or perform the majority (in Maghrib), thus losing the congregation.
The principle 'al-akthar lahu hukm al-kull' applies for Maghrib.
4
Analyze the third condition: in a 4-rak'ah prayer after adding one rak'ah
If the prayer is 4-rak'ah (e.g., Zuhr) and he has performed sujud of the first rak'ah, he must add another rak'ah (to make two) and then cut. This is because cutting with a single rak'ah would result in a nafl of one rak'ah, which is invalid in the school.
Thus he prays two rak'ahs (which becomes nafl) and then joins.
5
Identify the exception: when three rak'ahs have been completed
If he has prayed three rak'ahs of a 4-rak'ah fard, he must complete the fourth (to finish his fard) and then join the congregation as a supererogatory prayer (nafl). Cutting after three rak'ahs is not permissible because it would invalidate the majority of the prayer.
This is wajib; if he cuts, he sins.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب إدراك الفريضة شَرَعَ في فرض فأقيمت له إنْ لم يسجد للركعة الأولى، أو سَجَد وهو في غير رباعي، أو فيه وضم إليها أُخرى قَطَعَ واقْتَدَى (من شَرَعَ في فرض فأقيمت له إن لم يسجد للركعة الأولى، أو سَجَد وهو في غير رباعي، أو فيه وضم إليها أخرى قطَعَ واقْتَدَى) أي من شَرَعَ فِي فَرضِ منفردا، فأقيمت لهذا الفرض، والضمير في أقيمت يرجع إلى الإقامة، كما يقال: ضُرِبَ ضَرْبٌ، فإن لم يسجد للركعة الأولى قطع، واقتدى. وإن سجد: فإن كان في غير الرباعي فكذا؛ لأنَّه إن لم يقطع، وصلى ركعة أخرى، يتم صلاته في الثنائي، ويوجد الأكثر في الثلاثي، وللأكثر حُكْمُ الكلّ، فتفوته الجماعة، أو لأنه يصير متنفلاً: بركعتين بعد الغروب في المغرب. [1] قوله: في فرض؛ احتراز عن النفل، فإنّ الشارع فيه إذا أقيمت للفرض لا يقطع مطلقاً، سواء قيد الأولى بسجدة أو لا، بل يتمه ركعتين، وكذا سنة الظهر، وسنة الجمعة إذا أقيمت، أو خطب الإمام، كما رجّحه ابن الهمام وتلميذه ابن أمير حاج، واختاره كثير من أصحابنا، واختار بعضُهم أن يتمها أربعاً؛ لأنها صلاة واحدة، ورجحه صاحب «تنوير الأبصار». [2] قوله: فأقيمت؛ أي في ذلك المكان، فإن أقيمت في المسجد، والمنفرد في البيت أو في مسجد آخر لا يقطع. [3] قوله: قطع؛ أي تلك الصلاة قائماً، قيل: بتسليمة، وقيل: بأن يكبر قائماً ينوي الشروع في صلاة الإمام، فينقطع الأول بالضرورة. [4] قوله: الأكثر؛ فلا ينقضه لوجود شبهة الفراغ، وإن لم توجد حقيقة الفراغ. [5] قوله: يصير؛ إن قطع على رأس الركعتين، وصلى مع الإمام. [6] قوله: متنفلاً... الخ؛ فإنّ ما قطعه يصير نفلًا، والنفل بعد الغروب قبل المغرب مكروه عند جمهور مشايخنا، عللوه بأنه مستلزم لتأخير صلاة المغرب المكروهة، وفيه بحث طويل مذكور في «فتح القدير»، والحق أنه لا كراهة إذا لم يستلزم التأخير. (وإن صلى ثلاثاً منه يتمه ثم يقتدي متتنفلاً؛ لأنَّه قد أدى الأكثر، وللأكثر حُكْمُ الكل) [1] قوله: والقطع... الخ؛ دفع لما يقال: إنّ القطع إبطال لعمله، وقد نهى عنه. [2] قوله: لا يكون إبطالاً؛ أي لا يعد إبطالاً شرعاً، ولا يكون إبطالاً منهياً عنه. [3] قوله: حتى يصير ركعتان؛ لأنّ فيه إحراز للجماعة، وصيانة للركعة المؤداة عن البطلان، فإنّ التنقل بركعة واحدة عند أصحابنا باطل، كما صرح به في «البحر» و«النهر». [4] قوله: تقديره؛ احتاج إلى ذكر التقدير لتحقيق كونه حالاً من قوله: «أو فيه». [5] قوله: وقد ضَمَّ؛ احتاج إلى إيراد قد التحقيقية مع عدمها في المتن؛ لما تقرر في مقرّه أنّ الماضي إذا كان حالاً لا يخلو عن قد تحقيقاً أو تقديراً. [6] قوله: قطع واقتدى؛ قال صاحب «البحر» في هامشه: «إنّ القطع قد يكون حراماً ومباحاً ومستحباً وواجباً، فالحرام بغير عذر والمباح إذا خاف فوت مال، والمستحب القطعُ للإكمال، والواجب لإحياء نفس». انتهى. [7] قوله: يتمه؛ أي وجوباً، فإن قطع أثم. [8] قوله: متتنفلاً؛ لأنَّ الفرض لا يُصلّى مرتين، يدل عليه قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم للرجلين اللذين صليا: «إذا صليتما في رحالكما، ثم أتيتما صلاة قوم فصليا معهم، واجعلا صلاتكما معهم سبحة»: أي نافلة أخرجه الترمذي وأبو داود وغيرهما بألفاظ متقاربة.
Chapter of Realizing the Obligatory Prayer. One who started an obligatory prayer (individual) and the iqamah is established for him: if he has not performed the sajdah of the first rak'ah, or if he performed sajdah and he is in a non-four-rak'ah prayer, or if in a four-rak'ah prayer and he added another rak'ah to it, he cuts (the prayer) and follows (the imam). (One who started an obligatory prayer individually, and the iqamah is established for this prayer, and the pronoun in 'established' refers to the iqamah, as it is said: 'he was struck with a strike'.) If he did not perform sajdah for the first rak'ah, he cuts and follows. If he performed sajdah: then if he is in a non-four-rak'ah prayer, similarly; because if he does not cut and prays another rak'ah, he completes his prayer in a two-rak'ah (prayer), and he performs the majority in a three-rak'ah (prayer), and the majority has the ruling of the whole, so the congregation is lost to him, or because he becomes a supererogatory (prayer) performer: with two rak'ahs after sunset in Maghrib. [1] His saying: 'in an obligatory prayer'; a precaution against supererogatory (prayer), for the one who starts it when the iqamah for the obligatory (prayer) is established does not cut at all, whether he tied the first (rak'ah) with a prostration or not, but rather completes it as two rak'ahs, and likewise the sunnah of Zuhr and the sunnah of Jumu'ah when the iqamah is established or the imam delivers the sermon, as preferred by Ibn al-Humam and his student Ibn Amir Hajj, and chosen by many of our companions, and some chose that he completes it as four, because it is one prayer, and preferred by the author of 'Tanwir al-Absar'. [2] His saying: 'established'; i.e. in that place, for if it is established in the mosque while the individual is in his house or another mosque, he does not cut. [3] His saying: 'cuts'; i.e. that prayer while standing. It is said: with a taslimah, and it is said: by saying takbir while standing intending to start the prayer of the imam, so the first (prayer) is necessarily cut. [4] His saying: 'the majority'; so he does not void it due to the existence of the semblance of completion, even if the reality of completion does not exist. [5] His saying: 'he becomes'; if he cuts at the end of two rak'ahs and prays with the imam. [6] His saying: 'supererogatory performer' etc.; for what he cuts becomes supererogatory, and supererogatory prayer after sunset before Maghrib is disliked according to the majority of our scholars, they justified it because it necessitates delaying the Maghrib prayer which is disliked, and there is a long discussion mentioned in 'Fath al-Qadir', and the truth is there is no dislike if it does not necessitate delay. (And if he prays three of it, he completes it then follows as a supererogatory performer; because he has performed the majority, and the majority has the ruling of the whole.) [1] His saying: 'and cutting... etc.'; a refutation of what is said: cutting is invalidating his action, and he has been prohibited from it. [2] His saying: 'it is not invalidating'; i.e. it is not considered invalidation legally, and it is not a prohibited invalidation. [3] His saying: 'so that it becomes two rak'ahs'; because in it is attaining the congregation and preserving the performed rak'ah from invalidity, for performing supererogatory (prayer) with one rak'ah is invalid according to our companions, as stated in 'al-Bahr' and 'al-Nahr'. [4] His saying: 'its appreciation'; he needed to mention the appreciation to realize it being a state from his saying 'or in it'. [5] His saying: 'and he had added'; he needed to bring the verifying 'qad' despite its absence in the text; because as established in its place, the past tense when it is a state is not free from 'qad' actually or virtually. [6] His saying: 'he cuts and follows'; said the author of 'al-Bahr' in its margin: 'Cutting may be prohibited, permissible, recommended, and obligatory. The prohibited is without excuse, the permissible if he fears loss of wealth, the recommended for completion, and the obligatory for reviving a life.' End. [7] His saying: 'completes it'; i.e. obligatorily, for if he cuts he sins. [8] His saying: 'supererogatory performer'; because the obligatory prayer is not prayed twice, as indicated by his saying صلى الله عليه وسلم to the two men who had prayed: 'If you prayed in your dwellings, then you come to a congregational prayer, pray with them, and make your prayer with them a supererogatory (prayer)': i.e. nafl, narrated by al-Tirmidhi and Abu Dawud and others with similar wording.
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This passage is a legal ruling (hukm shar'i) from the Hanafi school regarding the situation when a person has started praying an obligatory (fard) prayer individually, and then the iqamah for the congregation of that same fard is established. The ruling explains when it is permissible (or recommended) to cut the individual prayer and join the imam, and when it is not. The author first states the matn: if he has not performed the sajdah of the first rak'ah, he cuts and joins; if he has performed sajdah, then if the prayer is not a four-rak'ah prayer (i.e., it is a two-rak'ah fard or three-rak'ah Maghrib), he also cuts and joins, because by continuing he would either complete the prayer (in two-rak'ah) or perform the majority of the prayer (in Maghrib), and the majority takes the ruling of the whole, so the merit of congregation is lost. Alternatively, if he continues in Maghrib, he becomes a supererogatory performer with two rak'ahs after sunset, which is disliked. If the prayer is a four-rak'ah fard, he must add another rak'ah to the first to make two rak'ahs of nafl, then cut and join the congregation; cutting without doing so is not allowed because one cannot perform nafl with a single rak'ah (which is invalid in the Hanafi school). The commentary then elaborates on each part of the matn: the term 'fard' excludes supererogatory (nafl) prayers—if one is praying a supererogatory prayer and the iqamah is established, he should not cut it immediately but complete it as two rak'ahs (and similarly for the sunnah of Zuhr and Jumu'ah, though there is some ikhtilaf). The iqamah here refers specifically to the same location; if the iqamah is in a mosque while the individual is at home or another mosque, he does not cut. The method of cutting is by saying taslim while standing, or by intending to enter the imam's prayer with takbir. The principle 'the majority has the ruling of the whole' (al-akthar lahu hukm al-kull) is used to justify cutting after sajdah in a non-4-rak'ah prayer. For the case of having prayed three rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah prayer, the ruling is different: he must complete it (i.e., pray the fourth rak'ah) and then follow the imam as a supererogatory performer (nafl), because he has performed the majority, and it is not valid to cut after three rak'ahs as that would be invalidating an obligatory action. The hadith of the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) is cited as evidence that one can make his prayer supererogatory (nafl) when joining the congregation. This passage clarifies the precise conditions under which cutting an individual fard is permissible, and emphasizes that the act of cutting is not a prohibited invalidation (ibṭāl manhiyy 'anhu) but rather a permitted or recommended action for the sake of obtaining congregational merit.

Key Terms
إدراك الفريضة (idrāk al-farīḍah): Realizing (catching) the obligatory prayer in congregation by joining the imam.
قطع (qaṭ‘): Discontinuing the current prayer with the intention to join the congregation.
متنفل (mutanaffil): One who performs a supererogatory (nafl) prayer; here, refers to completing the individual prayer as nafl after joining the congregation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person is alone in a four-rak'ah fard prayer and has performed sujud of the first rak'ah when the iqamah for the same fard is established. What should he do?
A) Cut immediately and join the congregation.
B) Add a second rak'ah, then cut and join.
C) Complete the entire prayer as four rak'ahs.
D) Continue and pray only two rak'ahs then join.

Key Takeaway
Cutting an individual fard to join the congregation is allowed under specific conditions, and when three rak'ahs have been completed in a four-rak'ah prayer, finishing the prayer becomes obligatory.

Completing a Four-Rak'ah Fard When Joining Congregation
Ruling with proof for completing fard when congregation starts after three rak'ahs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a person who has prayed three rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah fard when the congregation begins, and explain the proof from Quran and hadith.

Core Idea
Complete your fard if you have prayed the majority; then join the congregation as nafl — nullification with intention to complete is not nullification.

This lesson addresses a common scenario: you start a four-rak'ah fard prayer, but after three rak'ahs, the congregation for the same prayer begins. Should you cut your prayer and join? According to the Hanafi school, you must complete your fard first, then follow the imam as a supererogatory prayer. This ruling is based on the principle that the majority takes the ruling of the whole, and on the Quranic prohibition against nullifying deeds, which is not violated when the intention is to complete the act by joining.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario and the Hanafi ruling
The person has prayed three of four rak'ahs of a fard prayer; the congregation starts. Ruling: he must complete the fourth rak'ah as wajib, then join the congregation as nafl.
2
Identify the primary reasoning
The majority (three out of four) has the ruling of the whole (al-akthar lahu hukm al-kull). Cutting is nullification, but with the intention to complete by joining, it is not prohibited nullification.
Quranic prohibition: 'Do not nullify your deeds' (47:33).
3
Examine the Quranic proof
The verse forbids nullification. The Hanafi school interprets that nullification with the intention to complete the act (by joining the congregation) is not a violation because the act is being 'completed' through the second prayer.
The cutting is for a valid shar'i purpose.
4
Examine the hadith proof
The Prophet ﷺ said: 'If you have prayed in your dwellings and then come to a congregational prayer, pray with them and make your prayer with them a supererogatory prayer (sabha).' This proves that the second prayer is nafl, not a repetition of fard.
Hadith shows that one can join the congregation even after having already prayed at home.
5
Understand the consequence of non-compliance
If he cuts after three rak'ahs without completing, he sins because he has left the fard incomplete. The obligation to complete is wajib.
Wajib in Hanafi: omission is sinful but does not invalidate the act (if he cuts, his fard is void).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن صلى ثلاثاً منه يُتِمُّهُ ثُمَّ يقتدي متنفلاً؛ لأنه قد أدى الأكثر، وللأكثر حُكْمُ الكل. والقطع، وإن كان إبطالاً للعمل، وهو منهي، لقوله تعالى: وَلَا تُبْطِلُوا أَعْمَلَكُم، فالإبطال بقصد الإكمال لا يكون إبطالاً. وإن كان في الرباعي يَضُمُّ ركعة أخرى حتى يصير ركعتين نافلة، ثم يقطع ويقتدي. ويتمه وجوبا، فإن قطع أثم. ومتنفلاً؛ لأن الفرض لا يصلى مرتين. يدل عليه قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «إذا صليتما في رحالكما ثم أتيتما صلاة قوم فصليا معهم، واجعلا صلاتكما معهم سبحة».
And if he prayed three of it [the four-rak'ah prayer], he completes it then he follows [the imam] as a supererogatory worshipper; because he has performed the majority, and the majority has the ruling of the whole. And cutting [the prayer], even if it is nullifying the action, and it is prohibited by His saying: 'Do not nullify your deeds' (Quran 47:33), but nullification with the intention of completion is not nullification. And if he is in a four-rak'ah prayer, he adds another rak'ah until it becomes two rak'ahs of nafl, then he cuts and follows. He completes it as an obligation, for if he cuts he sins. And as a supererogatory worshipper because the obligatory prayer is not performed twice. This is supported by his saying, peace be upon him: 'If you have prayed in your dwellings and then you come to a congregational prayer, pray with them and make your prayer with them a supererogatory prayer (sabha).'
Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on al-Wiqayah deals with the ruling for a person who has started a four-rak'ah obligatory prayer and then a congregation begins after he has completed three rak'ahs. The ruling is that he must complete his fourth rak'ah, thus finishing his fard, and then join the congregation as a supererogatory worshipper. The reasoning is that he has performed the majority of his fard, and the majority takes the ruling of the whole. The text addresses a potential objection: cutting the prayer would be nullifying one's action, which is prohibited. However, nullification with the intention of completing the prayer by joining the congregation is not considered a prohibited nullification. For a four-rak'ah prayer, he adds one rak'ah to the three he has performed, making it two rak'ahs of nafl (since he already has three, adding one gives four, but the text says 'until it becomes two rak'ahs of nafl' meaning that after adding, the total becomes two pairs? The precise ruling is that he makes the three into a witr-like pair by adding one? Actually, the Hanafi position is that he should add one rak'ah to the three he has performed, then cut, and then join the congregation. The hadith proof: the Prophet told two men who had prayed at home and then came to the mosque to pray with the congregation and consider it a supererogatory prayer. This establishes that one can join as nafl.

Key Terms
متنفل (mutanaffil): One who performs a supererogatory (nafl) prayer.
الإبطال (al-ibṭāl): Nullification of a prayer, which is prohibited unless for a valid reason like joining congregation.
سبحة (sabḥah): Supererogatory prayer, synonymous with nafl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What should a person do if he has prayed three rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah fard and then the congregation begins?
A) Cut the prayer immediately and join the congregation.
B) Complete the fourth rak'ah as fard, then join the congregation as nafl.
C) Abandon the congregation and continue his fard alone.
D) Not join the congregation at all.

Key Takeaway
You must complete your fard if you have prayed most of it; then join the congregation as a supererogatory prayer.

Exception for Asr Prayer and Dislike of Nafl in Congregation
Exception and clarification of ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain when joining a congregation as nafl is prohibited (Asr) and when performing nafl in congregation is disliked (both are nafl) versus not disliked (imam is fard).

Core Idea
Joining as nafl in Asr is forbidden; nafl in congregation is only disliked when both imam and follower are doing nafl.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah clarifies two interconnected rulings: the exception for Asr prayer regarding joining a congregation as a nafl follower, and the general ruling on performing supererogatory prayers in congregation. It addresses a potential objection and provides a critical distinction based on the imam's intention. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying the rules of congregational prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Exception
The text begins 'Except in Asr' – the general permissibility of joining as nafl does not apply to Asr (and similarly Fajr) because performing nafl after these prayers is prohibited (makruh tahrimi).
This exception is well-known in the Hanafi school.
2
Understand the Reason for Prohibition
Nafl after Asr is disliked based on a hadith that implies staying in the mosque after adhan is important. The text cites: 'Whoever hears the adhan in the mosque, then leaves without a need and does not intend to return, he is a hypocrite.'
The hadith is weak but used as supporting evidence.
3
Recognize the Objection
A hypothetical objection is raised: joining as nafl in Asr would involve performing nafl in congregation, which is generally disliked.
The objection is based on a general ruling that nafl in congregation is disliked.
4
Analyze the Response and Distinction
The author responds by distinguishing the status of the imam. Dislike (karahah) applies only when both the imam and follower are performing nafl (mutatawwi'). When the imam is performing fard (muftarid), the follower's nafl is not disliked.
This distinction is from al-Binayah and is the relied-upon position.
5
Apply the Principle
Thus, one may join any fard congregation as nafl (except after Asr/Fajr) without dislike, provided the imam is performing fard. The ruling protects against the prohibition of nafl at certain times and avoids the dislike of nafl in congregation when both are nafl.
This principle applies to all prayers, not just Asr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إلا في العصر: أي لا يقتدي في العصر، فإن النافلة بعد أداء العصر مكروه. وكره (أي تحريماً)؛ لقوله: «من أدرك الأذان في المسجد، ثم خرج، لم يخرج لحاجة وهو لا يريد الرجوع فهو منافق». فإن قلت: يلزم أداء النفل بجماعة، وهو مكروه. قلت: الكراهة إنما هي إذا كان كل من الإمام والمؤتم متطوعين، وأما إذا كان الإمام مفترضاً فلا. كذا في «البناية»
Except in Asr: meaning do not follow [the imam] in Asr, for supererogatory prayer after performing Asr is disliked. And it is disliked (i.e., prohibitively disliked) because of his saying: 'Whoever hears the adhan in the mosque, then leaves without a need and does not intend to return, he is a hypocrite.' So if you say: this necessitates performing supererogatory prayer in congregation, which is disliked. I say: The dislike is only when both the imam and the follower are supererogatory worshippers. But when the imam is performing an obligatory prayer, it is not disliked. This is as stated in al-Binayah.
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage addresses two related issues. First, the exception for Asr prayer: the general rule that one who has started a fard may join the congregation as nafl applies to all prayers except Asr (and Fajr, as mentioned in the extended commentary) because performing supererogatory prayer after these times is prohibited due to the prophetic prohibition. Second, it responds to a potential objection: if one joins the congregation as nafl, he is performing nafl in congregation, which is generally disliked. The response clarifies that the dislike (karahah) applies only when both the imam and follower are performing nafl. Here, the imam is leading the fard prayer, so the follower's nafl is not disliked. This distinction is important for understanding the permissibility of joining as nafl in various contexts. The hadith cited (from Ibn Majah, though weak) emphasizes the importance of staying in the mosque after the adhan, reinforcing the ruling that one should not leave.

Key Terms
مكروه (makruh): Disliked; here it means prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi) for nafl after Asr, and disliked (makruh tanzih) for nafl in congregation when both are nafl.
متطوع (mutatawwi'): One performing a voluntary (nafl) prayer.
مفترض (muftarid): One performing an obligatory (fard) prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) When both the imam and follower are performing nafl.
B) When the imam is performing fard and the follower is performing nafl.
C) When it is after Asr prayer.
D) When the follower is performing fard.

Key Takeaway
Joining a congregation as nafl is not disliked when the imam is leading a fard prayer, except after Asr (and Fajr) where nafl is prohibited entirely.

Exception for Asr: When Joining a Nafl Congregation is Disliked
Commentary on ruling regarding nafl congregation after Asr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on joining a congregation for nafl after Asr and Fajr and identify the condition under which it is not disliked.

Core Idea
After Asr and Fajr, nafl is makruh; joining a nafl congregation then is also makruh unless the imam is performing fard.

You know that voluntary prayer after Asr and Fajr is disliked. But what if you arrive at the mosque and the imam is leading a prayer – can you join? This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah clarifies the ruling: generally, you should not join for a nafl after these times, but there is an important exception when the imam is performing an obligatory prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What specific action is being ruled upon? What is the hukm (legal classification)?
The act is joining a congregation (as a mu'tamm) for a voluntary prayer (nafl) after having performed Asr (or Fajr). The ruling is makruh tahrimi.
2
Locate the dalil
What evidence supports this ruling? Find the proof cited in the passage.
The passage cites the hadith in Sahihain that prohibits prayer after Asr and Fajr.
3
Apply the exception
When does the ruling change? Identify the condition that removes the dislike.
The dislike applies only when both the imam and the follower are performing voluntary prayers. If the imam is performing an obligatory prayer, it is not disliked.
4
Extend to other times
Does the same ruling apply to other prayer times? Note the extension to Fajr and Maghrib.
The same ruling applies to Fajr. For Maghrib, the apparent narration also prohibits joining due to the rak'ah count issue.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إلا في العصر وكره.
(إلا في العصر): أي لا يقتدي في العصر، فإنَّ النَّافلة بعد أداء العصر مكروه.
فإن قلت: يلزم أداء النفل بجماعة، وهو مكروه.
قلت: الكراهة إنما هي إذا كان كلّ من الإمام والمؤتم متطوعين، وأما إذا كان الإمام مفترضاً فلا. كذا في «البناية».
قوله: إلا في العصر؛ وكذا في الفجر؛ لأنَّ التنفّل بعد أدائهما مكروه؛ للنهي الوارد عن ذلك في الصحيحين وغيرهما. وكذا لا يقتدي في المغرب بعدما صلاه مرة في ظاهر الرواية؛ لأنه إن صلاه أربعاً صار مخالفاً لإمامه، وإن اكتفى على الثلاث صار متنفلاً بالثلاث، كما في «الهداية» وغيره.
Except in Asr and it is disliked. (Except in Asr): meaning he should not follow as a follower in Asr, because voluntary prayer after performing Asr is disliked. If you say: Performing voluntary prayer in congregation is necessary, and it is disliked. I say: Dislike is only when both the imam and the follower are volunteers, but if the imam is obligated, then no. Thus in al-Binaya. His statement: Except in Asr; and similarly in Fajr, because performing voluntary prayer after them is disliked due to the prohibition reported in the Sahihain and others. Similarly, he should not follow in Maghrib after having prayed it once in the apparent narration, because if he prays four rak'ahs he becomes contrary to his imam, and if he is satisfied with three he becomes a volunteer with three, as in al-Hidaya and others.
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with explanation from the commentator on why one should not join a congregation for voluntary prayer in specific times. The main text states an exception for Asr. The commentator explains that joining a congregation for a voluntary prayer is disliked when both imam and follower are performing voluntary prayers, but if the imam is performing an obligatory prayer, it is not disliked. However, after Asr and Fajr, voluntary prayer itself is disliked due to authentic hadith, so one cannot join for a voluntary prayer even if the imam is obligatory. The same applies to Maghrib in the apparent narration, because if one prays four rak'ahs he would be opposing the imam, and if he prays three it becomes a voluntary prayer of three rak'ahs, which is not a valid voluntary format. The commentator cites al-Binaya and al-Hidaya as sources.

Key Terms
النَّافلة (al-nafl): Voluntary supererogatory prayer
المؤتم (al-mu'tamm): The person following the imam in congregation

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is one prohibited from joining a congregation for nafl after Asr?
A) Because nafl after Asr is makruh
B) Because the imam must be doing fard
C) Because it is not allowed to pray in congregation for nafl at any time
D) Because the follower becomes a volunteer

Key Takeaway
The ruling on joining a congregation for nafl after Asr and Fajr is makruh, but this dislike is conditional on both imam and follower performing voluntary prayer.

Leaving Mosque After Adhan: Ruling and Exceptions
Ruling on leaving mosque after adhan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on leaving the mosque after the adhan without praying, cite the evidence, and list the exceptions where it is not disliked.

Core Idea
Leaving after adhan without a valid reason is prohibitively disliked—it resembles hypocrisy.

The Hanafi school considers leaving the mosque after the call to prayer without a valid reason a serious matter. This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya explains the ruling and its exceptions. Understanding when it is permissible requires careful attention to the evidence and the definition of the exceptional categories.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Pinpoint the act in question: leaving the mosque after the adhan without having prayed. Note that the ruling is 'makruh tahrimi' (prohibitively disliked).
The commentator explicitly states 'meaning tahriman'.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof cited: the hadith from Ibn Majah and the report from Sahih Muslim about Abu Hurairah's statement.
The hadith labels such a person a hypocrite, indicating the severity.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Understand how the hadith proves the ruling: the explicit comparison to hypocrisy shows that the act is forbidden and a grave sin.
In Hanafi usul, such a strong condemnation indicates karahah tahrimiyyah.
4
Identify the exceptions
Read the passage to find when leaving is not disliked: for those establishing another congregation (muqim) and for a legitimate need with intention to return.
The commentator explains that 'muqim' includes the imam, muezzin, or anyone whose absence would harm the congregation.
5
Note the scope
Recognize that the ruling applies regardless of whether the person was present in the mosque at the time of adhan or entered afterward.
The commentator says 'its absolute form indicates that the ruling includes whether he was in the mosque when the adhan was made, or it was made before his entry.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكره.
قوله: وكره؛ أي تحريماً؛ لقوله: «من أدرك الأذان في المسجد، ثم خرج، لم يخرج لحاجة وهو لا يريد الرجوع فهو منافق»، أخرجه ابن ماجة.
وعن أبي الشعثاء قال: «كنا قعوداً في المسجد مع أبي هريرة فأذن المؤذن، فقام رجل من المسجد يمشي فأتبعه أبو هريرة بصره حتى خرج من المسجد، فقال أبو هريرة: أما هذا فقد عصى أبا القاسم» في صحيح مسلم.
خروج مَن لم يُصَلِّ من مسجد أُذُنَ فيه لا لمقيم جماعة أخرى: أي لِمَن ينتظم به أمر جماعةٍ أُخرى بأن يكون مؤذن مسجد، أو إمامه، أو من يقوم بأمرِ جماعة يتفرقون، أو يقلون بغيبته.
ثُمَّ عَطَفَ على قوله: لا لمقيم جماعة أخرى قوله: وأخرج أصحاب السنن الأربعة ومسلم عن أبي هريرة أنه قال لرجل خرج من المسجد بعدما أذن فيه: «أما هذا فقد أبا القاسم عصى».
قوله: خروج؛ وكذا يكره المكث في المسجد بدون الشركة في الصلاة. كذا في «البحر».
قوله: أذن فيه؛ على صيغة المجهول، والجملة صفة لمسجد، وهو بإطلاقه يفيد أن الحكم شامل لما إذا أذن فيه وهو في المسجد، أو أذن قبل دخوله فيه.
قوله: لا لمقيم؛ أي لا يكره الخروج من مسجد بعد الأذان لمقيم جماعة أُخرى في غير هذا المسجد، وليس المراد به الذي يتكلم بألفاظ الإقامة، بل من ينتظم به أمر الجماعة الأخرى كما أشار إليه الشارح بتفسيره، فيدخل فيه إمام الجماعة الأخرى والمؤذن والمقيم، والذي بحضوره هناك تكثر الجماعة، وتقل عند غيبته، وإنما لم يكره الخروج لهؤلاء؛ لأنه ليس فيه إعراض عن الجماعة، ولا ترك للصلاة، بل تكميل لها، وكذا لا يكره الخروج لحاجة، ومن عزمه أن يعود إليه. كذا في «النهر».
قوله: لمقيم؛ الظاهرُ حذفُ اللام؛ لكونه معطوف على من لم يصل، ولعلّه أظهر اللام؛ لكونه مقدراً في الإضافة السابقة.
And it is disliked. His statement: And it is disliked; meaning tahriman; because of his saying: 'Whoever catches the adhan in the mosque, then leaves, not leaving for a need while not intending to return, is a hypocrite,' narrated by Ibn Majah. And from Abu al-Sha'tha: 'We were sitting in the mosque with Abu Huraira, then the mu'adhdhin called the adhan, so a man stood up from the mosque walking, and Abu Huraira followed him with his gaze until he left the mosque, then Abu Huraira said: As for this one, he has disobeyed Abu al-Qasim.' in Sahih Muslim. Leaving of one who has not prayed from a mosque in which the call to prayer has been made, except for one establishing another congregation: that is, for one who arranges the affair of another congregation, such as the mu'adhdhin of a mosque, or its imam, or one who undertakes the matter of a congregation that would disperse or decrease by his absence. Then he attached to his statement: except for one establishing another congregation, his statement: And the authors of the four Sunan and Muslim narrated from Abu Huraira that he said to a man who left the mosque after the adhan: 'As for this one, he has disobeyed Abu al-Qasim.' His statement: Leaving; and similarly it is disliked to remain in the mosque without participating in the prayer. Thus in al-Bahr. His statement: in which the call was made; in passive voice, and the clause is an adjective for mosque, and its absolute form indicates that the ruling includes whether he was in the mosque when the adhan was made, or it was made before his entry. His statement: except for one establishing; meaning it is not disliked to leave a mosque after the adhan for one establishing another congregation in another mosque, and what is meant is not the one who utters the words of iqama, but rather one who arranges the affair of another congregation as the commentator indicated by his interpretation. This includes the imam of another congregation, the mu'adhdhin, and the muqim, and one whose presence there increases the congregation, and who decreases by his absence. And it is not disliked for such persons to leave because there is no turning away from the congregation nor abandoning of prayer, but rather completion of it. Similarly, it is not disliked to leave for a need with the intention to return. Thus in al-Nahr. His statement: for one establishing; apparently the lam is omitted because it is coordinated with 'one who has not prayed,' and perhaps he made the lam apparent because it is implied in the previous idafa.
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the dislike of leaving the mosque after the adhan without praying. The main text 'And it is disliked' is explained by the commentator as meaning tahriman (prohibitively disliked), based on the hadith that such a person is a hypocrite. The additional heading 'Leaving of one who has not prayed from a mosque in which the call to prayer has been made, except for one establishing another congregation' specifies the exception: those who are needed to establish another congregation elsewhere, such as the muezzin, imam, or anyone whose absence would cause the congregation to diminish. The commentator elaborates that the ruling applies whether the person was in the mosque at the time of adhan or entered after. He also notes that it is not disliked to leave for a legitimate need with the intention to return. The sources cited include al-Bahr and al-Nahr. The practical takeaway is that leaving without a valid reason is a serious offense akin to hypocrisy, but exceptions are made for those fulfilling a greater communal obligation.

Key Terms
المقيم (al-muqim): One who establishes another congregation, typically the person who recites the iqama or arranges the congregation
الكراهة التحريمية (al-karahah al-tahrimiyyah): Prohibitively disliked; a sin but not as severe as haram

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition is it not disliked to leave the mosque after the adhan?
A) If one leaves to establish another congregation elsewhere
B) If one leaves without any reason
C) If one leaves after praying
D) If one leaves for a worldly need without intending to return

Key Takeaway
Leaving the mosque after adhan without praying is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi), except for legitimate purposes such as establishing another congregation or a genuine need with intention to return.

Leaving the Mosque After the Adhan: Ruling and Exceptions
Explains when leaving mosque after adhan is makruh or permissible

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on leaving the mosque after the adhan and identify the exceptions for those who have already prayed and those needed for another congregation.

Core Idea
Leaving after adhan without excuse is makruh tahrimi, except for congregation organizers and before iqamah for those who already prayed.

This lesson explores a detailed ruling from the Hanafi school concerning the proper etiquette after the adhan. While the general rule is that leaving the mosque is discouraged, the text outlines important exceptions based on one's role and prior prayer status, demonstrating the school's nuanced approach to balancing individual choice and communal obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Ruling
Find the core ruling: it is makruh (disliked) for a person who has not yet prayed to leave the mosque after the adhan, unless an exception applies.
The commentator uses the phrase 'قبيح جداً' (extremely ugly), indicating makruh tahrimi.
2
Locate the First Exception
The text excepts those who are needed to establish another congregation, such as the imam or mu'adhdhin of another mosque. For them, leaving is not disliked even at iqamah.
This exception is based on preventing harm to another group.
3
Locate the Second Exception
The second exception is for one who has already prayed Zuhr or 'Isha once. Such a person may leave without dislike, except when the iqamah is called.
At iqamah, leaving becomes disliked due to suspicion of opposing the congregation.
4
Understand the Distinction
Explain the rationale: the organizer of another congregation brings benefit to others, so leaving is not disliked. The one who already prayed, if he leaves at iqamah, appears to be avoiding the congregation, and staying gives him supererogatory reward.
This distinction is based on the principle of preventing suspicion and maximizing benefit.
5
Examine the Proof
The primary evidence is the hadith where Abu Hurayra said of a man leaving after adhan: 'This one has disobeyed Abu al-Qasim (ﷺ).' The strong censure indicates prohibition, leading to the ruling of makruh tahrimi.
The dalil is ahad but considered strong enough for this ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة/ إدراك الفريضة

خروج مَن لم يُصَلِّ من مسجد أُذِنَ فيه لا لمقيم جماعة أخرى
[٤] خروج من لم يُصَلِّ من مسجد أُذِنَ فيه لا لمقيم جماعة أخرى: أي لِمَن ينتظم به أمر جماعةٍ أُخرى بأن يكون مؤذن مسجد، أو إمامه، أو من يقوم بأمرِ جماعة يتفرقون أو يقلون بغيبته.
ثُمَّ عَطَفَ على قوله: لا لمقيم جماعة أخرى قوله: ولمن صلي الظهر أو العشاء مرة إلا عند الإقامة.

ولمن صلي الظهر أو العشاء مرة إلا عند الإقامة: أي لا يُكْرَه له الخروج إلا عند الإقامة، فالاستثناء متعلّق بقولِهِ: ولِمَن صلَّى الظهر أو العشاء، ولا تعلق له بقوله: لا لمقيم جماعة أخرى، فإن مقيم الجماعةِ الأُخرى لا يُكْرَهُ له الخروج وإن أقيمت، والفرق بين مقيم جماعة وبين مَن صلَّى الظهر أو العشاء مرة: أنَّ هذا إنما يُكْرَهُ له الخروج؛ لأنه إن خرج بعد الإقامة يتهم بمخالفة الجماعة، ولو لم يخرج ويصلي يَحُوزُ فضيلة الموافقة وثواب النافلة، فإيثار التهمة والإعراض عن الفضيلة والثَّواب قبيح جداً.
[۱] قوله: ولمن صلّى؛ أي لا يكره الخروج من المسجد بعد الأذان لِمَن صلى الظهر أو العشاء وحده أو بجماعة في مسجد آخر أو بيته؛ لأنه قد أجاب داعي الله وهو المؤذن مرة، ولم يوجد منه الإعراض، وأما الإعادة بالجماعة متنفلاً فليس بواجب، بل هو مخير فيه.
[٢] قوله: إلا عند الإقامة؛ المراد بها: شروع المؤذن في الإقامة، كما في الهداية وغيرها، وظاهره أنه يكره له الخروج عند ذلك وإن كان ممن ينتظم به أمر جماعة أخرى. كذا في رد المحتار نقلاً عن الشيخ إسماعيل شارح الدرر شرح الغرر.
[٣]وله: ولا تعلّق له؛ أي ليس هو منصرفاً إلى قوله: لا لمقيم جماعة أخرى؛ فإنّ مَن ينتظم به أمرها لا يكره له الخروج مطلقاً لا عند الأذان ولا عند الإقامة، وهذا إذا لم يكن صلى، فإن كان قد صلّى وحده يكره له الخروج عند الإقامة كما حققه اسماعيل النابلسي في شرح الدرر.
[٤] قوله: والفرق؛ حاصله أنّ الفرق بين مقيم الجماعةِ الأخرى وبين مَن صلَّى الظهر والعشاء مرة حيث لا يكره للأوّل الخروج عند الإقامة ويكره للثاني: أن من صلى مرة إن خرج عند الإقامة يكون متهماً بمخالفة الجماعة، وإن لم يخرج ويصلّي في الجماعة يجد ثوابَ النافلة وفضيلة الجماعة، ففي عدم خروجه وشركته نفع من دون ضرر، وفي الخروج ضرر من دون نفع؛ فلذا كره له الخروج، وأما مقيم الجماعة الأخرى فليس في خروجه اتهام، وفي شركته ضرر من حيث تفرّق الجماعة الأخرى، فلا يكره له الخروج مطلقاً.
Book of Prayer / Realizing the Obligatory Prayer

The ruling on leaving the mosque for one who has not prayed, from a mosque in which the call to prayer has been made, except for one who establishes another congregation:
[4] 'Leaving for one who has not prayed from a mosque in which the call has been made, except for one who establishes another congregation': i.e., for one whose presence organizes another congregation, such as a mu'adhdhin of a mosque, or its imam, or one who manages the affair of a congregation that would disperse or decrease without him.
Then He appended to His saying: 'except for one who establishes another congregation' His saying: 'And for one who has prayed Zuhr or 'Isha once, except at the time of iqamah.'
[PAGE_244]
'And for one who has prayed Zuhr or 'Isha once, except at the time of iqamah': i.e., it is not disliked (makruh) for him to leave except at the time of iqamah. So the exception is related to His saying: 'And for one who has prayed Zuhr or 'Isha', and it has no connection to His saying: 'except for one who establishes another congregation'. Indeed, the one who establishes another congregation is not disliked to leave even if the iqamah has been made. The difference between the one who establishes a congregation and the one who has prayed Zuhr or 'Isha once is that the latter is only disliked to leave because if he leaves after iqamah he is suspected of opposing the congregation, and if he does not leave and prays, he obtains the virtue of agreement and the reward of the supererogatory prayer. So preferring suspicion and turning away from virtue and reward is extremely ugly.
[1] His saying: 'And for one who has prayed': i.e., it is not disliked to leave the mosque after the adhan for one who has prayed Zuhr or 'Isha alone or with a congregation in another mosque or his home, because he has already answered the caller of Allah, the mu'adhdhin, once, and no turning away has occurred on his part. As for repeating the prayer in congregation as a supererogatory act, it is not obligatory; rather he has a choice.
[2] His saying: 'except at the time of iqamah': what is meant by it is the commencement of the mu'adhdhin in the iqamah, as in Al-Hidayah and others. Its apparent meaning is that it is disliked for him to leave at that time even if he is one who organizes another congregation. Thus in Radd al-Muhtar, quoting from Shaykh Isma'il, commentator of Durar Sharh al-Ghurarr.
[3] His saying: 'And it has no connection': i.e., it is not referring to His saying: 'except for one who establishes another congregation'; indeed, one who organizes it is not disliked to leave absolutely, neither at the adhan nor at the iqamah. This is if he has not prayed; if he has prayed alone, it is disliked for him to leave at the iqamah, as verified by Isma'il al-Nabulsi in Sharh al-Durar.
[4] His saying: 'And the difference': its summary is that the difference between the one who establishes another congregation and the one who has prayed Zuhr and 'Isha once, where the former is not disliked to leave at the iqamah and the latter is disliked, is that the one who prayed once, if he leaves at the iqamah, he is suspected of opposing the congregation, and if he does not leave and prays in the congregation, he obtains the reward of the supererogatory prayer and the virtue of congregation. So in his not leaving and his participation there is benefit without harm, and in his leaving there is harm without benefit. Therefore his leaving is disliked. As for the one who establishes another congregation, there is no suspicion in his leaving, and in his participation there is harm in terms of the dispersal of the other congregation, so his leaving is not disliked absolutely.
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This is an expansion (sharh) of a matn from Al-Wiqayah regarding the ruling on leaving the mosque after the adhan. The passage first states the general ruling: it is disliked (makruh) for a person who has not yet prayed to leave the mosque after the adhan is called, unless he is someone whose presence is necessary to organize another congregation — such as the imam or mu'adhdhin of another mosque. This is because his departure would cause harm to another jama'ah. Then the text adds an exception for those who have already prayed Zuhr or 'Isha once: for them, leaving is not disliked except at the time of iqamah. The commentator clarifies that this exception is not linked to the earlier exception for the organizer of another congregation; rather it is a separate category. The distinction is that the organizer of another congregation is never disliked to leave (whether at adhan or iqamah) because his leaving benefits another congregation. However, the one who has already prayed once — if he leaves at iqamah, he may be suspected of neglecting the congregation, and by staying he gains the virtue of joining the congregation in supererogatory prayer. Therefore his leaving at iqamah is disliked. The text also notes that if the one who has prayed alone leaves before iqamah, it is not disliked. The proof for the general ruling is a hadith from Abu Hurayra (may Allah be pleased with him) who said regarding a man leaving after adhan: 'This one has disobeyed Abu al-Qasim (ﷺ).' The commentary provides the precise conditions and exceptions, showing the nuanced Hanafi approach that balances benefit and harm. The relied-upon position (al-mufta bihi) is as stated: the general dislike for leaving after adhan unless one is needed for another congregation, and the specific dislike at iqamah for those who have already prayed once.

Key Terms
أذن (adhana): The call to prayer (adhan) that signals the beginning of the obligatory prayer time.
إقامة (iqamah): The second call that immediately precedes the beginning of the prayer, announcing its imminent commencement.
كراهة (karahah): Legal dislike; an act that is discouraged but not prohibited. In this text, it likely refers to makruh tahrimi (prohibited dislike) due to the strong language used.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling for a person who has prayed Zuhr alone at home and then enters a mosque where the iqamah is being called for Zuhr congregation?
A) It is disliked for him to leave the mosque at that time.
B) It is permissible for him to leave without any dislike.
C) It is recommended for him to leave to avoid crowding.
D) It is obligatory for him to stay and pray with the congregation.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that leaving the mosque after adhan is generally makruh tahrimi, with exceptions for those needed for another congregation and those who have prayed, except at iqamah.

Ruling on Leaving Mosque at Iqamah After Praying: Zuhr/Isha vs. Fajr/Asr/Maghrib
Commentary on rulings for leaving mosque after Zuhr/Isha vs. Fajr/Asr/Maghrib at iqamah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi ruling for leaving the mosque at iqamah after Zuhr/Isha (makruh tanzih) from after Fajr/Asr/Maghrib (ja'iz and awla), and explain the roles of avoiding accusation (tuhmah) and the hadith on disliked nafl.

Core Idea
The ruling on leaving at iqamah depends on whether staying leads to virtue or to a disliked act.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah clarifies a nuanced Hanafi ruling: leaving the mosque when the iqamah is called is not always the same. For Zuhr and Isha, leaving is disliked because it suggests avoiding the congregation. For Fajr, Asr, and Maghrib, leaving is permissible and even superior to avoid performing a disliked nafl prayer. Understanding this distinction requires balancing the principle of avoiding accusation (tuhmah) with the textual prohibition of nafl after certain prayers. The passage also addresses an exception for those establishing another congregation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage distinguishes between (1) one who has prayed Zuhr or Isha once, and (2) one who has prayed Fajr, Asr, or Maghrib. Note that the ruling differs for each.
2
State the default ruling for each scenario
For Zuhr/Isha: it is disliked (makruh tanzih) to leave at the time of iqamah. For Fajr/Asr/Maghrib: it is permissible (ja'iz) and even superior (awla) to leave.
The exception for muqim jama'ah will be handled later.
3
Understand the rationale for Zuhr/Isha
The ruling is based on avoiding accusation (tuhmah). If one leaves at iqamah, he may be suspected of avoiding the congregation. Staying allows him to gain the virtue of congregation and extra reward.
This is a rational (ma'qul) basis, not a direct textual command.
4
Understand the rationale for Fajr/Asr/Maghrib
If one stays and prays with the congregation, it would be a nafl prayer. However, nafl after Fajr and Asr is explicitly disliked by hadith. The passage extends this to Maghrib (though the hadith is specific to Fajr/Asr, the same principle applies because nafl after Maghrib is also considered disliked). Therefore, leaving avoids this disliked act.
The hadith cited: 'There is no prayer after Fajr until the sun rises, nor after Asr until the sun sets.' (Bukhari, Muslim)
5
Recognize the exception: muqim jama'ah
One who is establishing another congregation (e.g., imam or necessary member) is not disliked to leave even at iqamah, because his departure serves the greater good of that other congregation.
This exception applies regardless of which prayer was performed.
6
Note the intra-Hanafi nuance for Fajr/Asr/Maghrib
Al-Nahr suggested leaving might be obligatory (wajib) because staying without prayer is more severely disliked. However, al-Hidayah (Mukhtarat al-Nawazil) holds that leaving is superior (awla), and this is the preponderant (rajih) view.
The mufta bihi is that it is awla, not wajib.
