Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling of making up missed prayers. It begins by stating that from the Prophet's action in the hadith of al-Ta'ris (where he slept through Fajr and then made it up with congregation, adhan, iqama, and reciting aloud), several rulings are derived: the permissibility of making up a missed obligatory prayer in congregation, reciting aloud, and performing adhan and iqama for the qada, and that the sunnah of Fajr is also made up along with the fard. The commentator then explains that these rulings are not limited to Fajr alone; rather, they are generalized to all missed obligatory prayers through qiyas (analogy). However, an exception is made regarding the sunnah: the ruling that the sunnah is made up applies only to the sunnah of Fajr, not to the sunnahs of other prayers. This is because the sunnah of Fajr has a special emphasis (ta'kid) compared to other sunnahs. The commentator further delves into the reasoning: the obligation of qada for fard prayers is established by textual evidence, whereas for sunnah prayers, there is no such general evidence. The sunnahs are originally voluntary and do not occupy the dhimmah like obligations; hence, they are not necessarily made up unless specific evidence exists, and such evidence exists only for the sunnah of Fajr due to its high status.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada'): Making up a missed prayer after its prescribed time has passed.
سُنَّة (sunnah): A recommended act that is not obligatory; specifically the regular sunnah prayers (rawatib).
تعريس (ta'ris): The story of the Prophet and his companions oversleeping and missing Fajr prayer on a journey.
تعدية (ta'diyya): Extension of a ruling from a specific case to other cases via qiyas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the sunnah of Fajr made up but not other sunnahs?
A) Because the hadith mentioned only the Fajr sunnah and did not mention others.
B) Because the sunnah of Fajr is more emphasized (akdad) than other sunnahs.
C) Because other sunnahs are not obligatory, while the Fajr sunnah is wajib.
D) Because the Prophet himself only made up the Fajr sunnah.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school generalizes the qada rulings from the hadith of al-Ta'ris to all fard prayers, but restricts the qada of sunnah to the Fajr sunnah alone due to its special emphasis.

The Specificity of Qada for the Fajr Sunnah
Commentary on qada of sunnah, focusing on Fajr specificity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that qada of sunnah prayers is only prescribed for the Fajr sunnah in the Hanafi school and explain the proof from hadith.

Core Idea
Only the Fajr sunnah is made up because of its unique emphasis; other sunan have no qada.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling that the qada (make-up) of missed sunnah prayers is limited to the Fajr sunnah. The passage explains that this specificity is based on the sunnah's high status and a specific hadith, not on a general principle extending to all supererogatory acts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
What does the text say about qada of sunnah prayers? Which sunnah is singled out for qada? The ruling is that only the Fajr sunnah is made up after its time.
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
Find the hadith cited: 'Pray it even if the horses trample you' (أخرجه أبو داود). How does this hadith prove the high status of Fajr sunnah?
The imperative 'صلوها' indicates emphasis, and the fact that the Prophet never left it shows it is muakkadah.
3
Understand the refutation of time restriction
The text rejects the view that qada of Fajr sunnah is only before zawal. Why? Because qada is not time-specific; before and after zawal are equally not the original time.
The argument: 'لا اختصاص للقضاء بوقت دون وقت' – qada is not restricted to a particular time.
4
Apply the principle
If a person misses the Fajr sunnah and later prays Fajr fard, they should also pray the Fajr sunnah after it, even after zawal. This is the mufta bihi position.

And as for the qada of the sunnah, it is known that the sunnah of Fajr is more emphasized than other sunan, so the legality of its qada does not necessitate the legality of qada of other sunan, nor does its qada following the obligatory prayer necessitate its qada without the obligatory prayer. It is known that it is not specific; meaning the legality of qada or every ruling of the mentioned rulings is specific to the text's subject, which is the Fajr prayer: meaning when he made up Fajr in this manner, and it is known that these rulings are not specific to one prayer over another, and there is no reason for their specificity to some, so it is known that qada and likewise every ruling of these rulings is general, including all obligatory prayers. So it was transferred; passive from transfer; meaning he transferred the ruling of legality of qada from it, meaning from the subject of the text, to other than it, meaning the Fajr prayer, from the prayers, meaning the obligatory ones like Isha, Maghrib, and others, except the qada of the sunnah; the pronoun refers to the rulings. And it is [1] His statement: 'And as for the qada of the sunnah...etc.'; its summary: that the rulings mentioned in the story of the night of al-Ta'reef are general except for the qada of the sunnah, for it is specific to the sunnah of Fajr; and that is because analogy requires that its qada is not necessary; because if qada is obliged due to a new cause, then the qada of every supererogatory act depends on a scriptural proof, and there is no proof indicating the qada of every sunnah, just as a scriptural proof came for the qada of the obligatory and mandatory. And if it is obliged due to the previous cause as is the madhhab of the verifying scholars of principles, then its determination: that when the liability is occupied and its discharge is demanded in a specific time and it is missed, the cause remains demanding discharge according to capacity; because the disengagement of liability after its occupation is not realized except by release from the one who has the right or by performance, and this is absent in the sunan, because there is no occupation of liability in them, rather they are demanded on a basis of choice, initially in the manner he did, so when it becomes impossible, its demand does not remain, so by this determination the specificity of qada to the wajib is established. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. When you know this, then know that it came in the hadith of al-Ta'reef about the qada of the sunnah of Fajr with the obligatory prayer before zawal, and the establishment of its qada does not necessitate the establishment of qada of other sunan; because the sunnah of Fajr is more emphasized than other sunan, until it was said that it is obligatory; due to the hadith: 'Pray it even if the horses trample you', narrated by Abu Dawud and others. And it is not transmitted from the Prophet that he left it, neither in residence nor travel, and the establishment of qada of the more emphasized does not necessitate the establishment of qada of the lesser, and likewise the legality of its qada with the obligatory prayer does not necessitate the legality of its qada alone; because often a ruling is established for something by way of following, and is not established for it independently, and the establishment of the first does not necessitate the establishment of the other, unless a specific scriptural proof indicates that. [1] His statement: 'But' is a rebuttal to what might be said: Since the matter in the chapter of sunnah is restricted to what is reported, and it is known that what is reported about the sunnah of Fajr is only its qada before zawal, then it would necessitate that it is not made up with the obligatory prayer after zawal, as is the madhhab of some mashayikh. [2] His statement: 'has no meaning' meaning there is no apparent justification for restricting the qada of the sunnah of Fajr with the obligatory prayer to before zawal; for what is before and after are equal in both being other than the time of performance, and qada is not specific to one time over another. [3] His statement: 'in both situations' means whether he fears missing the congregation of Zuhr or does not fear, and that is due to the general meaning of the hadith: 'When the prayer is established, there is no prayer except the obligatory one', narrated by the authors of the Sahihs and Sunan. [4] His statement: 'before its shaf' (even number); this is according to Abu Yusuf, and according to Muhammad he precedes the two rak'ahs, as mentioned in some commentaries of al-Jami' al-Saghir and others, and some mention the disagreement.
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the ruling of making up (qada) sunnah prayers. It clarifies that the general ruling of qada for obligatory prayers does not automatically apply to sunnah prayers, based on the story of the night of al-Ta'reef (a journey of the Prophet where he made up Fajr sunnah after its time). The author argues that the qada of the Fajr sunnah is specific to that sunnah because of its high emphasis, and does not extend to other sunan by analogy. The text then discusses the sunnah of Zuhr when one joins the congregation: one should abandon the sunnah for the obligatory prayer, then make it up after the fard but before the shaf' (the two rak'ahs of sunnah after Zuhr). There is an intra-Hanafi difference: Abu Yusuf holds that one makes it up before the shaf', while Muhammad says one should do the two rak'ahs first, then make up the missed sunnah. The author also refutes the view that the qada of Fajr sunnah is only valid before zawal, arguing that qada is not time-specific. The passage uses hadith proofs: 'Pray it even if the horses trample you' for emphasis on Fajr sunnah, and 'When the prayer is established, there is no prayer except the obligatory one' for abandoning the sunnah when the congregation starts.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada'): Making up a missed prayer after its prescribed time.
سنة (sunnah): A recommended act of worship that was regularly performed by the Prophet, but not obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for not extending qada to other sunnah prayers?
A) Because other sunnan are not emphasized
B) Because there is a specific hadith for Fajr sunnah and no proof for others
C) Because qada is only for obligatory prayers
D) Because the Prophet never made up other sunnan

Key Takeaway
Only the Fajr sunnah is made up after its time, due to its unique emphasis and specific hadith; qada is not time-specific.

Order of Making Up the Zuhr Sunnah: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Commentary on the ruling for making up Zuhr sunnah when joining congregation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on the order of making up the Zuhr sunnah when joining the congregation, distinguishing the views of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Core Idea
When joining congregation, leave the Zuhr sunnah, then after fard make it up before the shaf' according to Abu Yusuf, but after the shaf' according to Muhammad.

This lesson addresses a practical scenario: a person arrives at the mosque and finds the Zuhr congregation already started. They must abandon the sunnah to join the fard. After the fard, should they make up the missed Zuhr sunnah first or perform the two rak'ahs of shaf' first? The Hanafi school has an intra-madhhab disagreement between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A person comes to the mosque and the Zuhr iqamah is being called. They have not yet prayed the sunnah of Zuhr. Should they pray the sunnah or join the congregation? The text says they leave the sunnah in both situations (whether they fear missing the congregation or not).
Based on the hadith 'When the prayer is established, there is no prayer except the obligatory one'.
2
Determine the order after fard
After completing the fard in congregation, the person has two missed sunan: the pre-fard sunnah of Zuhr (2 rak'ahs) and the post-fard shaf' (2 rak'ahs). In what order should they pray? The text presents two opinions.
3
State the view of Abu Yusuf
Abu Yusuf holds that the missed pre-fard sunnah should be made up before the shaf' (i.e., pray 2 rak'ahs sunnah, then 2 rak'ahs shaf').
His reasoning: the pre-fard sunnah is more connected to the fard and should be prioritized.
4
State the view of Muhammad
Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that one should first perform the shaf' (the two rak'ahs after fard) and then make up the missed pre-fard sunnah.
His reasoning: the shaf' is more emphasized (some say obligatory) and should be done first.
5
Note the tarjih
The text does not explicitly prefer one view, and both are within the Hanafi school. It is a legitimate ikhtilaf. The mufta bihi may depend on the local practice.

قبل الزوال وجه ؛ فإنّ ما قبله وما بعده سواسيان في كونهما غير وقت الأداء، والقضاء لا يختص بوقت دون وقت.
[٣] قوله في الحالين؛ أي سواء خافَ فوت جماعة الظهر أو لم يخف، وذلك

لعموم حديث: «إذا أقيمت الصلاة فلا صلاة إلا المكتوبة»(۳)، أخرجه أصحاب الصحاح والسنن.
[٤] قوله : قبل شفعه ؛ هذا عند أبي يوسف الله ، وعند محمد له يقدم الركعتين ، كذا ذكر اختلافهما في بعض شروح الجامع الصغير وغيره، ومنهم من ذكر الخلاف
(1) أي حال إدراك ركعة من الظهر وحال عدم إدراكها. ينظر : كمال الدراية»(ق۱۰۹). (۲) في سنن أبي داود (۱) : (٤٠٣ ، و مشكل الآثار» (۹) : (۱۲۷) ، و(مسند أحمد»(٢ : ٤٠٥)، وغيرها.

٢٨٢)، وغيرها.
And as for the qada of the sunnah, it is known that the sunnah of Fajr is more emphasized than other sunan, so the legality of its qada does not necessitate the legality of qada of other sunan, nor does its qada following the obligatory prayer necessitate its qada without the obligatory prayer. It is known that it is not specific; meaning the legality of qada or every ruling of the mentioned rulings is specific to the text's subject, which is the Fajr prayer: meaning when he made up Fajr in this manner, and it is known that these rulings are not specific to one prayer over another, and there is no reason for their specificity to some, so it is known that qada and likewise every ruling of these rulings is general, including all obligatory prayers. So it was transferred; passive from transfer; meaning he transferred the ruling of legality of qada from it, meaning from the subject of the text, to other than it, meaning the Fajr prayer, from the prayers, meaning the obligatory ones like Isha, Maghrib, and others, except the qada of the sunnah; the pronoun refers to the rulings. And it is [1] His statement: 'And as for the qada of the sunnah...etc.'; its summary: that the rulings mentioned in the story of the night of al-Ta'reef are general except for the qada of the sunnah, for it is specific to the sunnah of Fajr; and that is because analogy requires that its qada is not necessary; because if qada is obliged due to a new cause, then the qada of every supererogatory act depends on a scriptural proof, and there is no proof indicating the qada of every sunnah, just as a scriptural proof came for the qada of the obligatory and mandatory. And if it is obliged due to the previous cause as is the madhhab of the verifying scholars of principles, then its determination: that when the liability is occupied and its discharge is demanded in a specific time and it is missed, the cause remains demanding discharge according to capacity; because the disengagement of liability after its occupation is not realized except by release from the one who has the right or by performance, and this is absent in the sunan, because there is no occupation of liability in them, rather they are demanded on a basis of choice, initially in the manner he did, so when it becomes impossible, its demand does not remain, so by this determination the specificity of qada to the wajib is established. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. When you know this, then know that it came in the hadith of al-Ta'reef about the qada of the sunnah of Fajr with the obligatory prayer before zawal, and the establishment of its qada does not necessitate the establishment of qada of other sunan; because the sunnah of Fajr is more emphasized than other sunan, until it was said that it is obligatory; due to the hadith: 'Pray it even if the horses trample you', narrated by Abu Dawud and others. And it is not transmitted from the Prophet that he left it, neither in residence nor travel, and the establishment of qada of the more emphasized does not necessitate the establishment of qada of the lesser, and likewise the legality of its qada with the obligatory prayer does not necessitate the legality of its qada alone; because often a ruling is established for something by way of following, and is not established for it independently, and the establishment of the first does not necessitate the establishment of the other, unless a specific scriptural proof indicates that. [1] His statement: 'But' is a rebuttal to what might be said: Since the matter in the chapter of sunnah is restricted to what is reported, and it is known that what is reported about the sunnah of Fajr is only its qada before zawal, then it would necessitate that it is not made up with the obligatory prayer after zawal, as is the madhhab of some mashayikh. [2] His statement: 'has no meaning' meaning there is no apparent justification for restricting the qada of the sunnah of Fajr with the obligatory prayer to before zawal; for what is before and after are equal in both being other than the time of performance, and qada is not specific to one time over another. [3] His statement: 'in both situations' means whether he fears missing the congregation of Zuhr or does not fear, and that is due to the general meaning of the hadith: 'When the prayer is established, there is no prayer except the obligatory one', narrated by the authors of the Sahihs and Sunan. [4] His statement: 'before its shaf' (even number); this is according to Abu Yusuf, and according to Muhammad he precedes the two rak'ahs, as mentioned in some commentaries of al-Jami' al-Saghir and others, and some mention the disagreement.
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the ruling of making up (qada) sunnah prayers. It clarifies that the general ruling of qada for obligatory prayers does not automatically apply to sunnah prayers, based on the story of the night of al-Ta'reef (a journey of the Prophet where he made up Fajr sunnah after its time). The author argues that the qada of the Fajr sunnah is specific to that sunnah because of its high emphasis, and does not extend to other sunan by analogy. The text then discusses the sunnah of Zuhr when one joins the congregation: one should abandon the sunnah for the obligatory prayer, then make it up after the fard but before the shaf' (the two rak'ahs of sunnah after Zuhr). There is an intra-Hanafi difference: Abu Yusuf holds that one makes it up before the shaf', while Muhammad says one should do the two rak'ahs first, then make up the missed sunnah. The author also refutes the view that the qada of Fajr sunnah is only valid before zawal, arguing that qada is not time-specific. The passage uses hadith proofs: 'Pray it even if the horses trample you' for emphasis on Fajr sunnah, and 'When the prayer is established, there is no prayer except the obligatory one' for abandoning the sunnah when the congregation starts.

Key Terms
شفع (shaf'): The two rak'ahs of sunnah after the obligatory Zuhr prayer, considered more emphasized.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for leaving the Zuhr sunnah when joining the congregation?
A) The hadith 'Pray it even if the horses trample you'
B) The hadith 'When the prayer is established, there is no prayer except the obligatory one'
C) The principle that sunnah is always inferior to fard
D) The consensus of the companions

Key Takeaway
When joining the Zuhr congregation, leave the sunnah; after fard, Abu Yusuf says make up the sunnah before shaf', Muhammad says shaf' first.

Making Up Missed Sunnah of Zuhr After Joining the Congregation
Hashiyah discussing the ruling of making up missed sunan prayers when catching the congregational fard.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to STATE the ruling for leaving the sunnah of zuhr when the iqamah is called, and APPLY the preferred Hanafi position regarding the order of making up the qabliyyah and ba'diyyah.

Core Idea
When the congregation begins, abandon the sunnah and join the imam; then make it up after the fard, preferably after the ba'diyyah.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah clarifies a common scenario: you arrive for zuhr and the iqamah is called. Should you quickly pray the sunnah or join the congregation? The answer is clear, but what about making up that sunnah later? The Hanafi school provides a detailed ruling with an intra-madhhab dispute on the order of making up the qabliyyah and ba'diyyah. This lesson will walk you through the ruling, its evidence, and the preferred practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary ruling: leaving the sunnah when iqamah is called
The text states that one leaves the sunnah in both situations (whether he fears missing the congregation or not) and follows the imam. The dalil is the hadith prohibiting any prayer except the obligatory after the iqamah.
2
Understand the scope of making up missed sunnah
After the fard, one makes up the missed sunnah. The text specifies that this applies to the emphasized sunnan (fajr and zuhr qabliyyah). Other sunnan (maghrib, isha, etc.) are not made up at all, neither alone nor as a follow-up.
3
Recognize the intra-Hanafi dispute on the order
Abu Yusuf says to make up the qabliyyah before the ba'diyyah (shaf'). Muhammad says to pray the ba'diyyah first, then make up the qabliyyah. The same dispute applies for a person who catches only one rak'ah alone (mudrik)
4
Determine the preferred view and its evidence
The text considers Muhammad's view as sahih for the alone scenario, and later authorities like Ibn al-Humam (al-Fath) and al-Durr al-Mukhtar rely on it for both scenarios. The reasoning: the qabliyyah's time has passed, so it becomes a nafl mubtada', and the ba'diyyah should be performed in its established time.
5
Note the exceptions: other sunnan are not made up
The text states that sunan other than fajr and zuhr qabliyyah (e.g., sunnah of maghrib, ba'diyyah of zuhr itself) are not made up at all, even as a follow-up, according to the sahih opinion.

(1) This according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and in the Mabsoot of Shaykh al-Islam it is the sahih..., and likewise in Jami' Qadi Khan, and in Fath Bab al-Inayah (1:356): 'It is the mu'tamad.' And he proceeds accordingly in Tuhfat al-Muluk (p. 86). The second opinion is that he prays before the two rak'ahs after zuhr, and this is the saying of Muhammad, because when its time was missed, it became a nafl mubtada', so he begins with the two rak'ahs so that its time does not pass, as in al-Tabyeen (1:183), and in al-Durr al-Mukhtar (1:483): 'The fatwa is given accordingly,' and Ibn Abidin said in his Hashiyah (1:483): 'And the texts are upon it.' In al-Fath (1:415) he preferred presenting the two rak'ahs. He said in al-Imdad: And in Fatawa al-Atabi it is the chosen. [1] His statement: 'and other than these two': i.e., other than the sunnah of fajr and the sunnah of zuhr qabliyyah: like the sunnah of maghrib and the two rak'ahs of zuhr (ba'diyyah). [2] His statement: 'is not made up at all': al-Hidayah (1:479) and al-Binayah (2:612) said: As for other sunan, they are not made up alone; i.e., when they are without the fard, and the mashayikh differed regarding making them up as a follow-up to the fard: some said they are made up as a follow-up, because many things are established by implication and not intentionally. And some said they are not made up as a follow-up, just as they are not made up intentionally, and this is the sahih. [3] His statement: 'of zuhr': the restriction is incidental, for the ruling is likewise in asr and isha.
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage from the hashiah 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah' comments on 'Sharh al-Wiqayah' regarding the ruling on making up missed sunnah prayers when one catches the congregational fard prayer. The author begins by stating that when the congregation for zuhr is established, one should leave the sunnah (the qabliyyah) in both situations—whether one fears missing the congregation or not—and follow the imam. After the fard, one should make up the missed sunnah before the shaf' (the two rak'ahs of ba'diyyah sunnah). This is the position of Abu Yusuf. Muhammad holds that one should pray the ba'diyyah first, then make up the qabliyyah. The text then discusses a rebuttal to those who argue that the sunnah of fajr can only be made up before zawal, showing that such a limitation has no basis. It cites the hadith 'When the iqamah is called, there is no prayer except the obligatory' to justify leaving the sunnah when the congregation starts. For the sunnah of fajr, the hadith 'Pray them even if the horses trample you' indicates its emphasis. The text then rules that other sunnah prayers (like sunnah of maghrib and the ba'diyyah of zuhr) are not made up at all if missed, neither alone nor as a follow-up to the fard. This is the sahih opinion. For a person who catches one rak'ah of zuhr alone (not with the congregation), Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that he should make up the qabliyyah after the ba'diyyah, while Muhammad says he should pray the qabliyyah before the ba'diyyah. The preferred opinion is Muhammad's, as supported by a hadith from Aisha. The restriction to zuhr is incidental; the same applies to asr and isha.

Key Terms
سنَّة الظهر القبلية (sunnat al-zuhr al-qabliyyah): The two rak'ahs sunnah prayed before the fard of zuhr.
شفع (shaf'): The two rak'ahs after the fard of zuhr (the ba'diyyah sunnah).
مدرك ركعة (mudrik rak'ah): A person who catches at least one rak'ah of the congregational prayer.
قضاء (qada'): Making up a prayer after its designated time has passed.
تبعية (taba'iyyah): Performing the missed sunnah as a follow-up (taba'an) to the fard prayer, typically immediately after the fard.
سنن مؤكدة (sunan muakkadah): Emphasized sunnah prayers that the Prophet consistently performed and encouraged.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, when a person catches the zuhr congregation after the iqamah, what should he do after completing the fard with the congregation?
A) He should not pray any additional prayers, as all sunnah are prohibited.
B) He should make up the missed sunnah of zuhr, but only if he catches the full congregation.
C) He should make up the missed sunnah of zuhr, and the preferred order is to pray the ba'diyyah first, then the qabliyyah.
D) He should make up the missed sunnah of zuhr, and he must pray the qabliyyah before the ba'diyyah.

Key Takeaway
When the congregation is established, leave the sunnah and join; after the fard, make it up by first praying the ba'diyyah, then the qabliyyah.

Ruling on Making Up Missed Sunnah for a Latecomer in Zuhr
Clarifying the ruling on a mudrik who catches one rak'ah of zuhr regarding sunnah prayers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whether a mudrik who catches one rak'ah of zuhr makes up the pre-zuhr sunnah, and distinguish between the views of Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad.

Core Idea
A mudrik does not make up the pre-zuhr sunnah individually; he prays the post-zuhr sunnah first.

When a person joins the congregation late (mudrik) and catches only one rak'ah of Zuhr, a question arises: after completing the fard, should he make up the missed pre-zuhr sunnah? The Hanafi school has two views. This lesson examines the relied-upon position supported by the narrations of the Sahibayn and a hadith from Aisha.

Guided Path
1
Identify the mudrik and what they have missed
The passage defines a mudrik as someone who catches at least one rak'ah of the congregation but not the entire prayer. In this case, the mudrik catches one rak'ah of zuhr. He is not considered to have prayed in congregation but attains its virtue.
The ruling applies also to asr and isha according to the text.
2
State the primary ruling (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf)
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, the mudrik does not make up the pre-zuhr sunnah individually. He should pray the two rak'ahs of post-zuhr sunnah first. If he wishes to make up the missed pre-zuhr sunnah, he does so after the post-zuhr sunnah, but it is not required.
This is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) view.
3
Note the opposing view (Imam Muhammad)
Imam Muhammad holds that the mudrik should pray the pre-zuhr sunnah before the post-zuhr sunnah because once its time is lost, it becomes a new nafl prayer that should not be delayed.
The passage mentions this view and attributes it to Imam Muhammad.
4
Identify the dalil and how it supports the primary view
The passage cites a hadith narrated by al-Tirmidhi from Aisha: 'When he misses the four rak'ahs before zuhr, he makes them up after the two rak'ahs.' This indicates that the pre-zuhr sunnah, if missed, is made up after the post-zuhr sunnah, supporting the opinion that the post-zuhr sunnah takes precedence.
The hadith is zanni in transmission and meaning, but it is used as supporting evidence.

Source Text

وغيرهما لا يقضي أصلاً. ومدرك ركعة من ظهر غير مصل جماعة، بل هو مدرك فضلها. قوله: وغيرهما أي غير سنة الفجر وسنة الظهر القبلية كسنة المغرب وركعتي الظهر. قوله: لا يقضي أصلاً قال في الهداية والبناية أما سائر السنن فلا تقضى وحدها أي إذا كانت بدون الفريضة واختلف المشايخ في قضائها تبعاً للفرض فقال بعضهم يقضيها تبعاً لأنه كم من شيء يثبت ضمناً ولا يثبت قصداً وقال بعضهم لا يقضيها تبعاً كما لا يقضيها مقصودة وهو الأصح. قوله: من ظهر التقييد به اتفاقي فإن الحكم في العصر والعشاء أيضاً كذلك. هذا على قول أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف وفي مبسوط شيخ الإسلام أنه الأصح، وكذا في جامع قاضي خان وفي فتح باب العناية: وهو المعتمد. ومشى عليه في تحفة الملوك. والقول الثاني أنه يصلي قبل الركعتين بعد الظهر وهو قول محمد لأنه لما فات محلها صارت نفلاً مبتدأ فيبدأ بالركعتين كي لا يفوت محلها كما في التبيين، وفي الدر المختار: يفتى به وقال ابن عابدين في حاشيته: وعليه المتون، ورجح في الفتح تقديم الركعتين قال في الإمداد وفي فتاوى العتابي أنه المختار. ويشهد له ما روى الترمذي عن عائشة أنه إذا فاتته الأربع قبل الظهر قضاها بعد الركعتين.
And other than them, he does not make up at all. And the one who catches one rak'ah of zuhr is not someone who prayed in congregation, but he attains its virtue. His statement: 'other than them' means other than the sunnah of fajr and the pre-zuhr sunnah, like the sunnah of maghrib and the two rak'ahs of zuhr. His statement: 'does not make up at all' — said in al-Hidayah and al-Binayah: As for the other sunnahs, they are not made up individually, i.e., if they are without the obligatory prayer. And the scholars differed about making them up as a follower of the obligatory prayer: some said he makes them up as a follower because many things are established implicitly and not explicitly. And some said he does not make them up as a follower, just as he does not make them up intentionally, and this is the more correct. His statement: 'of zuhr' — the restriction is incidental, for the ruling applies to asr and isha as well. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and in Mabsut of Shaykh al-Islam it is the more correct, and likewise in Jami' Qadi Khan, and in Fath Bab al-Inayah it is the relied upon. And he acted upon it in Tuhfat al-Muluk. The second opinion is that he prays before the two rak'ahs after zuhr, and it is the view of Muhammad, because when its time was missed, it becomes a new nafl, so he begins with the two rak'ahs so that their time does not pass, as in al-Tabyin, and in al-Durr al-Mukhtar: fatwa is given with it, and Ibn Abidin said in his hashiyah: and the texts are upon it, and in al-Fath he preferred giving precedence to the two rak'ahs, and said in al-Imdad and in Fatawa al-Atabi that it is the chosen. And it is supported by what al-Tirmidhi narrated from Aisha: 'When he misses the four before zuhr, he makes them up after the two rak'ahs.'
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling of a latecomer (mudrik) who catches one rak'ah of zuhr congregation. The passage clarifies that such a person is not considered to have prayed in congregation but attains its virtue. The main issue is among scholars about making up missed sunnah prayers. The passage presents two positions: The first, attributed to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, is that he does not make up the missed pre-zuhr sunnah individually or even as a follower of the farḍ prayer, because it has lost its prescribed time; rather, he should pray the post-zuhr sunnah first. This is considered the more correct and relied-upon view. The second opinion, attributed to Imam Muhammad, is that he should pray the pre-zuhr sunnah before the two post-zuhr rak'ahs, because once its time is lost it becomes a new optional prayer that should be performed without delay. The passage also cites a hadith from Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) as supporting the first view: when one misses the four rak'ahs before zuhr, he makes them up after the two (post-zuhr sunnah). The discussion shows the internal Hanafi ikhtilaf and the resolution favoring Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf's position.

Key Terms
مدرك (mudrik): A person who joins the congregation after the imam has started but catches at least one rak'ah of the prayer.
قضاء (qada'): Performing a missed prayer outside its prescribed time, whether obligatory or sunnah.

Oath Broken by Catching Only One Rak'ah in Congregation
Explaining when an oath to pray in congregation is broken by catching only one rak'ah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why catching only one rak'ah in congregation does not fulfill an oath to pray in congregation, and state the ruling that the oath is broken.

Core Idea
Catching one rak'ah does not count as praying in congregation for oath fulfillment because the majority of the prayer was performed individually.

This lesson examines a specific case in Hanafi fiqh concerning oaths related to congregational prayer. When a person swears to pray zuhr in congregation but only catches a single rak'ah with the imam, the oath is considered broken. We will explore the reasoning behind this ruling and the distinction between the legal obligation of the oath and the virtue of congregation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the oath and its condition
The person swore to pray zuhr in congregation. The condition of the oath is to perform the entire prayer with the congregation.
An oath is a solemn promise to perform a specific action. The condition is determined by the wording and intention.
2
Determine what constitutes 'praying in congregation'
According to the Hanafi school, praying in congregation means performing the majority of the prayer with the imam. For a 4-rak'ah prayer like zuhr, the majority is three rak'ahs. Catching only one rak'ah means three are done individually.
The majority rule is based on the principle that the ruling of the majority applies to the whole.
3
Apply the ruling to the scenario
Since the person performed only one rak'ah with the congregation and three individually, the majority of the prayer was not in congregation. Therefore, he is not considered to have prayed in congregation, and the oath is broken.
Breaking the oath (hanth) triggers the obligation of expiation (kaffarah).
4
Note the nuance of virtue
Despite breaking the oath, the person still attains the virtue (fadilah) of congregation for the one rak'ah he caught, based on the hadith 'Whoever catches a rak'ah has caught the prayer.'
The virtue of congregation is separate from the legal fulfillment of the oath.
5
Conclude the legal consequence
The oath is broken (hanth), requiring expiation (kaffarah) as per the rules of oaths. The person must fast three days or feed ten poor people, etc.
Expiation is necessary because the oath was not fulfilled as sworn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وآتي مسجد صلي فيه، يتطوع قبل الفرض إلا عند ضيق الوقت أي إن حلف ليُصَلِيَنَّ الظَّهْرَ جماعة، فأدرك ركعة يحنث لأنه لم يصل جماعة، لكن أدرك فضيلة الجماعة.
And one who comes to a mosque where prayer was performed, he performs voluntary prayer before the obligatory except when time is restricted. That is, if he swore to pray zuhr in congregation and he caught one rak'ah, he breaks his oath because he did not pray in congregation, but he attained the virtue of congregation.
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage clarifies a specific case: if a person swears an oath that he will pray zuhr in congregation, but then he catches only one rak'ah with the imam and completes the rest alone, the oath is considered broken. The reason is that the majority of the prayer (three rak'ahs) was performed individually, and the ruling of the majority applies to the whole. Therefore, he is not considered to have prayed in congregation. However, he does receive the reward of congregation for the one rak'ah he caught, as indicated by the hadith about catching a rak'ah. This ruling emphasizes the precision of legal consequences in oaths.

Key Terms
حنث (hanth): Breaking an oath, requiring expiation (kaffarah).
جماعة (jama'ah): Congregational prayer, typically performed with an imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does a person who swore to pray zuhr in congregation break his oath if he catches only one rak'ah?
A) Because he missed the intention of congregation.
B) Because the majority of his prayer was performed individually.
C) Because he did not gain any virtue of congregation.
D) Because he cannot catch the full prayer.

Key Takeaway
An oath to pray in congregation is broken if the majority of the prayer is performed individually; catching only one rak'ah does not fulfill the oath.

Performing Sunnah Prayers When Praying Alone: The Hanafi Intra-School Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sunnah performance when alone

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi views on performing sunnah prayers when praying alone, and identify the mufta bihi position with its rationale.

Core Idea
The sunnah prayers remain recommended even when alone, as they complete the farḍ—precaution outweighs conditional emphasis.

What should you do when you arrive at the mosque after the congregation has finished? Should you still pray the confirmed sunnah prayers (rawatib) before or after the farḍ? The Hanafi school has two positions. This lesson explains the dispute and shows why the preferred view is to perform them, because they are complements to the obligatory prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
Understand the situation: a person comes to a mosque and finds that the congregational prayer has already ended. He intends to pray the farḍ alone. The question is whether he should also pray the sunnah rawatib.
This is not about praying in congregation; it's about praying alone.
2
State the Two Hanafi Positions
Position A (al-Kirmani): Do not pray the sunnah, because their emphasis was based on the Prophet's practice in congregation. Position B (Hasan ibn Ziyad, preferred): Pray them, because they are completions (mukammilat) for the farḍ.
The difference is whether the sunnah's ta'kid (emphasis) is conditional on congregation.
3
Analyze the Proof for Each View
For position A: The Prophet only consistently performed sunnah when he prayed with congregation. Therefore, when alone, the strong recommendation is lifted. For position B: The general texts on rawatib do not make congregation a condition; the sunnah completes the farḍ irrespective.
The Hanafi principle: 'al-asl baqa' ma kana 'ala ma kana' – the original ruling continues unless evidence changes it.
4
Evaluate the Tarjih (Preference)
The text says the view of performing the sunnah is 'al-ashahh' (more correct) and 'ahwat' (most precautionary). Precaution (ihtiyat) is a strong basis in Hanafi tarjih when proofs are balanced.
Mufta bihi: perform the sunnah prayers, following Hasan ibn Ziyad.
5
Determine the Practical Consequence (Thamarah al-Khilaf)
In practice, the person praying alone is advised to pray the sunnah. If he omits it, his prayer is still valid, but he loses the virtue. The dispute only affects whether the sunnah is still 'mu'akkadah' (emphasized) in this case.
Even those who say do not pray consider it permissible, not disliked.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: بالسنن أي بالسنن المؤكدة الرواتب القبلية والبعدية. قوله: لا أي لا يأتي بالسنن، فإنها إنما سنت إذا أدى الفرض بالجماعة، فإن النبي إنما واظب عليها عند أداء الصلاة بالجماعة، فلا يؤديها إذا أدى الفرض منفرداً أي لا يلزم عليه ذلك، ولا تبقى السنن مؤكدة في حقه، وليس معناه أنه يكره له ذلك، فإن الصلاة خير موضوع فمن شاء فليقلل ومن شاء فليكثر إلا أن يقوم دليل شرعي كما في الصلاة في الأوقات المكروهة ونحوها. قوله: أن يأتي بالسنن لكونها مكملات للفرائض، سواء أداها بالجماعة أو منفرداً، وهو الأحوط.
His statement: 'the sunnah' i.e., the confirmed sunnah prayers before and after. His statement: 'no' i.e., he does not perform the sunnah prayers, because they are prescribed only when he performs the obligatory prayer in congregation; the Prophet only consistently performed them when he performed the prayer in congregation, so he does not perform them if he performs the obligatory prayer alone. That is, it is not required of him, and the sunnahs are not confirmed for him. It does not mean that it is disliked for him, for prayer is a good act; whoever wishes may decrease and whoever wishes may increase, unless a legal proof prohibits, such as prayer at disliked times and similar. His statement: 'he performs the sunnah prayers' because they are completions for the obligatory prayers, whether one performs them in congregation or alone, and this is more precautionary.
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether one should perform the confirmed sunnah prayers (rawatib) when he comes to a mosque after the congregation has already finished and intends to pray the farḍ alone. One view, attributed to al-Kirmani, holds that he should not pray them because the sunnah prayer's emphasized nature (ta'kid) was established based on the Prophet's regular practice when praying in congregation; when praying alone, the emphasis drops. However, this does not mean it is disliked, but rather it is simply not required. The other view, from Hasan ibn Ziyad, and considered the preferred (al-ashahh), is that he should still pray them because they are complements to the farḍ and the texts do not differentiate between congregational and individual performance. This is also the more cautious approach.

Key Terms
سنن مؤكدة (sunan mu'akkadah): Confirmed sunnah prayers that the Prophet consistently performed, such as the rawatib before and after farḍ prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He should not pray any sunnah prayers because they were only prescribed for congregation.
B) He should pray the sunnah prayers because they are completions for the farḍ.
C) He should pray only the post-farḍ sunnah and skip the pre-farḍ.
D) He should avoid praying altogether to avoid innovation.

Key Takeaway
The preferred Hanafi view is to perform the sunnah prayers even when praying alone, as they are completions for the farḍ, and this is the more cautious position.

Performing Sunan Before Fard When Entering a Mosque with Congregation
Ruling on sunnah prayers when entering a mosque where congregation was held

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on performing sunnah prayers when entering a mosque after the congregation and identify the exception of tight time.

Core Idea
The sunnah prayers are prescribed even when praying alone; only time constraint justifies their omission.

When you enter a mosque and find the congregation has already finished, you may wish to pray your obligatory prayer alone. A natural question arises: should you perform the regular sunnah prayers before it? Hanafi scholars have differed, but the relied-upon view is that you should pray the sunnah unless you fear missing the obligatory prayer's time. This lesson examines the evidence, the intra-madhhab dispute, and the practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is performing the sunnah (rawatib) before the fard when one enters a mosque after the congregation. The ruling is that it is sunnah muakkadah, i.e., confirmed voluntary practice.
The ruling applies to anyone, whether praying alone or in congregation, except when time is tight.
2
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some Hanafi scholars (e.g., al-Kur) held that the sunnah is only prescribed when performing the fard in congregation; others (al-Hasan ibn Ziyad) said one should begin with the fard. Understand the basis of each view.
This ikhtilaf is resolved by the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position.
3
Understand the tarjih and its evidence
The relied-upon position (al-ahwat) is to perform the sunnah, as supported by al-Tanwir, Ibn Abideen, and al-Zayla'i. The evidence is that the sunnah was prescribed generally to complete the fard and the Prophet adhered to them regardless of congregation.
The exception of tight time is based on the principle that preserving the obligatory prayer's time is more important.
4
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Consider a case where a person has ample time: he should perform the sunnah first. If time is tight (fear of missing the fard), he should omit the sunnah and pray the fard immediately.
The key condition for skipping the sunnah is 'dīq al-waqt' (constrained time).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

فإنَّ النَّبي واظب عليها (۱)۱) ، فإن فاتته الجماعةُ لكن إذا ضاق الوقت يتركُ السُنَّةَ ويؤدِّي الفرض حذراً عن التفويت.
And one who comes to a mosque in which prayer was offered, he may perform voluntary prayer before the obligatory except when time is constrained. That is, if he swore to pray Zuhr in congregation, and he caught one rak'ah, he breaks his oath because he did not pray in congregation, but he attained the virtue of congregation. (And one who comes to a mosque in which prayer was offered, he may perform voluntary prayer before the obligatory except when time is constrained): Meaning, someone who comes to a mosque in which prayer was offered, and he wants to pray his obligatory prayer alone, does he perform the sunan? Some of our scholars, among them al-Kur, said: No, because the sunnah was only prescribed when one performs the obligatory prayer in congregation, otherwise not. And al-Hasan ibn Ziyad said: One who misses the congregation and wants to pray in his home mosque should begin with the obligatory. But the most correct is that he should perform the sunan. His statement: 'that is, if he swore...' indicates that mentioning this issue in this context is to clarify the ruling on another issue mentioned in al-Jami' al-Kabir and elsewhere. His statement: 'he breaks his oath' means he is violating his oath, not fulfilling it, because the condition of fulfillment is that he prayed Zuhr with the imam, but he prayed three rak'ahs alone, because the latecomer is alone in what he makes up, and the majority has the ruling of the whole, so he breaks his oath and owes expiation. His statement: 'but he attained the virtue of congregation' means the reward of congregation, based on the hadith: 'Whoever catches one rak'ah of the prayer has caught the prayer', reported by the authors of the Sahih and Sunan. His statement: 'by the sunan' means the confirmed regular sunan before and after. His statement: 'No' means he does not perform the sunan, because they were only prescribed when one performs the obligatory with congregation. The Prophet (PBUH) only adhered to them when performing prayer in congregation, so he should not perform them when praying alone. That is, it is not binding on him, and the sunan are not confirmed for him. It does not mean it is disliked for him to do so, for prayer is a good act; whoever wishes may do little, and whoever wishes may do much, except if a legal proof indicates otherwise, like prayer at disliked times. His statement: 'that he should perform the sunan' because they complete the obligatory prayers, whether performed in congregation or alone. And it was corrected by the author of al-Tanwir, and approved by Ibn Abideen in his gloss on al-Durr al-Mukhtar, and al-Zayla'i said in al-Tabyin: It is more cautious, because they were prescribed before the prayer to cut off the hope of the devil from the worshiper, and after it to compensate for any deficiency that may occur in the obligatory, and the one who prays alone is more in need of that. The text concerning them does not differentiate, so it applies generally, except if one fears missing the time, because performing the obligatory in its time is obligatory. (It is in Sahih Muslim and Sahih al-Bukhari, etc.) Indeed, the Prophet (PBUH) adhered to them. However, if one misses the congregation, but if time is tight, he abandons the sunnah and performs the obligatory, fearing loss of the time.
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage deals with a person who enters a mosque where the congregation has already been held and wishes to pray the obligatory prayer alone. The issue is whether he should pray the sunnah (regular voluntary prayers) before the obligatory or skip them. The author presents a difference of opinion among Hanafi scholars. Some, like al-Kur, hold that the sunnah is only prescribed when one prays with the congregation, so it should not be performed when praying alone. Others, like al-Hasan ibn Ziyad, say one should begin with the obligatory. However, the relied-upon position (al-ahwat) is that one should perform the sunnah, because the sunan are prescribed to complete the obligatory prayers, and the texts do not differentiate between congregational and individual prayer. The exception is when time is tight: if performing the sunnah would cause one to miss the obligatory prayer's time, then the sunnah is abandoned and the obligatory prayer is prioritized. The passage also includes a related sub-issue about a person who swore an oath to pray Zuhr in congregation and then only caught one rak'ah. According to the hadith 'Whoever catches a rak'ah...', he is considered to have caught the prayer in terms of reward, but for the oath, he is deemed to have broken it because he did not complete the prayer with the imam from the start. Thus, he must expiate his oath.

Key Terms
سنن (sunan): The regular voluntary prayers (rawatib) before and after the obligatory prayers.
جماعة (jama'ah): Congregational prayer performed with an imam.
ركعة (rak'ah): A unit of prayer consisting of standing, bowing, and prostrations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what should a person do if he enters a mosque where the congregation has already been held and wants to pray the obligatory prayer alone?
A) He should skip the sunnah and pray the obligatory immediately.
B) He should perform the sunnah before the obligatory unless he fears missing the time.
C) He should leave the mosque and pray elsewhere.
D) He should wait for the next congregation.

Key Takeaway
The sunnah prayers are prescribed before the fard even when praying alone, but they must be omitted if performing them would cause one to miss the obligatory prayer's time.

Catching a Rak'ah When Following an Imam in Ruku'
Ruling on catching a rak'ah when joining an imam in ruku'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi majority view on catching a rak'ah when joining an imam in ruku', explain the intra-Hanafi dispute with Imam Zufar, and apply the condition of participation in an actual action to similar scenarios.

Core Idea
To catch a rak'ah behind an imam, you must actually bow with him — mere presence or intent is not enough.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in congregational prayer: joining an imam who is already in ruku'. The Hanafi school holds that the follower must physically perform ruku' with the imam to earn that rak'ah. However, Imam Zufar, a prominent Hanafi, disagrees. We will explore the evidence and the underlying principle of participation in action (musharaka fi al-fi'l). Understanding this clarifies a fundamental rule of iqtida'.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi majority position
Identify what the majority of Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) rule regarding the latecomer who stands still during the imam's ruku'.
The ruling is that he does not catch that rak'ah.
2
Identify the dissenting view (Zufar)
State Imam Zufar's position and his reasoning: that ruku' has the ruling of standing because the lower half is straight, so standing still counts as participation.
Zufar's view is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Analyze the majority's evidence
Examine the hadith cited and the condition that following requires participation in an actual action (fi'l) of prayer, not just intention or resemblance.
The hadith: 'When you come to prayer while we are prostrating, prostrate, and do not count it as anything. Whoever catches the rak'ah (i.e., ruku') has caught the prayer.'
4
Compare the two positions and determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence of the disagreement: what happens if the latecomer stands still?
Under the majority, he misses the rak'ah and must make it up. Under Zufar, he catches it and no makeup is needed.
5
Note the tarjih (preferred view)
Establish which view is relied upon for fatwa and why.
The majority view is mufta bihi, supported by the hadith and the principle of actual participation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من اقتدى بإمام راكع فَوَقَفَ حَتَّى رَفَعَ رأسه لم يدرك ركعته) ، خلافاً لزُفَر . منفرداً.
[١] قوله : واظب عليها، فتركها من غير ضرورة موجب للملامة لقول ؛ ابن مسعود : ولو تركتم سنة نبيكم لضللتم»، أخرجه مسلم.
[٢]قوله : لكن إذا ضاق ؛ أي بقى من الوقت ما لو أدّى فيه السنن فات فرضه.
[٣) قوله : من اقتدى بإمام راكع ؛ بأن وصل إليه وهو راكع، فكبر للافتتاح مقتدياً به ووقف ولم يركع، سواء تمكن من الركوع أو لا حتى رفع الإمام رأسه لا يدرك تلك الركعة، خلافاً لزفـر الله ، فإنّه يقول : أدرك الإمام فـيـمـا لـه حكـم الـقـيـام وهـو الركوع ؛ ؛ لمشابهته للقيام من وجه ؛ لوجودِ استواء النصف الأسفل فيه.
ولنا : إنَّ الشرط في صحة الاقتداء هو المشاركة في فعل من أفعال الصلاة، ولم توجد لا في القيام ولا في الركوع ومجرّد المشاركة لا يكفي، ويؤيده حديث: «إذا جئتم إلى الصلاة ونحن سجود فاسجدوا ، لا تعدوها شيئاً، ومن أدرك الركعة ـ أي الركوع . فقد أدرك الصلاة ) ، فإن إدراك الركوع إنما يكون إذا ركع مع الإمام، وهو مخرج في «سنن أبي داود» وغيره، تفصيله مع ما له وما عليه في رسالتي : «إمام الكلام فيما يتعلّق بالقراءة خلف الإمام».
One who follows an imam who is bowing (in ruku') and then stands still until the imam raises his head: he does not catch that rak'ah, contrary to Zufar. (He prays alone?) His statement: 'He adhered to them' — leaving them without necessity is blameworthy due to the saying of Ibn Mas'ud: 'If you abandon the sunnah of your Prophet, you will go astray' — reported by Muslim. His statement: 'But if time is tight' means that if there remains only enough time that if he performs the sunnah, his obligatory prayer would be missed. His statement: 'Who follows an imam who is bowing' — meaning he arrives while the imam is bowing, he says the takbir to begin, following the imam, and stands still and does not bow, whether he is able to bow or not, until the imam raises his head — he does not catch that rak'ah, contrary to Zufar, may Allah have mercy on him. He says: He caught the imam in something that has the ruling of standing, namely bowing, because it resembles standing in one respect: the lower half is straight. Our argument: The condition for the validity of following is participation in one of the actions of prayer, and it is not found either in standing or in bowing; mere intent to participate is not sufficient. This is supported by the hadith: 'When you come to prayer while we are prostrating, prostrate, and do not count it as anything. Whoever catches the rak'ah — i.e., the bowing — has caught the prayer.' Catching the bowing is only when he bows with the imam. This hadith is reported in Sunan Abi Dawud and others. The detailed discussion with supporting and opposing evidence is in my treatise 'Imam al-Kalam fima Yata'allaq bi al-Qira'ah Khalf al-Imam'.
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage addresses the scenario where a person joins the congregation while the imam is already in ruku' (bowing). The person makes the opening takbir and stands still without bowing, waiting perhaps for the imam to come up. The ruling is that he does not catch that rak'ah, even if he intended to bow later. This is the Hanafi position. The dissenting opinion comes from Imam Zufar, a Hanafi scholar, who argues that since the imam is in ruku' and the lower half of the body is straight like standing, it can be considered akin to standing, and thus the latecomer has participated in the imam's posture. However, the majority Hanafi view rejects this. The key point is that valid following requires actual participation in a physical action of prayer (qiyam, ruku', sujud). Here, the latecomer did not perform ruku' with the imam, nor did he stand in qiyam with the imam (since the imam was in ruku'). Mere intention or being present is insufficient. The hadith cited supports this: when companions came to the prayer while the Prophet was in sujud, they were told to prostrate and not count that as a rak'ah. Similarly, catching the rak'ah is achieved only when one actually bows with the imam. Thus, the latecomer should join the imam in ruku' immediately and then follow. If he delays, he misses that rak'ah and must make it up later.

Key Terms
اقتداء (iqtida'): Following the imam in congregational prayer.
ركعة (rak'ah): A unit of prayer; in this context, it refers to the ruku' component as the key to earning the rak'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling if a person joins the imam while the imam is in ruku', but the latecomer stands still until the imam raises his head?
A) He catches that rak'ah because the imam was in ruku'.
B) He does not catch that rak'ah and must make it up later.
C) His prayer becomes invalid because he did not follow the imam.
D) He should perform the rak'ah alone after the imam completes the prayer.

Key Takeaway
To catch a rak'ah behind an imam, you must actually perform ruku' with him; standing still, even with intention, does not count.

Catching the Rak'ah in Congregational Prayer: Conditions and Dispute
Ruling on catching the rak'ah with proof and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two scenarios of joining the imam in ruku' and apply the condition of actual participation (musharaka) to determine validity.

Core Idea
You must actually bow with the imam to catch the rak'ah; merely joining in ruku' without bowing does not suffice.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah addresses a common situation for latecomers to congregational prayer: what constitutes catching a rak'ah when joining during ruku'? The Hanafi school, based on the principle of actual participation, distinguishes between two cases—one where the follower stands still and one where he bows before the imam. Understanding this ruling ensures proper performance of salah and avoids invalidating a rak'ah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Read the text and list the two distinct cases: (1) the follower joins the imam in ruku' but does not bow; (2) the follower bows before the imam and the imam then catches up.
The second scenario involves preceding the imam, which is makruh tahrimi.
2
Extract the ruling for each scenario
From the text, determine the validity of catching the rak'ah for each case. For scenario 1: does not catch the rak'ah. For scenario 2: catches the rak'ah (but with makruh tahrimi).
The ruling for scenario 2 is valid (sahih) but includes a prohibition.
3
Analyze the condition of participation
The text states the Hanafi condition: actual participation (musharaka) in one of the actions of prayer. Identify why scenario 1 fails (no participation) and scenario 2 succeeds (participation in bowing).
Participation means performing the action together with the imam, not just being present.
4
Compare with Zufar's opinion
Zufar argues that if the follower stands still, he still catches the rak'ah because bowing resembles standing. Identify the Hanafi rebuttal: resemblance is not sufficient; actual participation is required.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; the majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) oppose Zufar.
5
Apply the principle to a new case
Consider a follower who joins the imam in ruku', bows slightly but not fully, and the imam rises. Apply the condition of participation to determine validity.
Partial bowing may or may not count; the text emphasizes 'actual' participation.

Source Text

[٢] قوله : لكن إذا ضاق ؛ أي بقى من الوقت ما لو أدّى فيه السنن فات فرضه. [٣] قوله : من اقتدى بإمام راكع ؛ بأن وصل إليه وهو راكع، فكبر للافتتاح مقتدياً به ووقف ولم يركع، سواء تمكن من الركوع أو لا حتى رفع الإمام رأسه لا يدرك تلك الركعة، خلافاً لزفر، فإنّه يقول : أدرك الإمام فيما له حكم القيام وهو الركوع؛ لمشابهته للقيام من وجه؛ لوجود استواء النصف الأسفل فيه. ولنا : إنَّ الشرط في صحة الاقتداء هو المشاركة في فعل من أفعال الصلاة، ولم توجد لا في القيام ولا في الركوع ومجرّد المشاركة لا يكفي، ويؤيده حديث: «إذا جئتم إلى الصلاة ونحن سجود فاسجدوا ، لا تعدوها شيئاً، ومن أدرك الركعة ـ أي الركوع . فقد أدرك الصلاة ) ، فإن إدراك الركوع إنما يكون إذا ركع مع الإمام، وهو مخرج في «سنن أبي داود» وغيره، تفصيله مع ما له وما عليه في رسالتي : «إمام الكلام فيما يتعلّق بالقراءة خلف الإمام». من ركع فلحقه إمامه فيه صح) ، خلافاً لزفر فإن ما أتى به قبل الإمام غير معتد به، فكذا ما بنى عليه، قلنا : وُجِدَتْ المشاركة في جزء واحد. [١] قوله : من ركع؛ أي ركع المقتدي قبل الإمام، ثم ركع إمامه ووجدت مشاركته به فيه صح إدراكه لتلك الركعة، وإن كان ذلك مكروهاً تحريماً، لحديث: «لا تسبقوني بالركوع ولا بالسجود ولا بالقيام ولا بالانصراف»، أخرجه مسلم وغيره. [٢] قوله : إمامه؛ قيد به لأنه لو ركع قبل الإمام ورفع رأسه قبله لم يجز اتفاقاً. [٣] قوله : غير معتد به؛ أي غير معتبر شرعاً كما يدلّ عليه حديث: «إنما جعل الإمام ليؤتم به، فإذا ركع فاركعوا»، أخرجه أبو داود وغيره. [٤] قوله : قلنا؛ أي في الاستدلال على مذهبنا، وحاصله : أن الشرط هو المشاركة في جزء واحدٍ من أجزاء الصلاة كالركوع والقيام، وقد وجد ولا يلزم من كون جزء غير معتبر بسبب عدم المشاركة عدم كون جزء آخر غير معتبر.
One who follows an imam who is bowing, and then stands still until the imam raises his head, does not catch his bowing (rak'ah), contrary to Zufar. [1] He says: He became diligent upon it, so leaving it without necessity warrants blame due to the saying of Ibn Mas'ud: 'If you abandon the Sunnah of your Prophet, you will go astray' – narrated by Muslim. [2] He says: But if time is tight, meaning there remains of time that if he performs the sunan, his obligatory prayer would be missed. [3] He says: The one who follows an imam who is bowing – meaning he reaches him while he is bowing, says the takbir of iftitah following him, and stands still without bowing, whether or not he is able to bow, until the imam raises his head – does not catch that rak'ah, contrary to Zufar. For he says: He caught the imam in that which has the ruling of standing, namely bowing, because it resembles standing in some respect due to the equalization of the lower half. Our argument: The condition for the validity of following is participation in one of the actions of the prayer. It did not occur in either standing or bowing, and mere participation is insufficient. This is supported by the hadith: 'When you come to the prayer while we are prostrating, prostrate, do not count it as anything; and whoever catches the rak'ah – meaning the bowing – has caught the prayer.' For catching the bowing is only when he bows with the imam, and it is recorded in Sunan Abi Dawud and others. Its detail along with what supports it and what opposes it is in my treatise 'The Imam of Speech Regarding Recitation Behind the Imam'. One who bows, and then his imam catches up to him in it, it is valid – contrary to Zufar, for what he performed before the imam is not considered valid, and likewise what he built upon it. We say: Participation was found in one part. [1] He says: One who bows – meaning the follower bowed before the imam, then the imam bowed and his participation in it was found, so his catching that rak'ah is valid, although it is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi) due to the hadith: 'Do not precede me in bowing, nor in prostration, nor in standing, nor in leaving' – narrated by Muslim and others. [2] He says: 'his imam' – it is specified because if he bowed before the imam and raised his head before him, it is not valid by agreement. [3] He says: 'not considered valid' – meaning not legally valid, as indicated by the hadith: 'The imam is only appointed to be followed; so when he bows, bow' – narrated by Abu Dawud and others. [4] He says: 'We say' – meaning in arguing for our school. The gist of it is that the condition is participation in one part of the prayer, such as bowing and standing. This was found, and the invalidity of one part due to lack of participation does not necessitate the invalidity of another part.
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah, a commentary on Sharh al-Wiqayah, addresses the Hanafi ruling on catching a rak'ah when joining the congregation during the imam's ruku'. The author presents two main scenarios. The first: A person joins the imam while he is in ruku' but does not bow and instead stands still until the imam raises his head. According to the Hanafi school, this person does not catch that rak'ah. This is contrary to Zufar, a Hanafi jurist, who argued that because standing and bowing share a similarity (both involve straightening the lower back?), the follower has effectively caught the imam in a standing-like position. The Hanafi response, given as 'Our argument', is that the condition for valid following is actual participation in an action of the prayer. The follower participated in neither standing (since he was not in qiyam with the imam from the start) nor bowing (since he did not bow). The hadith about catching the rak'ah is cited: catching the bowing (ruk') means bowing with the imam. The second scenario: A follower bows before the imam, but then the imam bows and catches up to him. In this case, the follower's rak'ah is considered valid because there was participation in one part of the prayer (the bowing itself). However, this act of preceding the imam in bowing is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi) because of the hadith forbidding preceding the imam. The passage also clarifies that if the follower bowed and raised his head before the imam bowed, then he has not caught it by agreement. The key principle is that participation in even one part of the prayer is sufficient for catching the rak'ah, and the invalidity of one part does not affect the validity of another part.

Key Terms
اقتداء (iqtida'): Following the imam in prayer; the act of a ma'mum performing the prayer behind an imam.
ركعة (rak'ah): A unit of prayer consisting of standing, bowing, and two prostrations; catching a rak'ah means joining the imam before he raises from ruku'.
مشاركة (musharaka): Participation in a common action; in this context, the follower must actually perform a prayer action alongside the imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person joins the congregation while the imam is in ruku'. He says takbir and stands still without bowing until the imam raises his head. According to the Hanafi school, has he caught that rak'ah?
A) Yes, because he was present during the ruku'.
B) No, because he did not actually bow with the imam.
C) Yes, according to Zufar, but the majority say no.
D) No, unless he recites at least one tasbih in ruku'.

Key Takeaway
Actual participation in bowing with the imam is essential to catch a rak'ah; mere presence or resemblance does not suffice.

Ruling on Bowing Before the Imam
Ruling on a latecomer who bows before the imam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a follower who bows before the imam and is then joined by the imam, and explain why the rak'ah is valid despite the prohibition.

Core Idea
Bowing before the imam is sinful but does not ruin the rak'ah — participation in one part suffices.

This lesson examines a common scenario in congregational prayer: a follower accidentally bows slightly before the imam. Many assume the rak'ah is invalid, but the Hanafi school rules it valid. We will explore the proof from hadith, the reasoning of Imam Zufar's objection, and the Hanafi response.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act: a follower bows before the imam, then the imam bows while the follower is still in ruku'. The ruling: the rak'ah is validly caught, though the early bowing is sinful.
Focus on the validity of the rak'ah, not just the sin.
2
Understand the prohibition and its effect
The hadith 'Do not precede me...' prohibits preceding the imam. This makes the early bowing makruh tahrimi, but it does not automatically invalidate the rak'ah.
The prohibition addresses the sin, not the validity.
3
Compare Zufar's argument
Zufar argues that since the early part is invalid, the entire rak'ah built on it is invalid. This reflects a different view on the condition for catching a rak'ah.
Zufar requires the whole rak'ah to be validly performed from the start.
4
Apply the principle of participation (mushāraka)
The Hanafi response: the condition is participation in any one part of the rak'ah. Here, the follower and imam bow together, achieving participation. Invalidity of the early part does not negate this separate participation.
Participation is key; the part done with the imam is distinct.
5
Determine the practical consequence
According to Abu Hanifa (mufta bihi), the follower catches the rak'ah and does not repeat it. According to Zufar, the follower misses it and must make it up.
The difference affects whether the follower needs an extra rak'ah after salam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من ركع فلحقهُ إمامُهُ فيه صح ) ، خلافاً لزُفَرَ فَإِن مَا أَتَى بِهِ قَبْلَ الإِمَامِ غَيْرُ معتد به ، فكذا ما بنى عليه ، قلنا : وُجِدَتْ المشاركة في جزء واحد.
[١] قوله : من ركع ؛ أي ركع المقتدي قبل الإمام ، ثم ركع إمامه ووجدت مشاركته به فيه صح إدراكه لتلك الركعة، وإن كان ذلك مكروهاً تحريماً، لحديث: «لا تسبقوني بالركوع ولا بالسجود ولا بالقيام ولا بالانصراف»، أخرجه مسلم وغيره.
[٢] قوله : إمامه ؛ قيد به لأنه لو ركع قبل الإمام ورفع رأسه قبله لم يجز اتفاقاً.
[٣] قوله : غير معتد به ؛ أي غير معتبر شرعاً كما يدلّ عليه حديث : «إنما جعل الإمام ليؤتم به ، فإذا ركع فاركعوا»، أخرجه أبو داود وغيره.
[٤]قوله : قلنا ؛ أي في الاستدلال على مذهبنا ، وحاصله : أن الشرط هو المشاركة في جزء واحدٍ من أجزاء الصلاة كالركوع والقيام ، وقد وجد ولا يلزم من كون جزء غير معتبر بسبب عدم المشاركة عدم كون جزء آخر غير معتبر.
Whoever bows and his imam joins him in it, it is valid, contrary to Zufar, for what he did before the imam is not considered valid, so likewise what he built upon it. We said: Participation in one part is found. [1] His saying: 'Whoever bows' means the follower bowed before the imam, then his imam bowed and his participation with him in it is found, so his catching of that rak'ah is valid, even if that is makruh tahrimi, due to the hadith: 'Do not precede me in bowing, nor in prostration, nor in standing, nor in leaving.' Reported by Muslim and others. [2] His saying: 'his imam' is a restriction because if he bowed before the imam and raised his head before him, it is not valid by agreement. [3] His saying: 'not considered valid' means not valid according to sharia, as indicated by the hadith: 'The imam is appointed to be followed; so when he bows, bow.' Reported by Abu Dawud and others. [4] His saying: 'We said' refers to the argument for our madhhab, and its summary is that the condition is participation in one part of the parts of prayer such as bowing and standing, and it has been found, and it does not follow that because one part is not considered valid due to lack of participation, another part is also not considered valid.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hidayah sharh. It addresses the case of a follower who bows in prayer before the imam, and then the imam bows while the follower is still in ruku'. The ruling is that the follower validly catches that rak'ah, contrary to Zufar (a Hanafi scholar). The text first states the ruling: if someone bows (before the imam) and then his imam joins him in that bowing, the rak'ah is valid. Then it gives Zufar's objection: what was done before the imam is not valid, so what is built on it (i.e., the remaining parts) is also invalid. The Hanafi response is that participation in a single part (here, the bowing together) is sufficient to catch the rak'ah. The commentary elaborates: the follower's bowing before the imam is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked) due to the hadith 'Do not precede me...' but it does not invalidate the rak'ah. The hadith 'The imam is appointed to be followed' emphasizes that the follower's earlier bowing is not valid on its own, but when the imam bows, there is participation. The key point is that the condition for catching a rak'ah is participation in any one part, not that all parts must be validly performed from the start.

Key Terms
المشاركة (al-mushāraka): Participation in a part of the prayer; the condition for catching a rak'ah according to Hanafis.
معتد به (mu'tad bihī): Considered valid or recognized by sharia; opposite of invalid.
مكروهاً تحريماً (makrūhan taḥrīman): Prohibitively disliked; an act that is sinful but not invalidating.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a follower bows before the imam and then the imam bows while the follower is still in ruku', what is the ruling on the rak'ah?
A) The rak'ah is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The rak'ah is valid because participation in one part is found.
C) The rak'ah is valid only if the follower intended to follow the imam.
D) The rak'ah is invalid because the follower sinned.

Key Takeaway
Bowing before the imam is prohibited but does not invalidate the rak'ah if the imam joins the follower in that bowing, because participation in one part suffices to catch the rak'ah.
