Obligation of Sequence in Missed Prayers (Qada' al-Fawa'it)
Establishing the obligation of sequence between missed prayers and timely prayers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sequence between missed prayers and between missed and current prayers, identify the evidence from the hadith of Ibn Umar and the practice of the Prophet (ﷺ), and distinguish it from the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Sequence between missed prayers and timely prayers is fard (obligatory) in the Hanafi school.

This lesson addresses a fundamental question: when you have missed prayers, must you make them up in a specific order? The Hanafi school answers with a firm 'yes', extending the obligation even when mixing missed prayers with current timely ones. The source passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah explains both the ruling and the evidence, including a hadith from Ibn Umar and the incident of the Prophet at the Battle of the Trench.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling from the matn
Identify the core fiqh ruling: sequence (tartib) is obligatory (fard) between the five daily prayers and witr, whether all or some are missed, and also when some are missed and some are current.
The matn explicitly says 'فُرِضَ الترتيب' - sequence is made obligatory.
2
Identify the scope of the ruling
Confirm that the obligation applies to all five obligatory prayers (fard) and also witr. It applies whether all prayers are missed or only some, and when mixing with current timely prayers.
The commentary emphasizes: 'either when all are missed or some are missed and some are timely'.
3
Examine the evidence (dalil)
Two proofs are cited: the hadith of Ibn Umar (mawquf but supported by a marfu' weak chain) commanding the missed prayer before the timely one, and the Prophet's (ﷺ) action at Khandaq where he made up Zuhr, Asr, and Maghrib in sequence before praying Isha.
The hadith is considered sufficient for obligation despite being weak in transmission.
4
Appreciate the Hanafi tarjih (preference)
Recognize that while the hadith chain is weak and other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) do not require sequence when many prayers are missed, the Hanafi school holds it as fard due to the cumulative evidence and the prophetic practice.
The Hanafi position is zahir al-riwayah and the mufta bihi (operative for fatwa).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب قضاء الفوائت
[1] فُرِضَ الترتيب بين الفروض الخمسة والوتر فائناً كلها ، أو بعضها) : أي إن كان الكل فائتاً لا بدَّ من رعايةِ التّرتيب بين الفروض الخمسة، وكذا بينها وبين الوتر، وكذا إن كان البعض فائتاً، والبعض وقتياً لا بُدَّ من رعايةِ التَّرتيب، فيَقْضي الفائتة قبل أداء الوقتية
[١] قوله : باب قضاء الفوائت ؛ أي هذا باب في بيان الأحكام المتعلقة بقضاء الصلوات الفائتة، وفي هذا التعبير دون التعبير بالمتروكات رعاية للأدب، وحسن ظن بالمسلم، بأنه لا يترك الصلاة.
[٢] قوله : بين الفروض الخمسة...الخ ؛ الأصل فيه قول ابن عمر : «من نسي صلاة من صلاته فلم يذكرها إلا وهو مع الإمام ، فإذا سلم الإمام فليصل صلاته التي نسي ثم ليصل بعدها الصلاة الأخرى ) ، أخرجه مالك في «الموطأ»، وروى الدارقطني والبيهقي هذا الحديث مرفوعاً، وسنده ضعيف كما بسطناه في «التعليق الممجّد على موطأ محمد.
وبهذا احتج أصحابنا في فرضيّة الترتيب بين الوقتيّات والفوائت، وبين الفوائت بعضها ببعض، وقد روي أنّ رسول الله فاتته صلاة الظهر والعصر والمغرب باشتغاله بالغزو يوم الخندق ، فقضاها في وقت العشاء مرتباً ، ثم صلى العشاء، أخرجه الترمذي.
Chapter of making up missed prayers. [1] Sequence is made obligatory between the five obligatory prayers and witr when all or some of them are missed: i.e., if all are missed, observance of sequence between the five obligatory prayers is necessary, and likewise between them and witr, and likewise if some are missed and some are within their time, observance of sequence is necessary, so he prays the missed prayer before performing the timely prayer. [1] His saying: 'Chapter of making up missed prayers' means this chapter is for explaining the rulings pertaining to making up missed prayers, and this expression rather than 'the abandoned' is out of politeness and good opinion of the Muslim in that he does not abandon prayer. [2] His saying: 'between the five obligatory prayers...' the basis for it is the saying of Ibn Umar: 'Whoever forgets a prayer from his prayers and does not remember it except when he is with the imam, then when the imam says salam, let him pray the prayer he forgot, then let him pray the other prayer after it.' Reported by Malik in al-Muwatta, and al-Daraqutni and al-Bayhaqi reported this hadith as marfu', but its chain is weak as we explained in al-Ta'liq al-Mumajjad 'ala Muwatta' Muhammad. With this our companions argued for the obligation of sequence between timely prayers and missed prayers, and between missed prayers with one another, and it has been narrated that the Messenger of Allah missed the prayers of zuhr, asr, and maghrib due to his engagement in the battle of Khandaq, so he made them up in the time of isha in sequence, then prayed isha. Reported by al-Tirmidhi.
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage introduces a new chapter on making up missed prayers (qada' al-fawa'it). The matn states that sequence (tartib) between the five obligatory prayers and witr is compulsory when all or some are missed. The commentary clarifies: if all prayers are missed, they must be made up in order (zuhr, asr, maghrib, isha, fajr, witr). If some are missed and some are still within their time, the missed prayer must be made up before the current timely prayer. The expression 'fawa'it' (missed) is used instead of 'matruk' (abandoned) out of politeness. The proof comes from the report of Ibn Umar and the practice of the Prophet at the Battle of the Trench. Although the hadith is weak, the Hanafi school considers it sufficient for obligation, especially supported by the Prophet's action. Thus, sequence is fard (obligatory) in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
قضاء الفوائت (qaḍā' al-fawā'it): Making up missed prayers after their time has passed.
الترتيب (al-tartīb): The obligation to perform missed prayers in their original chronological order.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on sequence (tartib) when a person has a missed prayer and a current timely prayer?
A) Sequence is not required; either can be prayed first.
B) The timely prayer must be prayed first, then the missed one.
C) The missed prayer must be made up before the timely prayer.
D) Sequence is only required if both are missed prayers.

Key Takeaway
Sequence between missed prayers and between missed and current prayers is fard in the Hanafi school, based on the hadith of Ibn Umar and the Prophet's practice at Khandaq.

Order of Making Up Missed Prayers (Tartib) and the Status of Witr
Expanding the ruling of order between missed and current prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tartib between missed and current prayers, identify the proof from hadith, and apply the ruling to the case of witr including the intra-Hanafi difference.

Core Idea
Order between missed prayers is wajib; witr is wajib so it must be made up before Fajr if remembered.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya establishes a fundamental ruling in the Hanafi school: when you remember a missed prayer, you must pray it before the current one. The proof comes from the hadith of Ibn Umar and the action of the Prophet ﷺ at the Battle of the Trench. The passage also addresses a specific application: what if someone remembers that they missed witr before praying Fajr? Here, an intra-Hanafi difference emerges between Abu Hanifa and his two students, the Sahibayn, based on the status of witr — is it wajib or sunnah? This lesson will guide you through the ruling, its evidence, and the practical consequences of the ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling on tartib
Read the opening sentence: 'furiḍa al-tartīb bayna al-furūḍ al-khamsah wa al-witr'. Determine what exactly is prescribed (furiḍa) and the scope: between the five obligatory prayers and witr, whether all or some are missed, and between missed and current prayers.
The term 'furiḍa' is used but in Hanafi usul, since the proof is a hadith ahad, it is considered wajib, not fard. This is an important epistemological nuance.
2
Locate and analyze the proof (dalil)
The author cites two hadith: (1) The hadith of Ibn Umar about forgetting a prayer while with the imam, and (2) the hadith of the Battle of the Trench where the Prophet ﷺ made up missed prayers in order. Identify the specific wording that indicates order and explain how Hanafi usul derives wujub from the imperative (amr).
The hadith of Ibn Umar is narrated as mawquf (stopped at the Companion), but it is considered marfu' by some. Its chain is weak, but it is supported by the Khandaq hadith and general practice.
3
Apply the ruling to the witr case
The passage states: 'فلم يجز فجر مَن ذَكَرَ أَنَّه لم يوتر' (it is not valid that Fajr of one who remembers he has not performed witr). Understand why: because witr is wajib according to Abu Hanifa, so tartib applies between it and Fajr. If Fajr is prayed while remembering the missed witr, the Fajr is invalid and must be repeated after making up witr.
This is the position of Abu Hanifa. The Sahibayn disagree because they consider witr to be sunnah, not wajib, so tartib would not be required.
4
Distinguish the Sahibayn's view and identify the thamarah al-khilaf
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that witr is sunnah, so if someone prays Fajr while remembering they missed witr, Fajr is still valid. The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is that according to Abu Hanifa, Fajr must be repeated; according to the Sahibayn, it is valid and only the witr needs to be made up later.
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is the position of Abu Hanifa: witr is wajib and tartib applies. However, in cases of necessity (like fear of missing the current prayer time), exceptions may be made.

Source Text

باب قضاء الفوائت

[١] قوله : باب قضاء الفوائت ؛ أي هذا باب في بيان الأحكام المتعلقة بقضاء الصلوات الفائتة، وفي هذا التعبير دون التعبير بالمتروكات رعاية للأدب، وحسن ظن بالمسلم، بأنه لا يترك الصلاة.
[٢] قوله : بين الفروض الخمسة...الخ ؛ الأصل فيه قول ابن عمر : «من نسي صلاة من صلاته فلم يذكرها إلا وهو مع الإمام ، فإذا سلم الإمام فليصل صلاته التي نسي ثم ليصل بعدها الصلاة الأخرى ) ، أخرجه مالك في «الموطأ»، وروى الدارقطني والبيهقي هذا الحديث مرفوعاً، ا، وسنده ضعيف كما بسطناه في «التعليق الممجّد على موطأ محمد.
وبهذا احتج أصحابنا في فرضيّة الترتيب بين الوقتيّات والفوائت، وبين الفوائت بعضها ببعض، وقد روي أنّ رسول الله اللي فاتته صلاة الظهر والعصر والمغرب باشتغاله بالغزو يوم الخندق ، فقضاها في وقت العشاء مرتباً ، ثم صلى العشاء)، أخرجه الترمذي.

فلم يجز فجر مَن ذَكَرَ أنَّه لم يوتر ، ويُعيدُ العشاء والسُّنَّةَ لا الوترَ مَن عَلِمَ أَنَّه صَلَّى العشاء بلا وضوء والأخريين به
(فلم يجز" فجر مَن ذَكَرَ أنه لم يوتر) ، هذا تفريع لقوله : والوتر، وهذا عند أبي حنيفة له خلافاً لهما" بناء" على وجوب الوتر عنده.
( ويُعيدُ العشاء والسُنة) لا الوترَ مَن عَلِمَ أنه صلى العشاء بلا وضوء والأخريين به
Chapter of Making Up Missed Prayers: Order between the five obligatory prayers and witr is prescribed, whether all or some are missed. Meaning: if all are missed, order must be observed between the five obligatory prayers, and similarly between them and witr; and likewise if some are missed and some are timely, order must be observed, so one makes up the missed prayer before performing the timely one. [1] His saying: Chapter of Making Up Missed Prayers; i.e., this is a chapter explaining the rulings related to making up missed prayers, and in this expression rather than the expression 'the abandoned' is out of politeness and good opinion of the Muslim, that he does not abandon prayer. [2] His saying: between the five obligatory prayers...etc.; the basis for this is the saying of Ibn Umar: 'Whoever forgets a prayer of his and does not remember it except while with the imam, then when the imam says the salam, let him pray the prayer he forgot, then pray the other prayer after it.' Narrated by Malik in al-Muwatta, and al-Daraqutni and al-Bayhaqi narrated it as marfu', and its chain is weak as we detailed in al-Ta'liq al-Mumajjad on Muwatta Muhammad. And with this our companions argued for the obligatoriness of order between timely prayers and missed ones, and between missed prayers among themselves. And it has been narrated that the Messenger of Allah missed Zuhr, Asr, and Maghrib due to his engagement in the battle of the Trench, then he made them up in order in the time of Isha, then prayed Isha. Narrated by al-Tirmidhi. Then it is not valid that Fajr of one who remembers that he has not performed witr, and one who knows that he prayed Isha without wudu and the other two with it should repeat Isha and the sunnah, not witr. (It is not valid that Fajr of one who remembers that he has not performed witr) this is a branching from his saying: and witr, and this is according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to the two, based on the obligatoriness of witr in his view. (And he repeats Isha and the sunnah) not witr, for one who knows that he prayed Isha without wudu and the other two with it.
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the chapter of making up missed prayers. The author begins by stating the ruling: order (tartib) is prescribed (furida) between the five daily prayers and witr when they are all missed, or when some are missed and others are timely. This means that if one has missed multiple prayers, they must be made up in their proper sequence. If some are missed and the current prayer time has entered, the missed prayer must be made up first before the current one. The author explains the basis for this ruling: a hadith from Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) reported in al-Muwatta, and the well-known incident of the Prophet (peace be upon him) on the day of the Trench when he made up missed prayers in order. These serve as proofs for the Hanafi position. The passage then turns to two specific cases. First, if someone remembers that they have not performed witr (the odd-numbered prayer), and then prays Fajr, their Fajr is not valid according to Abu Hanifa. This is because witr is obligatory (wajib) in his view, and order is required between it and other prayers. However, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) consider witr as sunnah, so order would not be required. Second, if someone prays Isha without wudu (invalid), but then prays the sunnah of Isha and witr with wudu (valid), they must repeat the Isha prayer and its sunnah, but not the witr. The reasoning: the Isha prayer was invalid, so the subsequent sunnah (which is connected to it) is also invalid and must be repeated; witr is not connected to Isha in the same way, so it remains valid.

Key Terms
الترتيب (al-tartib): Order between prayers: that missed prayers must be made up in the sequence they were missed, and before current time prayers if remembered.
الوتر (al-witr): The odd-numbered prayer performed after Isha, considered by Abu Hanifa as wajib, by the Sahibayn as sunnah.
الفائتة (al-fa'itah): A prayer that was missed due to sleep, forgetfulness, or some excuse, and must be made up.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school (based on this passage), if a person remembers that they have not prayed witr and then prays Fajr, what is the ruling according to Abu Hanifa?
A) The Fajr prayer is valid because witr is sunnah.
B) The Fajr prayer is invalid and must be repeated after making up witr.
C) The Fajr prayer is invalid but the witr is not required to be made up.
D) The Fajr prayer is valid but the witr must be made up later.

Key Takeaway
Order between missed prayers is wajib in the Hanafi school, and witr is treated as wajib, so it must be made up before Fajr if remembered.
